---

## 17. 驕傲是最昂貴的特質：學習的敵人

### 逐句對照

**主持人:** The most expensive trait is pride. How come?
最昂貴的特質是驕傲。為什麼這麼說？

**Naval:** Oh, that was a recent one. I tweeted that just because I think that pride is the enemy of learning.
喔，那是我最近才發的。我會發那則推文，是因為我覺得驕傲是學習的敵人。

**Naval:** So when I look at my friends and colleagues, the ones who are still stuck in the past and have grown the least are the ones who were the proudest, because they sort of feel like they already had the answers.
所以當我看看我的朋友和同事，那些還困在過去、成長最少的人，往往是最驕傲的那群，因為他們覺得自己早就握有答案了。

**Naval:** And so they don't want to correct themselves publicly. And this goes back to the fame conversation. You get locked into something you said. It made you famous. You're known for that. And now you want to pivot or change.
所以他們不願意公開修正自己。這又回到剛才談名聲的話題。你被自己說過的話綁住了，那句話讓你出名，你因此被認識，而現在你想轉向或改變。

**Naval:** So pride prevents you from saying I'm wrong.
所以驕傲讓你說不出「我錯了」。

**主持人:** What's pride in this context here?
在這個脈絡下，驕傲指的是什麼？

**Naval:** It could be as simple as you're trading stocks and then you don't admit you were wrong, so you hang on to a lousy trade.
它可以單純到像是你在做股票交易，卻不肯承認自己看錯了，於是死抱著一筆爛部位不放。

**Naval:** It could be that you made a decision to marry someone or move somewhere or enter a profession, it doesn't work out, and then you don't want to admit that you were wrong, so you get stuck in it.
也可能是你決定跟某人結婚、搬到某個地方，或投入某個職業，結果行不通，你卻不願承認自己錯了，於是被困在裡面。

**Naval:** It's mostly about getting trapped in local maxima, as opposed to going back down and climbing up the mountain again.
它多半是關於被困在「局部最高點」，而不願意走下山、重新爬另一座更高的山。

**主持人:** And that's why it's an expensive trait, because you continue to need to repay it in one form or another.
這就是為什麼它是昂貴的特質，因為你得用這樣或那樣的形式不斷地為它付出代價。

**Naval:** Yeah. You're just stuck at a suboptimal point. It's going to cost you money, it's going to cost you success
對，你就卡在一個次佳的位置。它會讓你損失金錢、損失成功，

**主持人:** and time.
還有時間。

**Naval:** and time. The great artists always have this ability to start over, whether it's Paul Simon or Madonna or U2, and I'm dating myself a little bit.
還有時間。偉大的藝術家總是有從頭來過的能力，不管是 Paul Simon、瑪丹娜還是 U2，這樣講有點暴露我的年紀了。

**Naval:** But even the great entrepreneurs, they're just always willing to start over. I'm always struck by the Elon Musk story, where he did PayPal as X.com originally. Actually, it was his financial institution that got merged into PayPal.
但就連偉大的創業家也一樣，他們永遠願意重新來過。馬斯克的故事總讓我印象深刻，他一開始是以 X.com 的形式做 PayPal 的。其實是他的金融機構後來併進了 PayPal。

**主持人:** It's good that you've got the domain. You know what I mean?
還好你當初留著那個網域。你懂我意思吧？

**Naval:** Yeah, exactly. I'll park that. I'll hold on.
對，沒錯。「我先把它擺著，留在手上。」

**主持人:** He's consistent. He's been using it for quite a while.
他很一致，這個網域他已經用了好一陣子。

**Naval:** And he said something along the lines of, I made $200 million from the sale of PayPal. I put $100 million into SpaceX, 80 million Tesla, 20 into Solar City, and I had to borrow money for rent, right?
他說過類似這樣的話：我賣掉 PayPal 賺了兩億美元，我把一億投進 SpaceX、八千萬進特斯拉、兩千萬進 Solar City，然後我還得借錢來付房租，對吧？

**Naval:** This guy is a perennial risk taker. He's always willing to start over. He doesn't have any pride about being seen as successful or being seen as a failure. He's willing to put it all in.
這傢伙是個永遠的冒險者。他隨時願意重新開始。他對於別人怎麼看他——成功也好、失敗也罷——完全沒有那種驕傲的包袱。他願意把全部押上去。

**主持人:** Back himself again each time.
每一次都重新押注自己。

**Naval:** Back himself again each time. But the key thing is he's always willing to start over, right? Even now, his new startup is the USA, right? He's basically trying to fix it like he would fix one of his startups.
每一次都重新押注自己。但關鍵是他永遠願意從頭來過，對吧？就連現在，他的新創業就是整個美國，對吧？他基本上是在用修理自家新創公司的方式，試圖去修好它。

**Naval:** And I think that is a willingness to look like a fool, and that is a willingness to start over. And a lot of people just don't have that. They become successful or they become rich or they become famous and that's it. They're stuck. They don't want to go back to zero.
我覺得那是一種甘願讓自己看起來像個傻瓜的意願，也是一種願意重新開始的意願。很多人就是沒有這個。他們變得成功、變得有錢、變得有名，然後就這樣了。他們卡住了。他們不想再回到零。

**Naval:** And creating anything great requires zero to one. And that means you go back to zero, and that's really painful and hard to do.
而創造任何偉大的事物都需要「從零到一」。這意味著你得先回到零，而那真的很痛苦、很難做到。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| pride | /praɪd/ | n. | 驕傲、自尊 |
| trait | /tret/ | n. | 特質、特性 |
| pivot | /ˋpɪvət/ | v. | 轉向、轉型 |
| suboptimal | /sʌbˋɑptəml/ | adj. | 次佳的、不夠理想的 |
| perennial | /pəˋrɛnɪəl/ | adj. | 長年的、始終如一的 |
| local maxima | /ˋlokl ˋmæksəmə/ | n. | 局部極大值（比喻卡在小高點） |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`How come?`**：口語版的「為什麼？」，語氣比 `Why?` 更輕鬆、帶好奇。
- **`hang on to a lousy trade`**：死抱著一筆爛部位不放；`hang on to` 意為「緊抓不放」。
- **`I'm dating myself`**：直譯是「我在洩漏自己的年紀」，意指提到的東西暴露了說話者的年代。
- **`back himself`**：相信、支持自己（源自賭博下注 `back` 某人）。
- **`go back to zero` / `zero to one`**：回到原點／從零到一；後者出自 Peter Thiel 的創業概念，指「無中生有」。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`the ones who ... are the ones who were the proudest`** — `the ones who...` 是關係子句作主詞與補語，用來替代 `the people who...`，口語中常見。
- **`It could be as simple as you're trading stocks and then you don't admit...`** — `as simple as + 子句`表「單純到就像⋯⋯」；後面接一整句說明情境。
- **`creating anything great requires zero to one`** — 動名詞片語 `creating anything great` 當主詞；注意 `anything` 後置形容詞 `great`（不定代名詞的形容詞後置）。

---

## 18. 不必默默受苦：選擇當快樂的人

### 逐句對照

**主持人:** Talking about risk, something I've been thinking about a lot to do with you. Any moment when you're not having a good time, when you're not really happy, you're not doing anyone any favors.
說到風險，有件跟你有關的事我最近想了很多。任何一個你過得不開心、不是真的快樂的時刻，其實你並沒有在幫任何人的忙。

**主持人:** I think lots of people have become unusually familiar with suffering silently, in that sort of way of not having a high bar for your expectation for quality of life.
我覺得很多人已經異常習慣默默受苦，習慣到對自己生活品質的期待標準訂得很低。

**Naval:** Yeah, a lot of it is just you're memeing yourself into a bad outcome, because you think that somehow suffering is glorious or that it makes you a better person.
對，這裡面很大一部分是你把自己「洗腦」進了一個壞結果，因為你以為受苦莫名地很崇高，或者以為它讓你變成更好的人。

**Naval:** You know, my old quip was: if you're so smart, why aren't you happy? Why can't you figure that one out? The reality is you can be smart and happy. There are plenty of people in human history who are smart and happy.
我以前有句俏皮話是：你既然這麼聰明，為什麼不快樂？這個你怎麼想不通呢？事實是，你可以既聰明又快樂。人類歷史上有一大堆人既聰明又快樂。

**Naval:** And I think it just starts with saying, yeah, you know what, I'm going to be happy. There was a guy that I met in Thailand a long time ago, and he used to work for Tony Robbins. He had a great attitude.
我覺得它就從一句話開始：對，你知道嗎，我就是要快樂。很久以前我在泰國認識一個人，他以前替 Tony Robbins 工作，他的態度超棒。

**Naval:** We were sitting around and he said, I realized one day that someone out there had to be the happiest person in the world. That person just has to exist. He said, why not me? I'll take on that burden. I'll be that guy.
我們坐在一起聊，他說，有一天我意識到，這世界上總得有一個「最快樂的人」。那個人一定存在。他說，那為什麼不是我？我來扛下這個重擔。我來當那個人。

**Naval:** And I heard that and I was like, wow, that's pretty good. That's a good frame, right? He knew how to reframe things.
我聽到就想，哇，這觀點真不錯。這是個很好的框架，對吧？他很懂得怎麼重新框定事情。

**Naval:** And so I think a lot of happiness is just a choice, in the sense that first you just identify yourself as, actually, I'm going to be a person that's going to be happy. I'm going to figure it out. And you just figure it out along the way.
所以我覺得快樂很大一部分只是一種選擇，意思是你首先把自己定位成：其實，我要當一個會快樂的人。我會把它想通。然後你就在過程中一路把它摸索出來。

**Naval:** You're not going to lose your other predilections. You're not going to lose your ambition or your desire for success. I think a lot of people have this fear that, oh, if I'm happy, then I won't want to be successful.
你不會因此失去其他的偏好。你不會失去你的企圖心，或你對成功的渴望。我覺得很多人有這種恐懼：喔，如果我快樂了，那我就不會想要成功了。

**Naval:** No, you'll just want to do things that are more aligned with the happy version of you, and you'll be successful at those things.
不會，你只是會想去做那些更貼合「快樂版本的你」的事情，而你會在那些事情上獲得成功。

**Naval:** And believe me, the happy version of you is not going to look back at the unhappy version and say, oh man, that guy was going to be more successful. I wish I was him.
而且相信我，快樂版本的你不會回頭看著不快樂的那個版本說，唉，那傢伙本來會更成功，真希望我是他。

**主持人:** You're actually trying to be successful so you'll be happy. That's the whole point. You've gotten it backwards.
你其實是為了快樂才去追求成功的。這才是重點。你把順序搞反了。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| glorious | /ˋglorɪəs/ | adj. | 光榮的、崇高的 |
| quip | /kwɪp/ | n. | 妙語、俏皮話 |
| frame / reframe | /frem/ /riˋfrem/ | n. / v. | 框架／重新框定 |
| predilection | /ˏpridḷˋɛkʃən/ | n. | 偏好、偏愛 |
| ambition | /æmˋbɪʃən/ | n. | 企圖心、抱負 |
| aligned with | /əˋlaɪnd/ | phr. | 與⋯⋯一致、契合 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`you're not doing anyone any favors`**：你並沒有在幫任何人的忙（雙重否定加強語氣）。
- **`meme yourself into ...`**：把自己「洗腦／催眠」進某種狀態，源自網路迷因用語，指用重複的想法說服自己。
- **`figure that one out`**：把那件事想通、搞懂；`that one` 口語指前面提到的難題。
- **`why not me?`**：那為什麼不是我？——一種反問式的自我賦權。
- **`you've gotten it backwards`**：你把它搞反了、順序弄顛倒了。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`if you're so smart, why aren't you happy?`** — 「if + 現在事實 + 反問句」的挑釁句型，帶質疑語氣，並非真正的條件句。
- **`things that are more aligned with the happy version of you`** — 關係子句 `that are aligned with...` 修飾 `things`；`the happy version of you` 是把抽象狀態「人格化」的口語表達。
- **`the happy version of you is not going to look back ... and say ...`** — `be going to` 表推測/預測未來；`look back and say` 兩個動作並列共用一個主詞。

---

## 19. 為成功犧牲快樂是本末倒置

### 逐句對照

**主持人:** You unlocked one of my trap cards. One of my favorite insights is that we sacrifice the thing we want for the thing that's supposed to get it.
你打開了我的一張陷阱卡。我最喜歡的體悟之一是：我們為了那個「本該幫我們得到目標」的東西，反而犧牲了我們真正想要的東西。

**主持人:** So we sacrifice happiness in order to be successful, so that when we're finally sufficiently successful, we can actually be happy.
所以我們為了成功而犧牲快樂，好讓自己終於足夠成功的時候，才能真正快樂。

**主持人:** And if you have some sort of simultaneous equation and you just stripped success off from both sides, at least in my own life, I have not found there to be a trade-off.
如果你把它想成某種聯立方程式，然後把「成功」從等式兩邊同時消去，至少在我自己的人生裡，我並沒有發現這中間存在什麼取捨。

**主持人:** If anything, I have found that the happier I get, the more I am going to do the things that I'm good at and aligned with, and that will make me even happier. And so I actually end up more successful, not less.
如果真要說，我反而發現：我越快樂，就越會去做那些我擅長、又契合我的事，而那又會讓我更快樂。於是我最後變得更成功，而不是更不成功。

**主持人:** The "aligned with" thing is interesting. I'm going to try and put this across as delicately as I can. I would say, from the bit of time that we've spent together, you have a really interesting trait of holistic selfishness.
「契合」這件事很有意思。我盡量委婉地表達。我會說，從我們相處的這段時間看來，你有一個很有意思的特質，一種「全方位的自私」。

**主持人:** You're sort of prepared to put yourself first. You seem largely unfazed by saying or doing things that might result in other people feeling a little bit awkward, if it's truthful for you.
你算是準備好把自己擺在第一位。只要那對你來說是真實的，你似乎大致上不太在意去說或做一些可能讓別人有點尷尬的事。

**主持人:** It's like unapologetically self-prioritizing, I guess.
大概就像是，毫不愧疚地把自己擺第一。

**Naval:** Yeah, I think everybody is. Maybe unapologetic is the part that's relatively rare. But I think everybody puts themselves first. That's just human nature. You're here because you survive. You're a separate organism.
對，我覺得每個人都是這樣。也許「毫不愧疚」才是相對稀有的部分。但我覺得每個人都把自己擺第一。那就是人性。你存在，是因為你活了下來。你是一個獨立的生物個體。

**主持人:** That's interesting. Maybe. But I know we like to virtue signal and pretend we're doing it for each other.
這很有意思。也許吧。但我知道我們喜歡「道德作秀」，假裝我們是在為彼此付出。

**主持人:** How many times does somebody say, yeah, of course, I'd love to come to the wedding? They're like, I don't want to be at the wedding. How many times does someone say, how are you doing today, and they don't tell you?
有多少次，有人嘴上說：好啊當然，我很樂意去參加婚禮？心裡其實是：我根本不想去那場婚禮。又有多少次，有人問你「你今天過得怎樣」，卻根本不想聽你回答？

**Naval:** I don't go to weddings.
我不去婚禮的。

**主持人:** But this is my point. So I don't think you're necessarily right with that. I think people don't put themselves first. I sometimes think they compromise what it is that they want in order to appease socially what's in front of them.
但這正是我要說的。所以我不覺得你那個說法一定對。我認為人們並沒有把自己擺第一。我有時候覺得，他們會為了在社交上安撫眼前的人，而犧牲掉自己真正想要的東西。

**Naval:** Yeah. I just view it as everyone's wasting their time on it. Don't do something you don't want to do. Why are you wasting your time? There's so little time on this earth.
對。我只是把它看成大家都在浪費時間在這種事上。不要去做你不想做的事。你幹嘛浪費自己的時間？我們在這世上的時間這麼少。

**Naval:** Life goes fast. What is it, 4,000 weeks? That's your lifespan. And yes, we hear that, but we don't remember it. But I guess I'm keenly aware of how little time I have, so I'm just not going to waste it.
人生過得很快。是多少來著，四千個禮拜？那就是你一輩子的長度。是啦，我們都聽過這句話，但我們記不住。而我想我非常清楚地意識到自己剩下的時間有多少，所以我就是不打算浪費它。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| sacrifice | /ˋsækrəˏfaɪs/ | v. | 犧牲 |
| trade-off | /ˋtredˏɔf/ | n. | 取捨、權衡 |
| holistic | /hoˋlɪstɪk/ | adj. | 整體的、全方位的 |
| unfazed | /ʌnˋfezd/ | adj. | 不為所動的、鎮定的 |
| unapologetically | /ˏʌnəˏpɑləˋdʒɛtɪklɪ/ | adv. | 毫不愧疚地、理直氣壯地 |
| appease | /əˋpiz/ | v. | 安撫、討好 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`unlocked one of my trap cards`**：打開了我的一張陷阱卡（源自遊戲王卡牌），比喻「正好戳中我準備要講的重點」。
- **`put this across as delicately as I can`**：盡我所能委婉地表達；`put across` 意為「把想法傳達出去」。
- **`put yourself first`**：把自己擺在第一位。
- **`virtue signal`**：道德作秀——為了博取好感而刻意表現得很有德行。
- **`Life goes fast.`**：人生飛逝——簡短有力的感嘆句。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`we sacrifice the thing we want for the thing that's supposed to get it`** — `sacrifice A for B`（為了 B 犧牲 A）；`that's supposed to` 表「本該、被認為應該」。
- **`the happier I get, the more I am going to do ...`** — 「the + 比較級, the + 比較級」句型，表「越⋯⋯就越⋯⋯」。
- **`If anything, I have found ...`** — `if anything` 是轉折語，表「若真要說，反倒是⋯⋯」，用來修正或加強前面的說法。

---

## 20. 越來越無情地把自己擺第一：刪掉行事曆

### 逐句對照

**主持人:** How have you got more comfortable at being the unapologetic self-prioritizer?
你是怎麼變得越來越自在，去當那個毫不愧疚、把自己擺第一的人的？

**Naval:** Yeah, I've gotten more and more ruthless on it. Mainly it's that I see or hear people's freedom, and then that liberates me further.
對，我在這件事上變得越來越無情。主要是因為我看到或聽到別人的自由，那又進一步解放了我。

**Naval:** So I read a blog post by Mark, aka Marc Andreessen, where he said don't keep a schedule, and I took that to heart. So I deleted my calendar and I don't keep a schedule. I try to remember it all in my head. If I can't remember it, I'm not going to add it.
我讀了一篇 Mark，也就是 Marc Andreessen 寫的部落格文章，他說「不要排行程」，我把這句話牢記在心。所以我刪掉了我的行事曆，我不排行程。我試著把所有事都記在腦子裡。如果我記不住，那我就不會把它加進來。

**主持人:** I'm glad you got here on time.
還好你準時到了。

**Naval:** Yeah, exactly. I hate to look things up at the last minute. So, ironically, I don't even know if Mark himself follows that, but he made the correct point.
對，沒錯。我討厭到最後一刻還要去查東西。所以說也諷刺，我根本不知道 Mark 自己有沒有照做，但他講的道理是對的。

**Naval:** I read a little story about Jack Dorsey doing all his business off his iPhone and iPad and not even going into a Mac, and I said, okay, I want to do that. So I'm going to operate through text messaging and not put up my nasty email.
我讀到一個關於 Jack Dorsey 的小故事，說他所有生意都用 iPhone 和 iPad 處理，甚至不碰 Mac，我就想，好，我也要這樣。所以我打算全靠簡訊來運作，不去架起我那個討人厭的電子郵件。

**主持人:** Does that feel like more freedom?
那感覺起來更自由嗎？

**Naval:** It does, yeah. Because you're on the go. So I have a nasty email autoresponder that says, I don't check email, and don't text me either. If you need to find me, you'll find me.
確實，對。因為你隨時在移動。所以我設了一個很機車的郵件自動回覆，寫著：我不看信，也別傳簡訊給我。你要找我，你自然找得到我。

**Naval:** Obviously, some of this is a luxury of success, but some of these habits I adopted long before. Actually, the hostile email autoresponder started a long time ago.
顯然這裡面有些是成功帶來的奢侈，但有些習慣是我很早以前就養成的。事實上那個很不友善的郵件自動回覆是很久以前就開始用了。

**Naval:** I used to own the domain. I let it go. I don't do coffee.com. I used to reply from that email just so people would get the point. But I stopped being rude about it. Now I just ghost. I just disappear.
我以前擁有那個網域，後來我放掉了。我不搞 coffee.com（意指「別找我喝咖啡」）。我以前會用那個信箱回信，就是要讓人家聽懂弦外之音。但我後來不再那麼失禮了。現在我就直接「玩失蹤」，人就消失。

**Naval:** My wife knows not to ever book or schedule me for anything. I'm not expected to go to couples dinners. I'm not expected to go to birthdays. I'm not expected to go to weddings.
我太太知道永遠不要幫我預約或安排任何事情。大家不會期待我出席夫妻聚餐，不會期待我去生日派對，也不會期待我去婚禮。

**Naval:** If somebody tries to rope her into having me show up, she says, he makes his own decisions. You've got to ask him directly.
如果有人想拉她下水、想辦法讓我出席，她會說：他自己會做決定。你得直接去問他。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| ruthless | /ˋruθlɪs/ | adj. | 無情的、毫不留情的 |
| liberate | /ˋlɪbəˏret/ | v. | 解放、使自由 |
| autoresponder | /ˋɔtorɪˏspɑndɚ/ | n. | 自動回覆（郵件） |
| hostile | /ˋhɑstḷ/ | adj. | 有敵意的、不友善的 |
| ghost | /gost/ | v. | 突然斷聯、玩失蹤（口語） |
| rope (sb) into | /rop/ | v. | 拉某人參與、慫恿某人 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`take (something) to heart`**：把某句話牢記在心、認真看待。
- **`on the go`**：在移動中、忙個不停。
- **`get the point`**：聽懂重點、領會弦外之音。
- **`I just ghost.`**：我就直接玩失蹤（不回訊息、直接消失）。
- **`rope her into ...`**：把她拉進來、慫恿她做某事（通常是對方本不情願）。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`I'm not expected to go to weddings.`** — 被動語態 `be expected to`，表「（別人）不期待我去⋯⋯」，語意是「我沒有出席的義務」。
- **`If somebody tries to rope her into having me show up`** — `rope sb into + V-ing`；`having me show up` 是動名詞，`me` 為意義上的主詞，`show up` 為使役 `have + 受詞 + 原形動詞`。
- **`some of these habits I adopted long before`** — 受詞 `some of these habits` 前置（topicalization），強調主題，口語常見的倒裝。

---

## 21. 自由即機緣：最怕過去的我綁架現在的我

### 逐句對照

**主持人:** What about vice versa? Are you not killing serendipity in a way?
那反過來呢？你這樣做，難道不是在某種程度上扼殺了機緣嗎？

**Naval:** No, no. I'm freeing up all my time. So my entire life is serendipity. I get to interact with whoever I want, whenever I want, wherever.
不不。我是在把我所有的時間都空出來。所以我的整個人生就是機緣。我可以跟我想見的任何人、在我想要的任何時間、任何地點互動。

**Naval:** You'll hear the invite, but make the decision, because if there's fewer things incoming, you're assuming that you know what's best for you at anything in the future.
你會聽到邀約，但當下再做決定，因為如果排進來的事情比較少，就代表你在假設自己現在就知道未來任何時刻對你最好的是什麼。

**Naval:** So I'll say, okay, if that thing is interesting, I'll see if I can get in that day when I'm in the mood. But there's nothing worse than something coming up that your past self committed you to that your present self doesn't want to do.
所以我會說，好，如果那件事有趣，我到那天有心情的話，再看看能不能參加。但沒有什麼比這更糟的了：一件由「過去的你」替你答應下來、「現在的你」卻不想做的事，冒了出來。

**主持人:** God damn it.
真該死。

**Naval:** Yeah. And then it destroys your entire calendar. It destroys your day, because there's like this one-hour slot sitting like a turd on my calendar that I have to schedule my whole day around. I can't do anything the 20 minutes before, the 20 minutes afterwards.
對。然後它摧毀你整個行事曆。它毀了你一整天，因為行事曆上就杵著這麼一個一小時的時段，像坨屎一樣，我整天的安排都得繞著它轉。它前面二十分鐘、後面二十分鐘，我什麼都做不了。

**Naval:** Even for phone calls, if someone wants to do a phone call, say, okay, just text me when you're free, I'll text you when I'm free, and we'll just do it on the fly.
就連打電話也是，如果有人想通電話，就說：好，你有空的時候傳個訊息給我，我有空也傳給你，我們臨時起意直接打就好。

**Naval:** It's a much better way of living than this overly scheduled cal.com or iCal, whatever.
這種生活方式比那種被 cal.com 或 iCal 之類的東西排得滿滿的日子好太多了。

**主持人:** The overscheduled life is not worth living.
被過度安排的人生不值得過。

**Naval:** It's not. I think it's a terrible way to live life. That's not how we evolved. It's not how we grew up. It's not how we were as children, hopefully, unless you're a helicopter parent or a tiger mom.
確實不值得。我覺得那是很糟糕的生活方式。我們不是這樣演化來的，不是這樣長大的，小時候也不是這樣過的——但願如此，除非你是那種直升機父母或虎媽。

**Naval:** Your natural order is freedom. I had a friend who said to me once, I never want to have to be at a specific place at a specific time. And I was like, oh my god, that's freedom. When I heard that, that changed my life right there.
你的自然狀態就是自由。我有個朋友有次跟我說，我永遠不想被迫在特定的時間出現在特定的地點。我就想，天哪，那就是自由。當我聽到那句話，我的人生當場就被改變了。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| serendipity | /ˏsɛrənˋdɪpətɪ/ | n. | 機緣、意外的美好巧合 |
| incoming | /ˋɪnˏkʌmɪŋ/ | adj. | 進來的、即將到來的 |
| commit | /kəˋmɪt/ | v. | 使承諾、使負有義務 |
| slot | /slɑt/ | n. | 時段、空檔 |
| evolve | /ɪˋvɑlv/ | v. | 演化、演變 |
| helicopter parent | — | n. | 直升機父母（過度盯著孩子的父母） |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`free up (time)`**：空出、騰出（時間）。
- **`on the fly`**：臨時起意、即興地、當場處理。
- **`sitting like a turd on my calendar`**：像坨屎一樣杵在行事曆上——粗俗但生動地形容礙眼又擺脫不掉的行程。
- **`vice versa`**：反之亦然（拉丁語外來語）。
- **`tiger mom`**：虎媽——對孩子要求極嚴的母親。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`there's nothing worse than something ... that your past self committed you to that your present self doesn't want to do`** — `nothing worse than` 最高級比較；後接兩個關係子句連續修飾 `something`（一個由 that 引導）。
- **`Are you not killing serendipity ...?`** — 否定疑問句，帶質疑/反問語氣，期待對方澄清或反駁。
- **`That's not how we evolved.`** — `how + 子句`當補語，指「那不是我們演化的方式」；下文以平行結構重複 `It's not how we grew up / were as children`。

---

## 22. 不用鬧鐘、自由是本性、一天的能量節奏

### 逐句對照

**主持人:** Are you still alarm-clockless?
你還是不用鬧鐘嗎？

**Naval:** Yes, I'm alarm-clockless. Today I did set my alarm clock just so I wouldn't miss this.
對，我不用鬧鐘。今天我倒是有設鬧鐘，就只是為了不要錯過這場訪談。

**主持人:** Very important.
非常重要。

**Naval:** Yeah. But just so you know, I set the alarm clock for 11:00 a.m. in case I was stricken with a flu that day. I wasn't going to set my alarm clock for 8:00 a.m. or 9:00 a.m. And sure enough, I got up many hours before that.
對。不過跟你說一聲，我把鬧鐘設在早上十一點，以防那天我剛好中了流感。我才不會把鬧鐘設在八點或九點。而果不其然，我在那之前好幾個小時就起床了。

**Naval:** But it was sort of a backup emergency alarm. In fact, sometimes when there's something that I need to do, I don't want to look at a calendar, so I'll just set an alarm for it.
但它算是一個備用的緊急鬧鐘。事實上，有時候當我有件事必須做，我又不想去看行事曆，我就乾脆設個鬧鐘來提醒。

**主持人:** Just sink a little bit more into that kind of that "fuck you" energy, that self-prioritizing energy, because I think people rationally love the idea of this. I'm going to do what only I want to do, even if they've got the level of freedom.
再多深入聊一下那種「去你的」能量、那種把自己擺第一的能量，因為我覺得人們在理智上都很愛這個主意。我只做我想做的事——就算他們已經擁有足夠的自由。

**Naval:** It's not "fuck you" energy in the sense that I think everyone should live their life that way to the greatest extent possible. Obviously, we have our requirements around work and obligations that are genuinely important to us.
它不是那種「去你的」能量，因為我認為每個人都應該盡可能地那樣過生活。顯然我們有一些圍繞著工作的必要事項，還有一些對我們真正重要的責任義務。

**Naval:** But don't fritter away your life on randomly scheduled things and things that aren't important, and events and weddings and tedious dinners with tedious people that you don't want to go to.
但別把你的人生浪費在那些隨機排進來、又不重要的事情上，還有那些活動、婚禮，以及跟無趣的人吃的、你根本不想去的無趣晚餐。

**Naval:** To the extent you can bring freedom into your life, optimize for that. You'll actually be more productive. You won't just be happier and more free, you will be more productive, because then you can focus on what is in front of you, whatever the biggest problem of that day.
在你能把自由帶進生活的範圍內，就以它為最佳化目標。你其實會變得更有生產力。你不只會更快樂、更自由，你還會更有生產力，因為那樣你就能專注在你眼前的事情上，也就是那天最大的問題。

**Naval:** When I wake up in the morning, the first four hours are when I have the most energy, and that's when I want to solve all the hard problems.
當我早上醒來，頭四個小時是我精力最充沛的時候，那也是我想解決所有難題的時候。

**Naval:** And the next four hours are when I kind of want to do some more outdoorsy activities, or I want to work out, or maybe I can have some meetings, but I'll try to do those last-second based on whatever the day's priorities demand.
接下來的四個小時，我大概會想做些比較戶外的活動，或想健身，或者也許安排一些會議，但我會盡量根據那天的優先順序臨時決定要不要開這些會。

**Naval:** The last four hours, I kind of want to wind down. I want to hang out with the kids, and I want to play games or read a book or something like that.
最後四個小時，我大概會想放鬆下來。我想陪陪孩子，想玩玩遊戲，或讀本書之類的。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| stricken | /ˋstrɪkən/ | adj. | 受侵襲的、患病的 |
| obligation | /ˏɑbləˋgeʃən/ | n. | 責任、義務 |
| fritter away | /ˋfrɪtɚ/ | v. | 一點一點浪費掉 |
| tedious | /ˋtidɪəs/ | adj. | 冗長乏味的、無趣的 |
| optimize | /ˋɑptəˏmaɪz/ | v. | 最佳化 |
| wind down | /waɪnd/ | v. | 放鬆、慢下來 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`sure enough`**：果不其然、果然如此。
- **`just so you know`**：只是先跟你說一聲、讓你知道一下。
- **`fritter away your life`**：把人生一點一滴地浪費掉。
- **`to the extent (that) you can`**：在你能力所及的範圍內。
- **`wind down`**：放鬆、收尾（一天的節奏慢下來）。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`I set the alarm clock ... in case I was stricken with a flu`** — `in case + 子句`表「以防萬一」；此處用過去式呼應敘事時態。
- **`the first four hours are when I have the most energy`** — `時間名詞 + be + when 子句`，用 `when` 引導名詞子句當補語，口語中常見（等同 `the time when...`）。
- **`To the extent you can bring freedom into your life, optimize for that.`** — `To the extent (that)...` 引導程度副詞子句；主句為祈使句 `optimize`。

---

## 23. 彈性分配時間：靈感易逝，立刻行動

### 逐句對照

**Naval:** So having that flexibility and freedom is really important, so you can just put whatever is most needed into the slot at that moment.
所以擁有那種彈性和自由真的很重要，這樣你就能在當下那一刻，把最需要做的事放進那個時段。

**Naval:** And instead, if I have like a meeting at 2 p.m. and then I have to get a thing and some emails done, I put that off till 6 p.m. I'm rushing, I'm not going to be productive.
反之，如果我下午兩點有個會議，然後我還得完成一件事和一些郵件，我把那些拖到晚上六點，那我就會很趕，就不會有生產力。

**主持人:** You're certainly not free.
你肯定不自由。

**Naval:** I'm definitely not free. But also another thing that I really believe is that inspiration is perishable. Act on it immediately. So when you're inspired to do something, do that thing.
我絕對不自由。但還有一件我非常相信的事：靈感是會腐壞的。要立刻行動。所以當你受到啟發想做某件事，就去做那件事。

**Naval:** If I'm inspired to write a blog post, I want to do it at that moment. If I'm inspired to send a tweet, I want to do it at that moment. If I'm inspired to solve a problem, I do it that moment. If I'm inspired to read a book, I want to read it right then.
如果我有靈感想寫篇部落格文章，我就想在那一刻寫。如果我有靈感想發則推文，我就想在那一刻發。如果我有靈感想解決一個問題，我就在那一刻解決。如果我有靈感想讀本書，我就想當下馬上讀。

**Naval:** If I want to learn something, I do it at the moment of curiosity. The moment the curiosity arrives, I go learn that thing immediately. I download the book. I get on Google. I get on ChatGPT, whatever. I will figure that thing out on the spot, and that's when the learning happens.
如果我想學某樣東西，我就在好奇心湧現的那一刻去學。好奇心一到，我就馬上去學那個東西。我下載那本書、上 Google、開 ChatGPT，隨便什麼都行。我會當場把那件事搞懂，而那正是學習真正發生的時候。

**Naval:** It doesn't happen because I've scheduled time, because I've set an hour aside, because when that time arrives I might be in a different mood. I might just want to do something different.
學習不會因為我排了時間、因為我空出了一小時就發生，因為當那個時間到了，我可能心情不一樣了。我可能只是想做點別的事。

**Naval:** So I think that spontaneity is really important. You're going to learn best when you're having fun, when you generally are enjoying the process, not when you're forced to sit there and do it.
所以我覺得自發性真的很重要。你會在玩得開心的時候學得最好，在你大致上享受這個過程的時候，而不是在你被逼著坐在那裡做的時候。

**Naval:** How much do you remember from school? You were forced to learn geography, history, mathematics on this schedule, at this time, according to this person. Didn't happen.
你還記得多少學校裡教的東西？你被逼著照這個課表、在這個時間、根據這個人的規定去學地理、歷史、數學。結果根本沒學進去。

**Naval:** All the stuff that sticks with you is you learned it when you wanted to, when you genuinely had the desire. And that freedom, that ability to act on something the moment you want to, is so liberating that most of us go through our lives with very, very little tastes of that.
所有真正留在你腦中的東西，都是你在「想學的時候」、在你真心有渴望的時候學的。而那種自由，那種一想做就能立刻去做的能力，是如此地令人解放，以至於我們大多數人一輩子只嘗到極少、極少的那種滋味。

**Naval:** If you live your entire life that way, that is a recipe for happiness.
如果你整個人生都那樣過，那就是一帖快樂的良方。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| flexibility | /ˏflɛksəˋbɪlətɪ/ | n. | 彈性、靈活度 |
| perishable | /ˋpɛrɪʃəbḷ/ | adj. | 易腐壞的、易消逝的 |
| inspiration | /ˏɪnspəˋreʃən/ | n. | 靈感、啟發 |
| spontaneity | /ˏspɑntəˋniətɪ/ | n. | 自發性、隨興 |
| stick with | /stɪk/ | v. | 留存、不忘 |
| recipe | /ˋrɛsəpɪ/ | n. | 食譜、（比喻）祕方 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`put (something) off`**：把某事拖延、延後。
- **`act on it`**：依它行動、付諸實行。
- **`on the spot`**：當場、立刻。
- **`set an hour aside`**：撥出／空出一小時。
- **`a recipe for happiness`**：快樂的祕方（`a recipe for X` 是慣用比喻，X 也可以是壞事，如 `a recipe for disaster`）。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`inspiration is perishable`** — 用形容 food 的字 `perishable`（易腐壞）比喻靈感，是生動的隱喻。
- **`The moment the curiosity arrives, I go learn that thing immediately.`** — `the moment + 子句` 當連接詞，等同 `as soon as`（一⋯⋯就⋯⋯）。
- **`that ability ... is so liberating that most of us go through our lives with very little tastes of that`** — `so + 形容詞 + that...` 表「如此⋯⋯以至於⋯⋯」。

---

## 24. 效率與快樂並不衝突：拖延就是想做別的

### 逐句對照

**主持人:** It feels like efficiency, that that you have.
你擁有的那個東西，感覺起來像是一種效率。

**Naval:** Efficient also.
也很有效率。

**主持人:** You have the inspiration that is going to be the most frictionless time to ever do that particular task. So, oh, I've had the inspiration to do that, I'll put that off until a time when I no longer really want to do it quite so much.
你有了靈感，而那正是做那件特定任務阻力最小的時刻。結果卻是：喔，我有靈感想做那件事了，我卻把它拖到一個我已經沒那麼想做它的時候。

**主持人:** And while I do want to do that thing, I'll do something else that I needed to do because it's on the schedule.
然後在我明明想做那件事的當下，我卻去做了另一件我「必須做」的事，只因為它排在行程上。

**Naval:** It does not work. Procrastination is because you don't want to do that thing right now. You want to do something else. Go do that something else.
那行不通。拖延的原因就是你現在不想做那件事。你想做別的事。那就去做那件別的事吧。

**Naval:** I reject this frame that efficiency and productivity and success are counter to happiness and freedom. They actually go together.
我不接受這種框架——認為效率、生產力和成功是跟快樂與自由對立的。它們其實是相輔相成的。

**主持人:** How so?
怎麼說？

**Naval:** The happier you are, the more you can sustain doing something, the more likely you're going to do something that will in turn make you even happier, and you'll continue to do it and you'll outwork everybody else.
你越快樂，就越能持續地做一件事，也就越可能去做那些反過來讓你更快樂的事，於是你會繼續做下去，而且會比其他所有人都更拚。

**Naval:** The more free you are, the better you can allocate your time, and the less you're caught up in a web of obligations and commitments, and the more you can focus on the task at hand.
你越自由，就越能分配好你的時間，就越不會被困在一張責任與承諾織成的網裡，也就越能專注在手上的工作。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| efficiency | /ɪˋfɪʃənsɪ/ | n. | 效率 |
| frictionless | /ˋfrɪkʃənlɪs/ | adj. | 無摩擦的、毫無阻力的 |
| procrastination | /proˏkræstəˋneʃən/ | n. | 拖延 |
| counter to | /ˋkaʊntɚ/ | phr. | 與⋯⋯相反、對立 |
| allocate | /ˋæləˏket/ | v. | 分配、配置 |
| outwork | /aʊtˋwɝk/ | v. | 比⋯⋯更勤奮、工作量勝過 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`How so?`**：怎麼說？——請對方進一步解釋的簡短問句。
- **`put (that) off`**：把某事往後拖延。
- **`go together`**：相輔相成、可以並存。
- **`caught up in a web of ...`**：被困在⋯⋯的網／羅網裡（`web` 比喻錯綜複雜的牽絆）。
- **`the task at hand`**：手邊的、當前的任務。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`Procrastination is because you don't want to do that thing right now.`** — 口語中把 `because` 子句直接接在 `is` 後當補語（正式寫法會是 `Procrastination happens because...`）。
- **`I reject this frame that efficiency ... are counter to happiness`** — `that` 引導同位語子句，說明 `frame`（框架、觀點）的內容。
- **`The happier you are, the more you can sustain ..., the more likely you're going to ...`** — 多重「the + 比較級」堆疊，層層遞進地表達連鎖因果。

---

---

## 25. 找到對你像玩、對別人像工作的事：把自己產品化

### 逐句對照

**主持人:** This is related to another insight of yours. The less you want something, the less you're thinking about it, the less you're obsessing over it, the more you're going to do it in a natural way, the more you're going to do it for yourself, in a way that you're good at, and you're going to stick with it. The people around you will see the quality of your work is higher.
這跟你另一個洞見有關。你越不想要某樣東西、越不去想它、越不對它執著，你反而越會自然而然地去做，越會為了自己而做，用你擅長的方式去做，而且越能堅持下去。你身邊的人會看到你作品的品質更高。

**主持人:** But this seems like a difficult tension to navigate because an obsessive attention to detail is a competitive advantage of your work as well. So you have these two things sort of conflicting with each other.
但這似乎是一個很難拿捏的張力，因為對細節的執著同時也是你作品的競爭優勢。所以這兩件事有點互相衝突。

**Naval:** No one is going to beat you at being you. So one of the things I like to say is: find what feels like play to you but looks like work to others. So it looks like work to them, but to you it feels like play. It's not work.
沒有人能在「當你自己」這件事上贏過你。所以我很喜歡講一句話：找到那件對你來說像在玩、但在別人眼中像工作的事。在他們看來那是工作，但對你而言像遊戲，根本不算工作。

**Naval:** So you're going to out-compete them because you're doing it effortlessly. You're doing it for fun. They're doing it for work, for some byproduct. To you it's art. It's beauty. It's joy. It's flow. It's fulfilling.
所以你會勝過他們，因為你做起來毫不費力。你是為了樂趣而做，他們是為了工作、為了某種附帶利益而做。對你來說那是藝術、是美、是喜悅、是心流、是充實。

**Naval:** You must enjoy podcasting. If you didn't, you wouldn't be good at it. If you decided that the right way to get ahead in life was to go write books, nobody would have heard of you. Chris Williamson's book would be a complete flop. That's not who you are. You're a podcaster. You enjoy talking to people. You enjoy interviewing them.
你一定很享受做 podcast。如果你不享受，你就不會做得好。如果你當初認定人生要出人頭地的正確方式是去寫書，那根本不會有人聽過你。Chris Williamson 的書會徹底慘敗。那不是真正的你。你是個 podcaster，你喜歡跟人聊天，喜歡訪問他們。

**Naval:** The more you do things that are natural to you, the less competition you have. You escape competition through authenticity, by being your own self.
你越是做那些對你來說自然的事，你面對的競爭就越少。你靠著做自己、靠著真實，來擺脫競爭。

**Naval:** If I had to summarize how to be successful in life in two words, I would just say: productize yourself. That's it. Just figure out what it is that you naturally do that the world might want, that you can scale up and turn into a product, and it'll eventually be effortless for you.
如果要我用兩個字總結人生怎麼成功，我會說：把自己產品化。就這樣。就是搞清楚你天生就會做、而世界可能想要的那件事，把它規模化、變成一項產品，最終它對你來說會毫不費力。

**Naval:** Yes, there's always work required, but it won't even feel like work to you. It'll feel like play to you.
沒錯，總是會有需要付出的工作，但它對你甚至不會感覺像工作，它會感覺像在玩。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| productize | /ˋprɑdʌkˏtaɪz/ | v. | 把（自己/能力）產品化 |
| effortlessly | /ˋɛfɚtlɪslɪ/ | adv. | 毫不費力地 |
| byproduct | /ˋbaɪˏprɑdʌkt/ | n. | 副產品、附帶結果 |
| authenticity | /ˏɔθɛnˋtɪsətɪ/ | n. | 真實性、真我 |
| flop | /flɑp/ | n. | 徹底失敗（作品）、慘敗 |
| scale up | /skel ʌp/ | phr. | 規模化、擴大規模 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`find what feels like play to you but looks like work to others`**：Naval 的名言——「找到對你像玩、對別人像工作的事」，暗示這就是不費力勝出的關鍵。
- **`out-compete`**：在競爭中勝過對方，`out-` 前綴表「超越、勝過」（如 outperform, outlast）。
- **`get ahead in life`**：在人生中出人頭地、往上爬。
- **`that's not who you are`**：「那不是真正的你」，口語中常用來否定某個不符本性的選擇。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`The less you want something, the more you're going to do it.`** — `The + 比較級..., the + 比較級...` 句型（越⋯⋯就越⋯⋯），此處連續堆疊多個 the less / the more，形成排比。
- **`If you didn't, you wouldn't be good at it.`** — 與現在事實相反的第二類條件句：`if + 過去式, would + 原形`。
- **`nobody would have heard of you`** — 混合條件：對過去的假設結果用 `would have + p.p.`。

---

## 26. 現代社會無限機會：人生是搜尋函數，別過早承諾

### 逐句對照

**Naval:** And modern society gives us that opportunity. If you were 2,000 years ago, you're born on a farm. Your choices are very limited. You're going to do stuff on that farm.
而現代社會給了我們這樣的機會。如果你活在兩千年前，你出生在一座農場，你的選擇非常有限，你就是會在那座農場上幹活。

**Naval:** Now, you can literally wake up and move to a different city. You can switch careers. You can switch jobs. You can change the people that you're with. You can change so many things about who you are and who you're with and what you're doing, that there is infinite opportunity out there for you. Literally infinite.
但現在，你真的可以一覺醒來就搬到另一座城市。你可以換跑道、換工作、換身邊的人。你能改變太多關於「你是誰、你和誰在一起、你在做什麼」的事情，以至於外面對你而言有無限的機會。真的是無限。

**Naval:** And so it's much better to treat this like a search function: to find the people who need you the most, to find the work that needs you the most, to find the place you're best suited to be at.
所以更好的做法是把這件事當成一個搜尋函數：去找到最需要你的人，找到最需要你的工作，找到最適合你待的地方。

**Naval:** And it's worthwhile to spend time in that exploration before diving into exploitation. The biggest mistake in a world with so many choices is premature commitment.
在一頭栽進「開發利用」之前，花時間去「探索」是值得的。在一個選擇這麼多的世界裡，最大的錯誤就是過早承諾。

**Naval:** If you prematurely commit to being a lawyer or a doctor, and now you've got like 5 years invested into that, you might have just completely missed. You might end up in the wrong profession, the wrong place, or with the wrong people for 30 years of your life, grinding away.
如果你太早就一頭栽進當律師或醫生，結果已經投入了大概五年，那你可能整個押錯了。你可能落入錯的行業、錯的地方，或跟錯的人一起，磨了整整三十年。

**Naval:** And yes, the best time to figure that out was before, but the second best time is now. So just change it.
沒錯，想通這件事最好的時機是當初，但第二好的時機就是現在。所以就去改變它吧。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| infinite | /ˋɪnfənɪt/ | adj. | 無限的 |
| exploration | /ˏɛkspləˋreʃən/ | n. | 探索 |
| exploitation | /ˏɛksplɔɪˋteʃən/ | n. | 開發利用、發揮 |
| premature | /ˏpriməˋtʃʊr/ | adj. | 過早的、倉促的 |
| commitment | /kəˋmɪtmənt/ | n. | 承諾、投入 |
| grind away | /graɪnd əˋwe/ | phr. | 埋頭苦幹、辛苦磨 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`a search function`**：把人生比喻成「搜尋函數」——不斷嘗試以找到最佳解，而非一開始就鎖死。
- **`dive into`**：一頭栽進、投入某事。
- **`best suited to`**：最適合（做某事／待某處）。
- **`the second best time is now`**：化用諺語「種樹最好的時機是二十年前，其次是現在」，強調亡羊補牢猶未晚。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`If you were 2,000 years ago, you're born on a farm.`** — 口語中的假設，時態並不嚴謹（正式應為 `If you were born 2,000 years ago, you'd be born...`），這正是逐字稿口語的特徵。
- **`explore ... before diving into exploitation`** — `before + 動名詞` 表時間先後；此處也是探索期 vs 開發期的核心對比。

---

## 27. 預設一律說不：探索期 vs 開發期、保護心流

### 逐句對照

**主持人:** And also, presumably kill things that aren't working very quickly.
另外，大概也要很快地砍掉那些行不通的事吧。

**Naval:** By default, you should kill everything. If you can't decide, the answer is no. And most things you should just be saying no to. The way I keep my calendar free is just by default saying no to everything.
預設情況下，你應該砍掉一切。如果你決定不了，答案就是不。而大多數事情你就該直接說不。我之所以能讓行事曆保持空白，就是靠著預設對一切說不。

**Naval:** One of the other things: early on in life, you're looking for opportunities. So you're saying yes to everything. And that is a phase that you go through — that is the exploration phase. Later, when you've found the thing you want to work on, you're in the exploitation phase. You have to say no to everything by default.
還有一件事：人生早期，你在尋找機會，所以你對一切說是。那是你會經歷的一個階段——那是探索期。之後，當你找到了想投入的那件事，你就進入了開發期。這時你必須預設對一切說不。

**Naval:** And if you don't say no to everything by default, if you have to even explicitly go out of your way to say no to something, that will take up time.
如果你不預設對一切說不，如果你甚至還得特地繞路去對某件事說不，那都會佔用你的時間。

**Naval:** For example, there are a lot of people into hustle culture, and a big piece of hustle culture is like: well, you're not going to get something if you don't ask for it. So they'll hustle people. They'll always be sending you requests, messages.
舉例來說，有很多人信奉「拼命三郎文化」，而這種文化很重要的一環就是：你不開口要，就得不到。所以他們會去死纏爛打，不停地傳給你各種請求和訊息。

**Naval:** Yeah, this is a famous person problem, but I have it. People are always asking me for things. And I kind of squirm when I get these messages — and I'm sure you get these too — texts and emails saying, "Hey, Chris, my friend so-and-so should really be on your podcast," or "you should come to my event," or "you should write a foreword for my book." And you kind of squirm when you get this, right? You have to figure out how to say no.
對，這算是名人才有的煩惱，但我確實有。大家老是來拜託我做各種事。收到這些訊息時我會有點渾身不自在——我相信你也會收到——那些簡訊、email 說：「嘿 Chris，我某某朋友真的很該上你的節目」，或「你該來我的活動」，或「你該幫我的書寫序」。收到這些你會有點不自在吧？你得想辦法說不。

**Naval:** And one of the things I learned along the way is that if you wouldn't ask somebody else to do it, and then you get that request yourself, you can just dismiss it. You don't have to respond. You don't even let it enter your brain.
我一路上學到的一件事是：如果這件事你自己都不會開口去拜託別人，那當你收到同樣的請求時，你大可直接無視它。你不必回覆，你甚至不讓它進到你的腦子裡。

**Naval:** You have to be able to delete emails and text messages without flinching if you want to scale. And scaling your time is really important. Every interruption will take you out of flow.
如果你想要規模化，你必須能夠眼睛都不眨地刪掉 email 和簡訊。把你的時間規模化非常重要。每一次打擾都會把你拉出心流。

**Naval:** So the only way you can remain in flow is if you get very good at ignoring these things by default, or closing yourself off like a hermit — like our mutual friend Tim Ferriss does — or you just become emotionally capable of not registering these as something that causes turbulence inside of you.
所以你能維持在心流裡的唯一方法，就是變得非常擅長預設忽略這些東西，或者像隱士一樣把自己封閉起來——就像我們共同的朋友 Tim Ferriss 那樣——再不然就是你在情緒上變得有能力，不把這些東西登記成會在你內心掀起波瀾的事。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| by default | /baɪ dɪˋfɔlt/ | phr. | 預設地、在沒特別決定時 |
| squirm | /skwɝm/ | v. | （尷尬得）渾身不自在、扭捏 |
| dismiss | /dɪsˋmɪs/ | v. | 打發掉、不予理會 |
| flinch | /flɪntʃ/ | v. | 畏縮、退卻 |
| hermit | /ˋhɝmɪt/ | n. | 隱士 |
| turbulence | /ˋtɝbjələns/ | n. | 動盪、內心波瀾 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`hustle culture`**：拼命三郎／狂拚文化，強調無止盡地努力與爭取。
- **`so-and-so`**：某某人（不指名時的泛稱）。
- **`without flinching`**：眼睛都不眨、毫不猶豫地。
- **`go out of your way to`**：特地、不辭麻煩地去做某事。
- **`take you out of flow`**：把你拉出心流狀態。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`If you can't decide, the answer is no.`** — 零條件句（普遍真理／原則）：`if + 現在式, 現在式`。
- **`if you wouldn't ask somebody else to do it ... you can just dismiss it`** — 假設語氣 `wouldn't` 表「（在假想情境下）不會去做」，作為判斷是否無視請求的準則。

---

## 28. 被他人慾望操縱太久，說不像犯了戰爭罪

### 逐句對照

**主持人:** That "not registering it emotionally" thing — it's fundamental. That's so fundamental to so many things in life. Okay, can we dig into that a little bit? Because again, I've only seen you as you, right? I didn't know you 20 years ago, I didn't know you as a child. So I've only seen you with this holistic selfishness, this integrated self-prioritization — whatever we called it.
你說的那個「不在情緒上把它登記下來」，這太根本了。這對人生中好多事情都太根本了。好，我們可以稍微深入談一下嗎？因為說到底，我只見過現在這個你，對吧？我二十年前不認識你，我不認識小時候的你。所以我只見過帶著這種「整體性自私」、這種「整合過的自我優先」的你——不管我們怎麼稱呼它。

**Naval:** Selfish is fine. I'll take selfish. I'm selfish. I'm a very selfish person. Don't contact me.
「自私」沒問題，我接受「自私」。我很自私，我是個非常自私的人。別聯絡我。

**主持人:** Yeah, that emotional reaction. I also get the sense that maybe people have lived an obligation life for so long that they actually kind of struggle to tap into what it is that they want. They've hidden their wants and their desires and their needs, and they've deprioritized themselves so much for so long that they go, "What do I actually want? What is it? Do I want to go to this thing or not?"
對，那種情緒反應。我也有種感覺，也許有些人過「被義務綁住的人生」過了太久，久到他們其實很難去觸及自己真正想要什麼。他們把自己的想要、慾望、需求都藏了起來，把自己擺在最後太久太久，久到他們會問：「我到底想要什麼？那是什麼？我到底想不想去這個活動？」

**主持人:** Because all I've done is be puppeted, right? I've been marionetted by other people's desires for so, so long that I can't even tap into that anymore. And saying no feels like a war crime.
因為我做的一切都只是被人操縱，對吧？我被別人的慾望像牽線木偶一樣擺弄了太久太久，久到我再也接不上自己的想法了。而說「不」感覺就像犯了戰爭罪。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| fundamental | /ˏfʌndəˋmɛntl̩/ | adj. | 根本的、基礎的 |
| selfish | /ˋsɛlfɪʃ/ | adj. | 自私的 |
| obligation | /ˏɑbləˋgeʃən/ | n. | 義務、責任 |
| deprioritize | /diˏpraɪˋɔrəˏtaɪz/ | v. | 把⋯⋯降到次要、擺後面 |
| marionette | /ˏmærɪəˋnɛt/ | n./v. | 牽線木偶；像木偶般操縱 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`tap into`**：接通、汲取（內在的想法、資源或潛能）。
- **`I'll take selfish`**：「自私我照單全收」，`take` 在此表「接受、認了」。
- **`get the sense that...`**：有一種感覺、隱約覺得⋯⋯。
- **`feels like a war crime`**：誇飾用法，形容說「不」時內心強烈的罪惡感，彷彿犯了滔天大罪。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`people have lived an obligation life for so long that they struggle to...`** — `so ... that ...`（如此⋯⋯以至於⋯⋯）表結果，句中連用兩次強化程度。
- **`I've been marionetted by other people's desires`** — 現在完成式被動語態 `have been + p.p.`，強調長期持續至今的被操縱狀態。

---

## 29. 冥想觀照思緒：問題先在腦中成形，要挑剔問題

### 逐句對照

**Naval:** So I think it's really good to be able to view your own mind and your own thoughts objectively, and that is the big benefit of meditation. It creates a small gap between your conscious observation self and your mind, and that lets you look at your thoughts and evaluate them a little bit like you would a third party's statements.
所以我覺得能夠客觀地看待自己的心智、自己的思緒，是很棒的一件事，而這正是冥想最大的好處。它在你「有意識的觀察者自我」和你的心智之間創造出一個小小的縫隙，讓你能去審視自己的念頭、評估它們，有點像你在評估第三方說的話那樣。

**Naval:** If you just take your mind to be you — they're integrated, one and the same at all times — and you're reacting from the mind, then you're not even going to question the things that come into your mind. Anything that comes in and creates a reaction will immediately create a reaction.
如果你直接把你的心智當成「你」——認定兩者隨時都是合而為一的——並且從心智出發去做反應，那你甚至不會去質疑那些進到腦子裡的東西。任何進來、會引發反應的東西，就會立刻引發反應。

**Naval:** But if you can observe your thoughts a little bit — and not in some woo way; you can do it through therapy, through journaling, any way you'd like, you can just take long walks. You don't have to meditate and sit in lotus position, all that is unnecessary. But if you can observe your own thoughts and view them a little objectively, then you can start being a little more choosy, a little more critical.
但如果你能稍微觀察自己的思緒——而且不必用什麼玄之又玄的方式；你可以透過心理治療、透過寫日記，用任何你喜歡的方式，你可以就只是去散長長的步。你不必非得冥想、盤成蓮花座，那些都不必要。但只要你能觀察自己的念頭、稍微客觀地看待它們，你就能開始變得挑剔一點、批判一點。

**Naval:** And you can realize that there are no problems in the real world other than maybe things that inflict pain on your body. Everything else has to become a problem in your mind first. You have to view it, interpret it, and create a narrative that it is a problem before it becomes a problem.
你會體認到：真實世界裡其實沒有什麼問題，頂多就是那些直接讓你身體疼痛的東西。其他一切，都得先在你的腦子裡變成一個問題。你得先去看待它、詮釋它，並編織出「它是個問題」的敘事，它才會真的變成問題。

**Naval:** And then you realize that a lot of your emotional energy is spent reacting to things that your mind is automatically saying are problems. And you don't need all those problems. Do you really need that many problems in your life?
接著你會發現，你有很多情緒能量都花在對那些「你的腦子自動判定為問題」的事物做反應。而你根本不需要那麼多問題。你的人生真的需要那麼多問題嗎？

**Naval:** Again, I would say try to focus on just one overarching problem, and then go solve that problem. It's like: if you want to be successful, define success very concretely. Focus on that. Everything else, when it enters your mind, becomes a problem.
再說一次，我會建議你試著只專注在一個最高層次的問題上，然後去解決那個問題。就好比：如果你想成功，就把成功定義得非常具體，專注在那上面。至於其他一切，一旦進到你腦子裡，就會變成問題。

**Naval:** Whether it's a judgment about the girl walking down the street, or the car that just cut in front of you, or your accountant did this stupid thing — yes, it's going to trigger you, but observe for a moment: it's triggering me. I've created a problem. Do I really want to have this problem right now? Do I want to spend the energy on this problem, or do I want that going somewhere else?
不管是對街上走過的女生下的評斷、剛剛插到你前面的那台車，還是你的會計做了某件蠢事——沒錯，它會踩到你的點，但花一秒觀察一下：這件事踩到我了，我製造了一個問題。我現在真的想擁有這個問題嗎？我想把能量花在這個問題上，還是想把它用在別的地方？

**Naval:** And it doesn't have to be that overt. The mind mud-wrestling with itself is also a problem, because it loves to do that.
而且這不必那麼外顯。心智跟自己「泥巴摔角」也是一種問題，因為它超愛這麼幹。

**主持人:** I have my problems, my problems have got problems, and I have a real problem about fixing my problems.
我有我的問題，我的問題還生出了問題，而且我對「修好我的問題」這件事本身還有個大問題。

**Naval:** Yeah, exactly. So you're going to be much happier and much more focused. Again, I think happiness and focus and success can complement each other. You're going to have much more mental energy to focus on the actual problems you want to solve, if you don't start unconsciously, subconsciously, reactively picking up problems everywhere.
對，正是如此。所以你會快樂很多，也專注很多。再說一次，我認為快樂、專注和成功是能相輔相成的。你會有多得多的心智能量，去專注在你真正想解決的問題上——前提是你別開始無意識地、下意識地、反射性地到處撿問題。

**Naval:** So before anything can be a problem that takes up your emotional energy, you have to accept it as a problem. You can be choosy about your problems. And I'm not saying I'm perfect in that regard, but I think I'm better than I used to be.
所以，在任何東西能夠成為一個佔用你情緒能量的問題之前，你得先接受它是個問題。你可以對自己的問題很挑。我不是說我在這方面很完美，但我想我比以前好多了。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| objectively | /əbˋdʒɛktɪvlɪ/ | adv. | 客觀地 |
| meditation | /ˏmɛdəˋteʃən/ | n. | 冥想、靜坐 |
| narrative | /ˋnærətɪv/ | n. | 敘事、故事線 |
| overarching | /ˏovɚˋɑrtʃɪŋ/ | adj. | 最高層次的、統攝全局的 |
| trigger | /ˋtrɪgɚ/ | v. | 觸發、踩到情緒的點 |
| choosy | /ˋtʃuzɪ/ | adj. | 挑剔的、講究的 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`in some woo way`**：用某種「玄玄的、故弄玄虛的」方式（woo 是 woo-woo 的簡稱，帶調侃玄學／偽科學）。
- **`take X to be Y`**：把 X 當成／認定為 Y。
- **`cut in front of you`**：（開車）插隊、切到你前面。
- **`mud-wrestling with itself`**：跟自己「泥巴摔角」，形容心智無謂地自我糾纏、內耗。
- **`pick up problems`**：（沿路）撿起、招惹一堆問題。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`there are no problems ... other than maybe things that inflict pain on your body`** — `other than` 表「除了⋯⋯之外」，用來設下唯一的例外。
- **`Everything else has to become a problem in your mind first.`** — `has to` 表邏輯上的必然（必須先如此才會如何），呼應後句 `before it becomes a problem`。
- **`Do I want to spend the energy on this, or do I want that going somewhere else?`** — `want + 受詞 + Ving`（want that going）口語用法，表「希望它往別處去」。

---

## 30. 沉迷解決問題：對無法掌控之事培養漠然、媒體是迷因病毒

### 逐句對照

**Naval:** Well, lots of people are addicted to solving problems. So much so that sometimes people create problems when we don't have any, simply so that we can solve them. We have that going on. And then even worse, we take on problems that we can't affect.
嗯，很多人沉迷於解決問題。沉迷到有時候我們明明沒有問題，卻還去製造問題，就只為了能去解決它。我們就是在幹這種事。而更糟的是，我們還去攬下那些我們根本影響不了的問題。

**Naval:** So another one of my little quips was: a rational person can find peace by cultivating indifference to things that are out of their control. And I'm as guilty as anybody of doom-surfing on X or social media and getting worked up about things that I can't do anything about.
所以我另一句小格言是：一個理性的人可以透過對「自己無法掌控之事」培養漠然，來找到內心的平靜。而我跟任何人一樣，也免不了在 X 或社群媒體上「末日式滑手機」，為那些我根本無能為力的事情動氣。

**Naval:** Like, do I want to be fighting those battles in my mind when I literally cannot do anything about it? So if you find yourself looping on a problem — you're watching the news too much and getting caught up in a problem you can't do anything about — you have to step away from that.
像是，我真的想在腦子裡打那些仗嗎？當我實際上根本什麼都做不了的時候？所以如果你發現自己在某個問題上鬼打牆——你新聞看太多，陷進了一個你無能為力的問題裡——你必須從那裡抽身。

**Naval:** And modern media is a delivery mechanism for mimetic viruses. 100 years ago, 500 years ago, if something wasn't happening in your immediate vicinity, you wouldn't hear about it. It wouldn't be a problem for you.
而現代媒體是一套「迷因病毒」的傳播機制。一百年前、五百年前，如果某件事不是發生在你近旁，你根本不會聽說。它就不會是你的問題。

**Naval:** But now every single one of the world's problems has turned into a mimetic virus, which is going into the battlefield of the news and trying to infect your mind in real time. So that you become obsessed with the war in Ukraine, which is really far away, or you get obsessed with climate change, or AI doom, or whatever.
但現在，世界上每一個問題都變成了一種迷因病毒，衝進「新聞」這個戰場，試圖即時感染你的心智。好讓你變得執迷於遠在天邊的烏克蘭戰爭，或執迷於氣候變遷、AI 末日，或隨便什麼東西。

**Naval:** And there's nothing as riveting as the old religion: the world is ending, the world is ending, pay attention, the world is ending. And if you don't—
而沒有什麼比那個古老的宗教更扣人心弦了：世界要毀滅了，世界要毀滅了，注意聽好，世界要毀滅了。而如果你不——

**主持人:** Cassandra complex at global scale.
全球規模的「卡珊德拉情結」。

**Naval:** Cassandra complex at global scale.
全球規模的卡珊德拉情結。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| addicted | /əˋdɪktɪd/ | adj. | 上癮的、沉迷的 |
| indifference | /ɪnˋdɪfərəns/ | n. | 漠然、無動於衷 |
| mimetic | /mɪˋmɛtɪk/ | adj. | 模仿的、迷因（傳染）性的 |
| vicinity | /vəˋsɪnətɪ/ | n. | 附近、鄰近地帶 |
| riveting | /ˋrɪvɪtɪŋ/ | adj. | 扣人心弦的、令人目不轉睛的 |
| quip | /kwɪp/ | n. | 妙語、俏皮的格言 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`so much so that...`**：（程度）到這種地步，以至於⋯⋯。
- **`doom-surfing / doom-scrolling`**：末日式滑手機——不斷刷負面新聞而停不下來。
- **`get worked up about`**：為某事情緒激動、動氣。
- **`loop on a problem`**：在一個問題上鬼打牆、反覆糾結。
- **`Cassandra complex`**：卡珊德拉情結——不停預言災難卻無人採信（或無濟於事）的心態。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`I'm as guilty as anybody of doom-surfing`** — `as ... as anybody`（跟任何人一樣⋯⋯）自嘲式強調；`guilty of + N/Ving` 表「犯了⋯⋯的毛病」。
- **`So that you become obsessed with...`** — `so that` 引導目的／結果子句，此處連續用 `or you get obsessed with...` 排比，堆疊多個被感染的對象。
- **`there's nothing as riveting as the old religion`** — `nothing as ... as ...`（沒有什麼像⋯⋯一樣⋯⋯）表最高級語氣。

---

## 31. 迷因病毒感染大眾：先整理好自己的家

### 逐句對照

**Naval:** Well, and I would argue that large percentages of the population are essentially just infected with these mimetic viruses that have taken over their brain and are causing them to do incredible gyration about things that probably aren't even true, or are greatly exaggerated. But even to the extent they are true, they're things that that person can do nothing about. And they should put their own house in order first.
嗯，而且我會主張，人口中有很大比例的人，基本上就是被這些迷因病毒感染了。這些病毒佔據了他們的大腦，害他們為那些「可能根本不是真的、或被大幅誇大的事」而天翻地覆地折騰。但就算那些事有幾分是真的，也都是那個人無能為力的事。他們應該先把自己的家整頓好。

**Naval:** So another little line I have for myself is: "Your family is broken, but you're going to fix the world?" People are running out there to try and fix the world when their own lives are a mess.
所以我留給自己的另一句小話是：「你自己的家都破碎了，你卻要去拯救世界？」大家跑到外頭想拯救世界，自己的人生卻是一團亂。

**主持人:** Oh my god.
天啊。

**Naval:** Right? And I think it defies credibility if you can't fix your own life first. I'm not going to take you seriously if you can't fix your own life. Like all these philosophers who seem like people you'd emulate, and so smart, or these brilliant celebrities — and they go off and commit suicide. Well, you just kind of invalidated your whole way of life.
對吧？我認為，如果你連自己的人生都修不好，那就令人難以置信、難以信服。如果你連自己的人生都搞不定，我不會把你當回事。就像那些哲學家，看起來像是你會想效法的人、聰明絕頂，或那些才華洋溢的名人——結果他們卻跑去自殺了。那你等於是親手推翻了自己整套的人生哲學。

**Naval:** It's like that line in No Country for Old Men, where the killer is waiting for the protagonist, and the protagonist shows up, and the killer says, "Well, if your set of rules brought you here, then what good are your rules?" It didn't work.
就像《險路勿近》裡那句台詞，殺手在那裡等著主角，主角現身後，殺手說：「這個嘛，如果是你那套規則把你帶到這裡的，那你的規則又有什麼用？」它行不通。

**Naval:** I am holistically selfish, in that I want to be objectively successful in everything I set out to want.
我是整體性地自私，意思是我想在每一件我立志想要的事情上，都取得客觀上的成功。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| gyration | /dʒaɪˋreʃən/ | n. | 劇烈翻攪、天翻地覆的折騰 |
| exaggerated | /ɪgˋzædʒəˏretɪd/ | adj. | 誇大的 |
| credibility | /ˏkrɛdəˋbɪlətɪ/ | n. | 可信度、說服力 |
| emulate | /ˋɛmjəˏlet/ | v. | 效法、仿效 |
| invalidate | /ɪnˋvæləˏdet/ | v. | 使失效、推翻（論點/正當性） |
| protagonist | /proˋtægənɪst/ | n. | 主角 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`put your own house in order`**：先把自己的家（事）整頓好——處理好自己的問題再管別人。
- **`defies credibility`**：令人難以置信、難以取信於人。
- **`take you seriously`**：把你當一回事、認真看待你。
- **`what good are your rules?`**：「你的規則又有什麼用？」——`what good is/are...?` 表反問「有何用處」。
- **`in that...`**：「就⋯⋯這一點而言」，用來解釋前述說法的具體含義。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`it defies credibility if you can't fix your own life first`** — `if` 條件子句後置，主句在前，加強「先修好自己」的前提。
- **`No Country for Old Men`** — 電影片名《險路勿近》；`No country for old men` 字面指「不適合老人生存的國度」。
- **`if your set of rules brought you here, then what good are your rules?`** — 條件句 + 反問句組合，用假設推導出對「規則本身」的質疑。

---

## 32. 別甘於平庸：智力的真正考驗是想要對的東西

### 逐句對照

**Naval:** Mhm. Yeah. You have one life. Don't settle for mediocrity.
嗯，對。你只有一次人生，別甘於平庸。

**主持人:** Don't settle for mediocrity.
別甘於平庸。

**Naval:** And I think — people debate intelligence, for example. We talk about IQ tests and all that, but I think the only true test of intelligence is if you get what you want out of life. And there are two parts to that. One is getting what you want — so, knowing how to get it. And the second is wanting the right things — knowing what to want in the first place.
而我認為——比方說，大家老在爭論智力這回事。我們談 IQ 測驗那一套，但我認為智力唯一真正的考驗，是你能不能從人生中得到你想要的。這裡面有兩個部分。一是得到你想要的——也就是知道怎麼得到它。二是想要對的東西——一開始就知道該想要什麼。

**Naval:** I could want to be a 6'8" basketball player, and I'm not going to get that. So it's wanting the wrong thing.
我可以想當一個六呎八吋高的籃球員，但我就是不會得到那個。所以那是想要了錯的東西。

**主持人:** That's wanting something you can't get.
那是想要一個你得不到的東西。

**Naval:** It's also wanting something that you don't want.
也可能是想要一個你其實並不想要的東西。

**主持人:** Yeah.
對。

**Naval:** Wanting something that's a booby prize. There are plenty of booby prizes out there too.
想要一個「安慰獎」等級的東西。外頭這種安慰獎也多得是。

**主持人:** I haven't heard that word in about 20 years.
這個詞我大概二十年沒聽過了。

**Naval:** Yeah. Prizes that are just not worth having, or that create their own problems.
對。那種根本不值得擁有、或者本身就會製造麻煩的獎品。

**主持人:** Well, if you're not careful, you can end up in a place in life not only that you don't want to be, but one that you didn't even mean to get to.
是啊，如果你不小心，你可能會落到人生中一個你不只不想待、甚至根本沒打算走到的地方。

**Naval:** That's if you're kind of proceeding unconsciously. But usually I think people end up there because they're going on autopilot with societal expectations or other people's expectations. Or out of guilt, or out of mimetic desire. Peter Thiel has this whole thing from René Girard about how mimetic desires are picked up from other people.
那是因為你有點在無意識地往前走。但我認為，人們通常會落到那裡，是因為他們順著社會期待或別人的期待在「自動駕駛」。或者是出於罪惡感，或出於「模仿性慾望」。Peter Thiel 有一整套源自 René Girard 的論述，講的就是模仿性慾望是怎麼從別人身上撿來的。

**Naval:** And some of those are automatically baked into society, like: go to law school, go to med school, go to business school. Or they might come from watching what your friends are doing, what the other monkeys are doing. Or it might just be what your parents' expectations are. It might be guilt. Guilt is just society's voice speaking in your head — socially programmed, so you'll be a good little monkey and do things that are good for the tribe.
而其中有些慾望是自動烘進社會裡的，像是：去念法學院、去念醫學院、去念商學院。或者它們可能來自你觀察朋友在做什麼、其他猴子在做什麼。又或者，它可能就只是你父母的期待。它也可能是罪惡感。罪惡感不過是社會的聲音在你腦中說話——你被社會編了程，好讓你當一隻乖巧的小猴子，去做那些對部落有利的事。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| settle for | /ˋsɛtl̩ fɔr/ | phr. | 將就、勉強接受（次好的） |
| mediocrity | /ˏmidɪˋɑkrətɪ/ | n. | 平庸、平凡 |
| booby prize | /ˋbubɪ praɪz/ | n. | 安慰獎、末名獎（帶調侃） |
| autopilot | /ˋɔtoˏpaɪlət/ | n. | 自動駕駛（比喻無意識行事） |
| mimetic desire | /mɪˋmɛtɪk dɪˋzaɪr/ | phr. | 模仿性慾望（欲望是從他人習得的） |
| baked into | /bekt ˋɪntu/ | phr. | 內建於、根植於 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`settle for mediocrity`**：甘於平庸、將就於平凡。
- **`in the first place`**：一開始、根本上（常帶「本來就該⋯⋯」語氣）。
- **`go on autopilot`**：進入自動駕駛模式，指不假思索、隨慣性行事。
- **`baked into society`**：像烘進蛋糕一樣「內建」在社會裡，難以察覺卻無所不在。
- **`a good little monkey`**：乖巧的小猴子——調侃人盲從群體、順從社會編程。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`the only true test of intelligence is if you get what you want out of life`** — `is if...` 口語中以 if 子句作主詞補語，等同 `is whether...`。
- **`not only ... but one that you didn't even mean to get to`** — `not only ... but (also) ...` 遞進，`one` 代替 `a place`，避免重複。
- **`Guilt is just society's voice speaking in your head.`** — `voice + speaking`（現在分詞後位修飾）表「正在說話的聲音」，把抽象的罪惡感擬人化。

---

## 33. 為自己思考：長週期的決定卻只花極短時間決定

### 逐句對照

**Naval:** But I think the best outcomes come when you think it through for yourself and decide for yourself. And I don't think people spend enough time deciding.
但我認為，最好的結果來自你自己把事情想透、自己做決定。而我覺得大家花在做決定上的時間根本不夠。

**Naval:** For example, we run on these four-year cycles. In Silicon Valley, you go join a startup, you vest your stock over four years. That's the standard. In college, you go for four years. High school, you go for four years.
舉例來說，我們的人生是以這種四年為週期在運轉。在矽谷，你加入一家新創，股票分四年授予（vest），這是標準做法。念大學，四年；念高中，也是四年。

**Naval:** Some things take longer. You have children, they hit puberty nine years later. That's like a nine-year cycle until that relationship changes. But we're used to these fairly long, multi-year cycles in which we are committed to things.
有些事週期更長。你生了小孩，九年後他們進入青春期，那大概是個九年的週期，直到那段關係開始改變。但我們早已習慣這些相當長、動輒好幾年、必須全心投入的週期。

**Naval:** You go to law school, four or five year cycle. You go be a lawyer, 40-year cycle. These are very long cycles. The amount of time we spend deciding what to do and who to do it with, very short, very very short.
你去念法學院，是個四五年的週期；你去當律師，是個四十年的週期。這些都是非常長的週期。可是我們花在「決定要做什麼、要和誰一起做」上面的時間，卻非常短，非常非常短。

**Naval:** We spend three months, one month deciding on a job where we're going to be for ten years or five years. And because a lot of discovery is path dependent, where the next thing you find on the path depends on where you were on the previous path, you sort of start going down this vector that is a very long distance.
我們花三個月、甚至一個月，就決定了一份會待上五年或十年的工作。而且因為很多探索是「路徑依賴」的——你在路上找到的下一樣東西，取決於你先前站在路的哪個位置——於是你就這樣沿著一個延伸得非常遠的方向一路走下去。

**Naval:** People decide frivolously which city to live in, and that's going to decide who their friends are, what their jobs are, their opportunity, their weather, their food supply, their air supply, quality of life. It's such an important decision, but people spend so little time thinking it through.
人們很草率地決定要住在哪座城市，而這將決定他們的朋友是誰、工作是什麼、機會、天氣、食物來源、空氣品質、生活品質。這是如此重要的決定，人們卻花這麼少的時間把它想清楚。

**Naval:** I would argue that if you're making a four-year decision, spend a year thinking it through. Like really thinking it through.
我會主張：如果你在做一個關乎四年的決定，就花一年好好把它想透，真的認真地想透。

**主持人:** 25% of the time.
花上四分之一的時間。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| vest | /vɛst/ | v. | （股票、權益）分期授予、歸屬 |
| puberty | /ˋpjubɚtɪ/ | n. | 青春期 |
| path dependent | /pæθ dɪˋpɛndənt/ | adj. | 路徑依賴的 |
| frivolously | /ˋfrɪvələslɪ/ | adv. | 輕率地、不當回事地 |
| vector | /ˋvɛktɚ/ | n. | 方向、向量 |
| commit (to) | /kəˋmɪt/ | v. | 投入、承諾 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`think it through`**：把一件事「從頭到尾想透、想清楚」，強調通盤思考而非草率決定。
- **`run on ... cycles`**：「以⋯⋯週期在運轉」，把人生比喻成一個個時間循環。
- **`go down this vector`**：口語化說法，「沿著這個方向一路走下去」。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`the best outcomes come when you think it through`** — `when` 引導時間副詞子句，描述「在⋯⋯情況下」最好的結果才會出現。
- **`the next thing you find on the path depends on where you were`** — 主詞 `the next thing (that) you find` 內含省略關係代名詞的形容詞子句；`depends on` 後接名詞子句 `where you were`。
- **`if you're making a four-year decision, spend a year thinking it through.`** — `if` 條件句 + 祈使句主句；`spend + 時間 + Ving` 表「花時間做某事」。
