## 34. 祕書定理：以迭代次數（非時間）為準，快進快出

### 逐句對照

**Naval:** Yeah, exactly. There's the secretary theorem. I don't know if you know that one.
對，正是如此。有個「祕書定理」（secretary theorem），不知道你聽過沒有。

**主持人:** Computer science. After you've done this many people, pick the best one of the next however many.
電腦科學裡的。看過這麼多人之後，就在接下來的那些人裡挑出最好的一個。

**Naval:** That's right. The secretary theorem is this computer science professor is trying to figure out how much time he should spend interviewing secretaries and then how long to keep the secretary. So let's say he's going to have a secretary for ten years. Does he keep searching for one year, two years, three years, one month, two months? What is the optimal time?
沒錯。祕書定理講的是：有位電腦科學教授想搞清楚，他該花多少時間面試祕書，以及聘用一位祕書要留多久。假設他打算聘一位祕書十年，那他該持續物色一年、兩年、三年，還是一個月、兩個月？最佳的時間點是什麼？

**Naval:** And it turns out that the optimal time is somewhere around a third. About a third of the way through, you take the best person you've worked with and try to find someone that good or better. So by the time you've gotten about a third of the way through, you have seen enough that you now have a sense of what the bar is. And then anybody who meets or exceeds that bar is good enough.
結果發現，最佳時間點大約落在三分之一處。走到大約三分之一的時候，你就把至今合作過最好的那個人當作標準，去找一個同樣好或更好的人。這樣一來，等你走完大約三分之一時，你已經看得夠多，對「標準」在哪裡有了感覺。之後任何達到或超過那條標準的人，就夠好了。

**Naval:** And this applies to dating, this applies to jobs and careers, this applies generally. But the interesting thing about the secretary theorem is that it's actually not time based. It's not based on one-third of the time. It's iteration based.
這適用於約會，適用於工作與職涯，普遍都適用。但祕書定理有趣的地方在於：它其實不是以時間為基準，不是「三分之一的時間」，而是以「迭代次數」為基準。

**主持人:** The number of candidates, the number of shots you took on goal.
是候選人的數量，是你朝球門射門的次數。

**Naval:** That's right. So you want to have lots and lots of iterations. So that means that you need to bail out quickly and you need to be decisive quickly.
沒錯。所以你會希望有非常非常多次的迭代。這意味著你必須很快抽身、很快做出決斷。

**主持人:** That's right. You need to take opportunities quickly and bail out quickly.
沒錯。你得快快抓住機會，也快快抽身。

**Naval:** Correct. Like if you go back and look through failed relationships, probably the biggest regret will be staying in the relationship after you knew it was over.
正是。像你回頭去檢視那些失敗的感情，最大的後悔大概就是：明明知道它已經結束了，卻還繼續留在那段關係裡。

**主持人:** Exactly. You should have left sooner.
沒錯。你早該更早離開。

**Naval:** The moment you knew it wasn't going to work out, you should have moved on. So in that sense, I think Malcolm Gladwell popularized this idea of 10,000 hours to mastery. I would say it's actually 10,000 iterations to mastery. It's not actually 10,000, it's some unknown number. But it's about the number of iterations that drives a learning curve.
在你知道它行不通的那一刻，你就該往前走了。從這個角度說，我想葛拉威爾（Malcolm Gladwell）讓「一萬小時達到精通」這個概念廣為人知。我會說，其實是「一萬次迭代」才能精通。當然不是真的一萬，是某個未知的數字，但重點在於推動學習曲線的是迭代次數。

**Naval:** And iteration is not repetition. Repetition is a different thing. Repeating is doing the same thing over and over. Iteration is modifying it with a learning and then doing another version of it. So that's error correction. So if you get 10,000 error corrections in anything, you will be an expert at it.
而且迭代不等於重複。重複是另一回事。重複是把同一件事一遍又一遍地做。迭代則是根據所學把它做調整，然後再做出另一個版本，這就是「錯誤修正」。所以只要你在任何事情上累積了一萬次的錯誤修正，你就會成為那件事的專家。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| theorem | /ˋθiərəm/ | n. | 定理 |
| optimal | /ˋɑptəməl/ | adj. | 最佳的、最適的 |
| iteration | /ˏɪtəˋreʃən/ | n. | 迭代、反覆修正 |
| decisive | /dɪˋsaɪsɪv/ | adj. | 果斷的 |
| repetition | /ˏrɛpɪˋtɪʃən/ | n. | 重複 |
| mastery | /ˋmæstərɪ/ | n. | 精通、掌握 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`bail out`**：口語「抽身、退出、及時脫身」，原指跳傘逃生。
- **`shots you took on goal`**：足球術語「射門次數」，比喻「你嘗試的次數」。
- **`move your chips to the center of the table`** 的近義概念 `move on`：這裡指「往前走、放下、繼續前進」。
- **`a third of the way through`**：「走到（過程的）三分之一處」，`... of the way through` 是很道地的進度說法。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`it turns out that the optimal time is somewhere around a third.`** — `it turns out that ...` 表「結果發現⋯⋯」，`it` 為虛主詞。
- **`anybody who meets or exceeds that bar is good enough.`** — `who` 引導形容詞子句修飾 `anybody`；主詞是單數概念故動詞用 `is`。
- **`you should have moved on.`** — `should have + p.p.` 表「（過去）早該做卻沒做」的後悔語氣。

---

## 35. 避免犬儒與悲觀：天生悲觀，但現代上檔非線性

### 逐句對照

**主持人:** Don't partner with cynics and pessimists. You mentioned there about the people who've got a nightmare going on at home and are trying to fix the world. But a lot of the time that cynicism and pessimism we find in ourselves.
別和犬儒與悲觀的人合夥。你剛剛提到那些家裡一團糟、卻想著要修好整個世界的人。但很多時候，那份犬儒與悲觀，是我們在自己身上發現的。

**主持人:** We see the world, whether it's because we've imbibed what the news or the negative people around us have said, or it's a bit more endogenous than that. It's just sort of in us. It's the way that we see the world. How can people avoid cynicism and pessimism within themselves?
我們看世界的方式，可能是因為我們吸收了新聞、或身邊那些負面的人所說的話，也可能比這更「內生」一點——它就是內建在我們裡面，是我們看世界的方式。人要怎麼避免自己心裡的犬儒與悲觀？

**Naval:** Yeah, cynicism and pessimism is a tough one. We're naturally hardwired for it. Again, I go back to evolution. I'm sorry to keep harping on evolution, but within biology there's very few good explanatory theories, and the theory of evolution by natural selection is probably the best one.
是啊，犬儒與悲觀是個難題。我們天生就被寫死成這樣。我又要回到演化了。抱歉一直嘮叨演化，但在生物學裡，真正好的解釋性理論非常少，而「天擇的演化論」大概是其中最好的一個。

**Naval:** So if you can't explain something about life or psychology or human nature through evolution, then you probably don't have a good theory for it. And I would say that pessimism is another one that comes out of this.
所以如果你沒辦法用演化來解釋生命、心理或人性的某件事，那你大概就還沒有一個好理論。而我會說，悲觀正是從這裡衍生出來的另一個例子。

**Naval:** In the natural environment, you're hardwired to be pessimistic. Because let's say I see something rustling in the woods. If I move towards it and it turns out to be food and prey, then good, I get to eat one meal. But if it turns out to be a predator, I get eaten, and that's the end of that. So we are hardwired to avoid ruin and just dying.
在自然環境裡，你被寫死成傾向悲觀。假設我看到樹林裡有東西在窸窣作響：如果我朝它走過去，結果是食物、是獵物，那太好了，我可以吃上一餐；但如果結果是掠食者，我就被吃掉了，然後一切就結束了。所以我們被寫死成要避免「毀滅」、避免「就這麼死掉」。

**Naval:** So we are naturally hardwired to be pessimists, but modern society is very different. Despite whatever problems you may have with modern society, it is far, far safer than living in the jungle and just trying to survive. And the opportunities on the upside are nonlinear.
所以我們天生被設定成悲觀者，但現代社會非常不一樣。不管你對現代社會有什麼不滿，它都遠遠比住在叢林裡、只求活下去要安全得多。而且在「上檔」（好的一面）的機會是非線性的。

**Naval:** For example, when you're investing, if you short a stock, the most money you can make is 2x. If the stock goes to zero, you double your money. But if the stock is the next Nvidia and it goes 100x or 1,000x, you make a lot of money. So upside, because of leverage, is nearly unlimited.
舉例來說，投資時如果你放空一檔股票，你最多能賺兩倍：股價跌到零，你的錢翻倍。但如果那檔股票是下一個 Nvidia，漲了一百倍、一千倍，你就賺翻了。所以上檔——因為有槓桿——幾乎是無限大的。

**Naval:** Also in modern society, because there's so many different people you can interact with, if you go on a date and it fails, there are infinite more people to go on a date with. In a tribal system, there might have been 20 people, and you can't even get through all of them. So modern society is far more forgiving of failure.
另外在現代社會，因為你能互動的人這麼多，如果你去約會、結果失敗了，還有無限多的人可以再約。在部落系統裡可能只有二十個人，你甚至還沒約完全部。所以現代社會對失敗的容忍度高得多。

**Naval:** And you just have to neocortically realize and override that. You have to realize that you're much more running a search function to find the thing that'll work. And then that one thing will pay off in massive compounding. Once you find your mate for the rest of your life, then you can compound in that relationship. It's okay if you had 50 failed dates in between.
你只需要動用新皮質（neocortex）去意識到、去覆寫掉那個本能。你得明白：你更像是在跑一個「搜尋函式」，去找到那個行得通的東西。而一旦找到，那一樣東西就會以龐大的複利回報你。一旦你找到共度餘生的伴侶，你就能在那段關係裡複利累積。中間就算有五十次失敗的約會，也沒關係。

**Naval:** The same way, once you find the one business you're meant to plow into, it'll compound returns. It's okay if you had 50 small failed ventures or 50 small failed job interviews. The number of failures doesn't matter. And so there's no point in being a pessimist. You want to be an optimist.
同樣地，一旦你找到那門你註定要投入的事業，它就會產生複利報酬。中間就算有五十次小小的失敗創業、或五十次失敗的面試，也沒關係。失敗的次數不重要。所以當個悲觀者毫無意義，你該當個樂觀者。

**Naval:** But I would say you want to be skeptical about specific things. Every specific opportunity is probably a fail. But you want to be optimistic in the general. In the general, you want to be like, something in here is going to work out.
不過我會說，你要對「具體的事情」抱持懷疑。每一個具體的機會，大概都會失敗。但你要在「大方向上」保持樂觀。在大方向上，你要抱著「這裡面總會有某樣東西成功」的心態。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| cynicism | /ˋsɪnɪˏsɪzəm/ | n. | 犬儒、憤世嫉俗 |
| hardwired | /ˋhɑrdˏwaɪrd/ | adj. | （天生）內建的、寫死的 |
| endogenous | /ɛnˋdɑdʒənəs/ | adj. | 內生的、由內而生的 |
| predator | /ˋprɛdətɚ/ | n. | 掠食者 |
| nonlinear | /nɑnˋlɪnɪɚ/ | adj. | 非線性的 |
| leverage | /ˋlɛvərɪdʒ/ | n. | 槓桿 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`harp on ...`**：「反覆嘮叨、老是講同一件事」，常帶點自嘲或不耐。
- **`forgiving of failure`**：「對失敗寬容」，`forgiving` 當形容詞形容「環境／制度容錯度高」。
- **`plow into ...`**：口語「一頭栽進、全力投入」（某事業、某項目）。
- **`there's no point in ...`**：「做⋯⋯毫無意義、沒必要」。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`we're naturally hardwired for it.`** — 被動語態 `be hardwired for/to`，表「天生被設定成⋯⋯」。
- **`the most money you can make is 2x.`** — 最高級名詞片語 `the most money (that) you can make` 內含省略關係代名詞的形容詞子句。
- **`it's okay if you had 50 failed dates in between.`** — `it's okay if ...` 口語讓步句型，表「就算⋯⋯也沒關係」。

---

## 36. 大方向樂觀、細節懷疑：槓鈴策略、標籤會自我設限

### 逐句對照

**主持人:** How do you navigate that tension?
你怎麼在那種張力之間拿捏？

**Naval:** I mean, exactly as I said, I'm optimistic in the general that if something fails right now, then—this is a little woo-woo, but—it wasn't meant to be. It was a learning experience. It was an iteration. As long as I learned something from it, then it's a win. If I didn't learn from it, then it's a loss.
就像我說的，我在大方向上是樂觀的：如果某件事現在失敗了，那麼——這說法有點玄——它本來就註定不成。它是一次學習經驗，一次迭代。只要我從中學到了東西，那就是贏；如果我沒學到，那才是輸。

**Naval:** But as long as you're learning and you keep iterating fast and cutting your losses quickly, then when you find the right thing, you have to be optimistic and compound into it. So you don't want to jump into the first thing. And you don't want to marry the first person you date necessarily, unless you got very lucky.
但只要你持續在學、持續快速迭代、快速停損，那麼當你找到對的那個東西時，你就必須樂觀起來、複利投入。所以你不會想一頭栽進第一個出現的東西，也不見得會嫁給你約會的第一個人——除非你運氣非常好。

**Naval:** But you want to investigate and explore very, very quickly until you find the match. And then you have to be willing to go all in. You have to be willing to move your chips to the center of the table. So both those approaches are required.
但你會想非常非常快速地調查、探索，直到找到那個對的匹配。然後你必須願意全押，必須願意把籌碼推到桌子中央。所以這兩種做法都是必要的。

**Naval:** So it's a barbell strategy. It's sort of black or it's white. And most people are sort of stuck in this gray bit. And I'm like half in, but I kind of don't really know if I am. I also think labels like pessimist, optimist, cynic, introvert, extrovert—these are very self-limiting. Humans are very dynamic.
所以這是一種「槓鈴策略」（barbell strategy）：不是黑就是白。而大多數人卡在中間那塊灰色地帶——「我算半投入吧，但我也不太確定自己算不算」。我還認為，像悲觀者、樂觀者、犬儒、內向、外向這些標籤，都非常會自我設限。人是非常動態的。

**Naval:** There are times when you feel like being introverted. There are times when you feel like being extroverted. There are contexts in which you'll be pessimistic. There are contexts in which you'll be optimistic. Leave all those labels alone. It's better just to look at the problem at hand. Look at reality the way it is.
有時候你想當個內向的人，有時候你想當個外向的人。在某些情境下你會悲觀，在某些情境下你會樂觀。別去碰那些標籤。更好的做法是直接看眼前的問題，如實地看待現實。

**Naval:** Try to take yourself out of the equation in a sense. Obviously you're involved, but motivated reasoning is the worst kind of reasoning. You're not going to find truth through highly motivated reasoning. You have to be objective. And objective means trying to take yourself out of it, or at least your personality out of it, as much as possible.
在某種意義上，試著把你自己從方程式裡拿掉。當然你身處其中，但「動機性推理」（motivated reasoning）是最糟糕的推理。你不可能靠高度帶有動機的推理找到真相。你必須客觀，而客觀意味著盡可能把你自己、至少把你的個性從中抽離出來。

**主持人:** And so to the extent you run with this thick identity and personality, it's going to cloud your judgment. It's going to try and lock you into the past.
所以，你越是帶著這種厚重的身分認同與個性去行動，它就越會蒙蔽你的判斷，越會試圖把你鎖進過去。

**Naval:** If you say, "I'm a depressed, unhappy person," yeah, you're going to be unhappy. That's a way of locking yourself into your past. Even saying, "I have trauma, I have PTSD"—yeah, you feel something, there are memories, there are flashes, there are occasional bad feelings. But don't define yourself by it, because then you'll lock it into your identity and you're just going to loop on it.
如果你說「我是個憂鬱、不快樂的人」，那沒錯，你就會不快樂。那是一種把自己鎖進過去的方式。就連說「我有創傷、我有創傷後壓力症候群（PTSD）」——沒錯，你確實感覺到了什麼，有記憶、有閃回、偶爾有壞情緒——但別用它來定義你自己，因為那樣你會把它鎖進你的身分認同，然後就一直在上面打轉。

**Naval:** It's better to stay flexible, because reality is always changing and you have to be able to adapt to it. Adaptation is also intelligence. Adaptation is survival. Adaptation is kind of how you're here. You're here because you're an adapter and your ancestors were adapters. So to adapt, you will be able to see things clearly. And if you're seeing them through your own identity, it's going to cloud your judgment.
保持彈性比較好，因為現實一直在變，而你必須有能力去適應它。適應也是智慧，適應就是生存。適應在某種程度上就是你為什麼能站在這裡——你之所以存在，是因為你是個適應者，你的祖先也都是適應者。所以，要適應，你就得看清事情；而如果你是透過自己的身分認同去看它們，它就會蒙蔽你的判斷。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| barbell strategy | /ˋbɑrˏbɛl ˋstrætədʒɪ/ | n. | 槓鈴策略（兩極押注、避開中間） |
| self-limiting | /ˏsɛlfˋlɪmɪtɪŋ/ | adj. | 自我設限的 |
| motivated reasoning | /ˋmotəˏvetɪd ˋriznɪŋ/ | n. | 動機性推理（先有結論再找理由） |
| objective | /əbˋdʒɛktɪv/ | adj. | 客觀的 |
| adaptation | /ˏædæpˋteʃən/ | n. | 適應 |
| cloud | /klaʊd/ | v. | 蒙蔽、使模糊 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`woo-woo`**：口語形容詞，指「玄玄的、偏靈性／超自然、聽起來不太科學的」。
- **`go all in` / `move your chips to the center of the table`**：撲克術語「全押、孤注一擲」，比喻全力投入。
- **`take yourself out of the equation`**：「把自己從局裡抽離」，指做判斷時排除私心。
- **`loop on it`**：口語「在某事上反覆打轉、跳針」。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`as long as I learned something from it, then it's a win.`** — `as long as` 引導條件句，表「只要⋯⋯就⋯⋯」。
- **`the way it is`**：`the way (that) it is` 表「照它本來的樣子」，`the way` 後接子句是道地口語結構。
- **`to the extent you run with this thick identity ...`** — `to the extent (that) ...` 表「到⋯⋯的程度、就⋯⋯而言」。

---

## 37. 幸福是什麼：安於當下、最快樂時多在「無所事事」、極樂機器

### 逐句對照

**主持人:** Moving on to thinking about happiness—obviously a topic of yours.
接著來談談幸福，這顯然是你關注的主題之一。

**Naval:** It's honestly the one that I feel least qualified to talk about.
老實說，這是我覺得自己最沒資格談的主題。

**主持人:** Is it like a guy that's got long arms teaching you how to bench press, or a dude that's really tall teaching you how to deadlift? Someone that feels like they came from behind the eight ball.
是不是像手臂很長的人教你臥推、或個子很高的人教你硬舉？一個感覺自己一開始就處於劣勢的人。

**Naval:** Yeah. You're asking a crazy person about their thoughts. So, just thought it through.
對啊，你這是在問一個瘋子他的想法。所以，就當我把它想過一遍吧。

**主持人:** Is happiness still more about peace than it is about joy?
幸福是不是仍然比較關乎「平靜」，而不是「喜悅」？

**Naval:** It's just one of those overloaded words that means different things to different people. So I'm not even sure we're communicating in the same language.
它就是那種被塞太多意思的字，對不同的人有不同的意思。所以我甚至不確定我們講的是不是同一種語言。

**主持人:** What is happiness?
幸福到底是什麼？

**Naval:** I think it's just basically being okay with where you are. Not wanting things to be different than the way they are. Not having the sense that anything is missing in this moment. Needing something to change—your current positive situation being contingent on an adjustment, on getting something from the outside world.
我想它基本上就是「安於你所在之處」。不希望事情變得跟現在不一樣，不覺得此刻有任何東西是缺少的。反過來，需要某樣東西改變、你當下的正向狀態得取決於某種調整、取決於從外在世界得到什麼——那就不是幸福。

**Naval:** Ironically, I think most people, if you were to ask them when they were happiest for a sustained period of time—not for a brief moment, because pleasure can override happiness and create this illusion of happiness—but if you ask people when they were happy for a sustained period, they were probably doing some variation of nothing.
諷刺的是，我覺得大多數人，如果你問他們「什麼時候持續地最快樂」——不是短暫的片刻，因為愉悅（pleasure）會蓋過幸福，製造出一種幸福的假象——但如果你問他們什麼時候持續地快樂，他們當時大概都在做某種形式的「無所事事」。

**主持人:** That's interesting, because in the chase is this sort of lack, this contingency.
這很有意思，因為在「追逐」之中，就存在著一種匱乏、一種「有條件性」。

**Naval:** That's right. But then you get bored. If you just sit around all the time, you get bored. So you want adventure, you want surprise. There's a funny thought experiment of the bliss machine. Suppose I could drill a hole in your head and put an electrode in—they did this with monkeys—and I put a wire in there and stimulate just the right part of your brain and put you in bliss, and you'll just be in bliss. Would you want that? Would that be nice?
沒錯。但接著你會無聊。如果你整天就只是閒坐著，你會無聊。所以你會想要冒險，想要驚喜。有個很有趣的思想實驗叫「極樂機器」（bliss machine）：假設我可以在你頭上鑽個洞，放進一根電極——他們真的對猴子做過——我在裡面接一條線，刺激你大腦剛剛好的那個部位，讓你進入極樂，你就一直處在極樂裡。你會想要那樣嗎？那樣好嗎？

**主持人:** For how long? Do it and I'll tell you.
持續多久？你先弄，我再告訴你。

**Naval:** Right. So most people will say, "Well, I don't want that. I want meaning, I don't want just bliss, I want meaning." And you're like, "Okay, I'll put an electrode in there and I'll give you meaning. How about that?" And if you run this thought experiment long enough, I think most people realize what I actually want is surprise. I want the world to surprise me, and I want to wrestle with it in ways that are somewhat predictable but somewhat not. And you kind of end up back where you started.
對。大多數人會說：「我才不要那樣，我要意義，我不要只有極樂，我要意義。」然後你說：「好啊，那我放個電極進去，給你意義，這樣如何？」而如果你把這個思想實驗跑得夠久，我想大多數人會意識到，自己真正想要的其實是「驚喜」。我要世界給我驚喜，我要去和它角力，在某種程度上可預測、又某種程度上不可預測。於是你等於又繞回了原點。

**Naval:** For some people, pure happiness is the ultimate goal—they want to just be blissfully happy wherever, whenever. But most people would say, "Well, I'm here in this world, I'm here in this life, I don't understand it or why, but I want to be engaged. I want to be surprised. I want to do things. I want to accomplish things. I want to want things and then get them." That's kind of the whole game that we're all playing here.
對某些人來說，純粹的幸福就是終極目標——他們只想無論何時何地都幸福無比。但大多數人會說：「嗯，我身處這個世界、這段人生，我不懂它、也不懂為什麼，但我想要投入、想要被驚喜到、想要去做事、想要成就一些事。我想要『渴望某樣東西、然後得到它』。」這差不多就是我們所有人正在玩的整場遊戲。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| qualified | /ˋkwɑləˏfaɪd/ | adj. | 有資格的、夠格的 |
| overloaded | /ˏovɚˋlodɪd/ | adj. | 被塞太多（意思）的、超載的 |
| contingent (on) | /kənˋtɪndʒənt/ | adj. | 取決於⋯⋯的、視情況而定的 |
| bliss | /blɪs/ | n. | 極樂、極致的幸福 |
| electrode | /ɪˋlɛktrod/ | n. | 電極 |
| wrestle (with) | /ˋrɛsl̩/ | v. | 與⋯⋯角力、搏鬥 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`came from behind the eight ball`**：源自撞球，指「一開始就處於劣勢、身陷不利處境」。
- **`being okay with ...`**：「對⋯⋯感到安然、接受、沒問題」。
- **`some variation of nothing`**：妙語，「某種形式的無所事事」。
- **`end up back where you started`**：「兜了一圈又回到原點」。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`the one that I feel least qualified to talk about.`** — 最高級 `least qualified` + 不定詞 `to talk about`，`the one` 後接形容詞子句。
- **`if you were to ask them when they were happiest ...`** — `if + were to + 原形` 表對未來的假設語氣；`when` 引導名詞子句作 `ask` 的受詞。
- **`I want to want things and then get them.`** — `want to want`（想要「去渴望」）雙層不定詞，語意上刻意堆疊，凸顯「渴望本身」也是目標。

---

## 38. 驚喜與多巴胺：過度排程扼殺驚喜、人生之河

### 逐句對照

**主持人:** Surprises are really interesting—the sort of unpredictability. I think it's total bro science here, but I'm pretty sure that's kind of how dopamine works. That things are a bit better than you expected.
驚喜真的很有意思——那種不可預測性。我知道這完全是「兄弟科學」（沒有嚴謹根據的說法），但我相當確定多巴胺大概就是這樣運作的：事情比你預期的稍微好一點。

**主持人:** Which means that for the perennial insecure overachievers who cloy for control, who really want the schedule to be perfectly done and we know the itinerary, we know where we're going to be at this time—you're in some ways reducing the capacity for surprise, because everything has become very contrived, prescribed, done in advance, laid out. Your ability to be surprised actually diminishes.
這意味著，對那些長期沒安全感、又追求成就、渴望掌控的人來說——那種一定要把行程排得完美無缺、知道行程表、知道自己幾點會在哪裡的人——你某種程度上正在削減「被驚喜的能力」，因為一切都變得非常刻意、事先規定好、提前做好、全部攤開安排妥當。你被驚喜到的能力其實在遞減。

**Naval:** Yeah. If nothing worked out the way you expected, if it was all serendipity and you didn't want that, you would just be a ball of anxiety. On the other hand, if everything worked out as you expected and wanted, you'd be so bored you might as well be dead. So there's some—you know, the river of life kind of flows between these two banks—and enjoy it.
對。如果沒有一件事照你預期的發展、全都是機緣巧合、而你又不想要那樣，那你就會變成一團焦慮。另一方面，如果每件事都照你的預期與期望發生，你會無聊到不如死了算了。所以有那麼一個——你懂的，人生之河就在這兩岸之間流動——好好享受它吧。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| unpredictability | /ˏʌnprɪˏdɪktəˋbɪlətɪ/ | n. | 不可預測性 |
| dopamine | /ˋdopəˏmin/ | n. | 多巴胺 |
| perennial | /pəˋrɛnɪəl/ | adj. | 長年的、反覆不斷的 |
| itinerary | /aɪˋtɪnəˏrɛrɪ/ | n. | 行程表 |
| contrived | /kənˋtraɪvd/ | adj. | 刻意造作的、人為安排的 |
| serendipity | /ˏsɛrənˋdɪpətɪ/ | n. | 機緣巧合、意外的好運 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`bro science`**：戲稱「兄弟科學」，指健身房或男性圈流傳、缺乏嚴謹依據的說法。
- **`a ball of anxiety`**：「一團焦慮」，形容人緊繃到不行的生動說法。
- **`you might as well be dead`**：「你不如死了算了」，`might as well` 表「（既然如此）乾脆⋯⋯」。
- **`the river of life flows between these two banks`**：比喻「人生在兩個極端之間流動」，banks 指河的兩岸。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`If nothing worked out the way you expected, you would just be a ball of anxiety.`** — 與現在事實相反的第二類條件句：`if + 過去式..., would + 原形`。
- **`you'd be so bored you might as well be dead.`** — `so + 形容詞 + (that) 子句` 表「如此⋯⋯以致於⋯⋯」，口語省略 `that`。
- **`the way you expected`** — `the way (that) you expected`，表「照你預期的方式」。

---

## 39. 想著自己是不快樂之源：自我這頭「野獸」

### 逐句對照

**主持人:** You say thinking about yourself is the source of all unhappiness, but presumably you need to work on yourself and your weaknesses as well. So some degree of reflection is important. And if thinking about yourself is a source of unhappiness, is this a price that you need to pay? "I need to reflect inward. I'm going to have to diminish this level of happiness for a little while, and then I can use this new level. I've got my brown belt on and I can go out into the world as a brown belt."
你說「想著自己」是一切不快樂的根源，但想必你也需要精進自己、改善自己的弱點，所以某種程度的自省是重要的。如果想著自己是不快樂的來源，這是不是一種你必須付出的代價？——「我需要向內反省，得暫時把快樂調降一段時間，然後我就能運用這個新的層次。我繫上了棕帶，能以一個棕帶的身分走進世界。」

**Naval:** What I'm specifically referring to is: if you're thinking about your personality and your ego and the character of you, and you're obsessing over that—that's where a lot of depression and unhappiness lingers and gets cultivated. Thinking "woe is me, this happened to me, that happened to me, I have this personality, I have this issue, I deserve this, I didn't get that"—you're just strengthening a little beast in there that is insatiable. And that's where I think a lot of unhappiness comes from.
我具體指的是：如果你一直想著你的個性、你的自我、你這個人的性格，而且對此念念不忘——那正是許多憂鬱與不快樂盤桓、被滋養出來的地方。想著「我好可憐，這種事發生在我身上、那種事也發生在我身上，我有這種個性、我有這個問題、我活該如此、我沒得到那個」——你只是在餵養裡面那頭永遠餵不飽的小野獸。而我認為，很多不快樂就是從那裡來的。

**主持人:** What's the beast?
那頭野獸是什麼？

**Naval:** It's the ego. But that word is so overused that I kind of hate to use it. It's like a recurrent collection of thoughts that are very self-obsessed and will never be satisfied.
是「自我」（ego）。但這個詞被用到爛，我其實不太想用它。它比較像是一堆反覆出現、極度自我沉迷、永遠不會滿足的念頭。

**主持人:** Very concretized as well. So they're not malleable, not particularly flexible.
而且非常固化。所以它們不可塑，也不特別有彈性。

**Naval:** So you're just adding to them by thinking about them all the time. You're creating narratives and stories and identities. But that's different from solving personal problems. If you encounter something, you learn from something, you're reflecting upon the learning—then you can reflect upon it, absorb it, and just move on.
所以你老是想著它們，只是在往上添加而已。你在製造敘事、故事和身分認同。但那和「解決個人問題」是不一樣的。如果你遇到某件事、從中學到東西、對那份學習加以反思——那你就可以思考它、吸收它，然後往前走。

**Naval:** But sitting there saying "I'm Chris, I'm Naval, I deserve this, this happened to me, that person wronged me, this is who I am, this shouldn't have happened, I need to go get revenge on this or fix that or change this"—that, I think, is where a lot of mental illness comes from.
但如果你只是坐在那裡說「我是 Chris、我是 Naval，我活該這樣，這種事發生在我身上，那個人虧待了我，這就是我，這本來不該發生，我得去報復這個、或修好那個、或改變這個」——那，我認為，正是許多心理疾病的來源。

**Naval:** So it depends: if you're thinking about something to solve a problem and get it off your chest and off your mind—if it leaves your mind clearer at the end, then I think it was worthwhile. If it leaves your mind busier at the end, then you're probably going the wrong direction.
所以這要看情況：如果你思考某件事，是為了解決一個問題、把它一吐為快、把它從心上卸下——如果到最後它讓你的心更清明，那我認為就值得。如果到最後它讓你的心更忙亂，那你大概走錯方向了。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| presumably | /prɪˋzuməblɪ/ | adv. | 想必、大概 |
| ego | /ˋigo/ | n. | 自我 |
| linger | /ˋlɪŋɡɚ/ | v. | 徘徊、逗留不去 |
| insatiable | /ɪnˋseʃəbl̩/ | adj. | 永不滿足的、貪得無厭的 |
| recurrent | /rɪˋkɝənt/ | adj. | 反覆出現的 |
| malleable | /ˋmælɪəbl̩/ | adj. | 可塑的、易改變的 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`woe is me`**：老派感嘆語「我好可慘、我真命苦」，常帶自憐或戲謔。
- **`get it off your chest`**：「把心事一吐為快、傾吐出來」。
- **`wrong someone`**：`wrong` 當動詞，「虧待、冤枉某人」。
- **`move on`**：「放下、往前走」，不再糾結於過去。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`that word is so overused that I kind of hate to use it.`** — `so ... that ...` 結果句型，「如此⋯⋯以致於⋯⋯」。
- **`thoughts that are very self-obsessed and will never be satisfied.`** — 一個關係子句 `that` 帶兩個並列述語（`are ...` 與 `will never be ...`）。
- **`it depends: if ... then ...`** — `it depends` 後以條件句展開，是口語裡「看情況，要是⋯⋯就⋯⋯」的常見結構。

---

## 40. 抽離是副產品：想比自己更大的事、反芻式治療

### 逐句對照

**主持人:** Is this a justification for detachment? Cultivated ignorance, distraction?
這算不算是為「抽離」找藉口？——刻意培養的無知、分散注意力？

**Naval:** Detachment is not a goal. Detachment is a byproduct. It's just a byproduct of realizing what matters and what doesn't. And just for one moment on the self thing: I think everybody craves thinking about something more than themselves. If you want to be happy to some extent, you have to forget about your personal problems. And one way to do that is to take on other problems—bigger problems.
抽離不是目標，抽離是「副產品」。它只是「認清什麼重要、什麼不重要」之後的副產品。順帶再談一下「自我」這件事：我認為每個人都渴望去想一件比自己更大的事。如果你想在某種程度上快樂，你就得忘掉自己的個人問題。而做到這點的一個方法，就是去承擔別的問題——更大的問題。

**Naval:** That could be a mission, that could be spirituality, that could be kids, it could be caring about the planet—although I think people take that a little far, and then they get kind of oppressive and tyrannical in support of abstract concepts. So these can be taken too far, just like religion, just like anything in excess.
那可以是一個使命，可以是靈性，可以是孩子，也可以是關心這個星球——不過我覺得有些人在這件事上走得有點遠，然後為了捍衛抽象的概念，變得有點壓迫、有點專橫。所以這些都可能被推得太過頭，就像宗教一樣，就像任何過了頭的東西一樣。

**主持人:** Anything in excess, right?
任何過量的東西，對吧？

**Naval:** Right. But generally, the less you think about yourself, the more you can think about a mission, or about God, or about a child, or something like that.
對。但大致來說，你越少想自己，就越能去想一個使命、或神、或一個孩子、或類似的東西。

**主持人:** I remember Vinay Hiremath, the founder of Loom, said, "I am rich and I have no idea what to do with my life," and you replied, "God, kids, or mission—pick at least one."
我記得 Loom 的創辦人 Vinay Hiremath 說過：「我很有錢，卻完全不知道這輩子要做什麼。」而你回他：「神、孩子、或使命——至少挑一個。」

**Naval:** That's right. Preferably all three. It's very liberating.
沒錯。最好三個都要。這非常令人解脫。

**Naval:** Yeah, overthinking about yourself—it may not be the cause of depression, but it certainly doesn't help. Rumination.
是啊，過度想著自己——它或許不是憂鬱的成因，但肯定沒幫助。就是「反芻」（rumination）。

**主持人:** I kind of had a self-induced Stockholm syndrome from this sort of thing, because I like to think about stuff, and it provides you with an endless number of things to think about. So you're kind of—
我對這種東西有點像是「自我誘發的斯德哥爾摩症候群」，因為我喜歡思考，而它會提供你無窮無盡可以想的東西。所以你有點像是——

**Naval:** Yeah, you have this—um—you're the prisoner and the prison guard at the same time.
對，你會有一種——嗯——你同時是囚犯，也是獄卒。

**主持人:** And I had Abigail Shrier on the show. She wrote this book called Bad Therapy, pushing back against therapy culture for kids, specifically for kids. There was a blast radius that covered pretty much everything, including CBT. I'm like, we're getting perilously close to some really evidence-based stuff here.
我請過 Abigail Shrier 上節目。她寫了一本叫《壞的治療》（Bad Therapy）的書，反對針對孩子的治療文化，特別是針對孩子的。但那波「爆炸半徑」幾乎涵蓋了所有東西，包括認知行為治療（CBT）。我就想，我們這下危險地逼近某些真的很有實證基礎的東西了。

**主持人:** But the more that I've thought about it and looked at the evidence, there is basically a direct correlation between how much you think about yourself and how miserable you are. Therapy is great if it lets you vent and it solves a thing, and then x sessions later you're done, you're clear. But if you're just looping on the same thing forever, then it's actually the opposite.
但我越是思考、越是去看證據，就發現「你想自己想得越多」與「你有多悲慘」之間，基本上是直接正相關的。治療如果能讓你發洩、解決一件事，然後幾次晤談之後你就結束了、清爽了，那很棒。但如果你只是永遠在同一件事上打轉，那其實效果恰恰相反。

**Naval:** You're bathing in it. You're indulging in it.
你是在裡面泡澡，你是在沉溺其中。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| detachment | /dɪˋtætʃmənt/ | n. | 抽離、超然、不執著 |
| byproduct | /ˋbaɪˏprɑdəkt/ | n. | 副產品 |
| tyrannical | /taɪˋrænɪkl̩/ | adj. | 專橫的、暴虐的 |
| liberating | /ˋlɪbəˏretɪŋ/ | adj. | 令人解脫的、使人自由的 |
| rumination | /ˏruməˋneʃən/ | n. | 反芻、反覆咀嚼（負面念頭） |
| vent | /vɛnt/ | v. | 發洩（情緒） |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`take something too far` / `take that a little far`**：「把某事做得太過頭、走得太遠」。
- **`in excess`**：「過量、過度」。
- **`push back against ...`**：「反對、抵制、頂回去」。
- **`bathe in it / indulge in it`**：「泡在其中／沉溺其中」，比喻對負面情緒的自我耽溺。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`the less you think about yourself, the more you can think about a mission.`** — `the + 比較級 ..., the + 比較級 ...` 表「越⋯⋯就越⋯⋯」。
- **`a direct correlation between how much you think about yourself and how miserable you are.`** — `correlation between A and B`，A、B 皆為 `how + 形容詞/副詞` 名詞子句。
- **`the more that I've thought about it ... there is basically a direct correlation`** — 口語裡以 `the more (that) ...` 起頭，主句改用一般直述來承接，是自然語流的鬆散結構。

---

---

## 41. 放下「變快樂」的技巧：沒有公式、問對問題

### 逐句對照

**主持人:** How have your "become happy" techniques developed over time?
你那套「讓自己變快樂」的技巧，隨著時間是怎麼演變的？

**Naval:** Yeah, I used to have a lot of them. Now I kind of try not to have any, because I think the techniques themselves are kind of a struggle.
是啊，我以前有一大堆。現在我盡量一個都不要，因為我覺得那些技巧本身就是一種掙扎。

**Naval:** It's sort of like bidding for status implies you're low status. It reveals that you're low status. So someone who's basically trying to show off comes across as low status.
這有點像是：去爭地位，本身就暗示你地位低。它反而洩露了你地位低。所以一個拼命想炫耀的人，給人的感覺反而是地位低。

**Naval:** The same way, someone who's trying to be happy is sort of saying "I'm unhappy" and creating that frame. So it's better just to not even think in terms of...
同樣道理，一個努力想變快樂的人，等於在說「我不快樂」，還把這個框架建立起來。所以最好連想都不要用這種角度去想。

**主持人:** You position yourself as being in lack in order to attain.
你為了得到，反而先把自己定位在「匱乏」的狀態。

**Naval:** Yeah. I don't even think in terms of happiness / unhappiness anymore. I just kind of do my thing.
對。我現在根本不再用快樂／不快樂去思考了。我就是做我自己的事。

**主持人:** Another question that's similar to a bunch of them. Do you think you could have got there had you not done the procedural, systematic, step-by-step "this is what it is" and then come out the other side?
再問一個跟前面很類似的問題。你覺得，如果你沒有走過那套按部就班、一步一步「這就是它」的流程，最後從另一端走出來，你還能到達現在的境界嗎？

**Naval:** I don't think there are any formulas. I think it's unique to each person. It's like asking a successful person, "How did you become successful?" Each one of them will give you a different story.
我不覺得有什麼公式。我認為那是因人而異的。這就像去問一個成功者：「你是怎麼成功的？」每個人給你的故事都不一樣。

**Naval:** You can't follow anyone else's path. And most of them are even probably telling you some narratized version of it that isn't quite true.
你沒辦法照別人的路走。而且他們大多還可能給你一個被包裝成故事的版本，其實不太真實。

**主持人:** That's something that I continually realize, especially as I get to spend more time around people that are successful. You hear "it's very important to prioritize work-life balance," right? That's one of the most common things that people who have attained success say.
這是我不斷體會到的一件事，尤其是我有更多機會待在成功者身邊。你會聽到「把工作與生活的平衡擺第一非常重要」，對吧？這是已經成功的人最常講的話之一。

**主持人:** That's not my experience. You shouldn't be asking somebody who is successful what they do to continue their success now. You should be asking them what they did to attain their success when they were where you were.
但那不是我的經驗。你不該去問一個成功者「現在」做什麼來維持成功。你該問的是：當他還在你現在這個位置時，他做了什麼才闖出成功。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| bid for | /bɪd/ | v. phr. | 競逐、爭取 |
| show off | /ʃo ɔf/ | v. phr. | 炫耀、賣弄 |
| frame | /frem/ | n. | 框架、看事情的角度 |
| formula | /ˋfɔrmjələ/ | n. | 公式、方程式 |
| attain | /əˋten/ | v. | 達成、獲得 |
| lack | /læk/ | n. | 匱乏、不足 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`come across as ...`**：給人「⋯⋯的感覺／印象」。例：`comes across as low status`（給人一種地位低的感覺）。
- **`do my thing`**：做自己的事、走自己的路，不理會別人的期待。
- **`in terms of ...`**：「就⋯⋯而言、用⋯⋯的角度」。`think in terms of happiness`＝用快樂與否的框架去思考。
- **`come out the other side`**：熬過整個過程、從另一頭走出來（常指走過艱難後的成長）。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`Do you think you could have got there had you not done ...?`** — `had you not done` 是第三類條件句的倒裝（＝`if you had not done`），與過去事實相反；搭配 `could have got` 表「當時本來能否做到」。
- **`someone who's trying to be happy is sort of saying "I'm unhappy"`** — `who's trying to be happy` 為關係子句修飾 `someone`；`sort of` 是口語緩和詞，「算是、有點在說」。

---

## 42. 極成功者不看「成功色情片」：壓倒性的渴望與專注

### 逐句對照

**Naval:** And the people who are really extraordinarily successful didn't sit around watching success porn. They just went and did it.
而那些真正極其成功的人，並不是坐在那裡看「成功色情片」。他們就是直接去做了。

**Naval:** They had such an overwhelming desire to be successful at the thing they were doing that they just went and did that thing. They didn't have time to study and learn and listen. They just did it.
他們對「把手上這件事做成功」有一種壓倒性的渴望，強烈到他們就直接去做了。他們根本沒空去研究、去學、去聽。他們就是做了。

**Naval:** It's the overwhelming desire that's the most important, and the focus that comes from that.
最重要的就是那股壓倒性的渴望，以及從中而生的專注。

**主持人:** That tweet of yours — "people who are good at making wealth, people who are good at attaining wealth, don't need to teach anybody else how to do it."
你那則推文說：「真正擅長創造財富、擅長取得財富的人，根本不需要去教別人怎麼做。」

**Naval:** Yeah. You don't need mentors, you need action. That was one of them. Another one is: the people who actually know how to make money don't need to sell you a course on it. There it is.
對。你不需要導師，你需要行動。那是其中一則。另一則是：真正懂得怎麼賺錢的人，不需要賣你一套課程。就是這樣。

**Naval:** There's lots of variations on it. Another one is: if you don't lie awake at night thinking about it, you don't want it badly enough.
這主題有很多變體。還有一則是：如果你不會半夜睡不著、滿腦子都在想它，那代表你還不夠想要它。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| extraordinarily | /ɪkˋstrɔrdnˏɛrəlɪ/ | adv. | 非凡地、極其地 |
| overwhelming | /ˏovɚˋhwɛlmɪŋ/ | adj. | 壓倒性的、排山倒海的 |
| desire | /dɪˋzaɪr/ | n. | 渴望、慾望 |
| mentor | /ˋmɛntɔr/ | n. | 導師、指導者 |
| variation | /ˏvɛrɪˋeʃən/ | n. | 變體、變化版本 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`success porn`**：戲稱「成功色情片」，指看不完的成功心法、勵志內容——看得爽卻不行動。
- **`sit around`**：無所事事地閒坐、乾耗時間。
- **`lie awake at night`**：（因掛念某事）夜裡睡不著、輾轉難眠。
- **`There it is.`**：口語「就是這樣、你看吧」，補一句作結。
- **`want it badly enough`**：夠渴望、想要到骨子裡。`badly` 在此是「極度地」。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`They had such an overwhelming desire ... that they just went and did that thing.`** — `such a(n) + 形容詞 + 名詞 + that ...` 表「如此⋯⋯以致於⋯⋯」的因果句型。
- **`It's the overwhelming desire that's the most important.`** — `It is ... that ...` 強調句，把 `the overwhelming desire` 提出來加以強調。
- **`if you don't lie awake ..., you don't want it badly enough`** — 第一類條件句（真實條件），表通則式的推論。

---

## 43. 睡不好也不苛責自己：改變來自渴望與理解，非強迫

### 逐句對照

**主持人:** I've heard you talk before about how unclosed loops — problems that you're working on — can cause you to be sleepless.
我以前聽你談過，那些「沒閉合的迴圈」，也就是你正在處理的問題，會害你睡不著。

**Naval:** I'm not a good sleeper.
我睡眠品質不好。

**主持人:** Tell me about that.
跟我說說。

**Naval:** Oh, my Eight Sleep hates me. It's always telling me I failed at sleeping again. And Brian Johnson thinks I'm going to die early. He's probably right.
喔，我的 Eight Sleep（智慧床墊）很討厭我。它老是告訴我，我又睡失敗了。而且 Brian Johnson 覺得我會早死。他八成是對的。

**主持人:** How much do you reckon you sleep a night? You got any idea?
你估計自己一晚睡多久？有概念嗎？

**Naval:** Oh, it's so random. Some nights I'll sleep 8 hours. Some nights I'll sleep 4 hours. But it's literally just random.
喔，超級隨機。有些晚上我睡八小時，有些晚上只睡四小時。真的完全是隨機的。

**主持人:** Are you bothered about that? You trying to optimize? You got a sleep coach teaching you how to—
你會為這件事困擾嗎？有想去優化它嗎？有請睡眠教練教你怎麼——

**Naval:** I don't flog myself over things. If I want to sleep, I'll sleep. If I don't want to sleep, I don't sleep. I don't think I'm doing anything right or wrong.
我不會為了這種事鞭打自己。想睡我就睡，不想睡我就不睡。我不覺得自己做對了什麼、或做錯了什麼。

**主持人:** You don't label it "good night, bad night."
你不會給它貼上「好眠、壞眠」的標籤。

**Naval:** No. I work out every day because I think it gives me more energy, and I've gotten into a good habit with it. Maybe I'll do the same thing with sleep. Maybe I'll develop a good habit, but I'm not going to beat myself up over it.
不會。我每天運動，因為我覺得那給我更多能量，而且我已經養成好習慣了。也許哪天我對睡眠也會這樣，也許會養成好習慣，但我不會為它自責。

**Naval:** There'll come a point where it's important to me, and when it's important to me, I'll just do it. For example, you look at people with addictions — overeating or smoking or whatever. They kind of go through all the different methods, but it's half-hearted.
總會有那麼一刻，它對我變得重要，而當它對我重要時，我自然就會去做。舉例來說，你看那些有癮的人——暴食、抽菸之類的。他們會把各種方法都試一遍，但都是半調子。

**Naval:** And then one day they're like, "Oh, I've got lung cancer. My dad has lung cancer." And they drop it immediately.
然後某一天他們忽然：「天啊，我得了肺癌。我爸有肺癌。」於是他們立刻就戒了。

**Naval:** So I think a lot of change is more about desire and understanding than it is about forcing yourself or trying to domesticate yourself.
所以我認為，很多改變靠的是渴望與理解，而不是逼迫自己、或試圖馴化自己。

**主持人:** It's efficiency again, I guess — aligning the thing that you want to do with the way that you feel about what it is that you want to do.
我想這又回到效率了——把你想做的事，跟你對「你想做的事」的感受對齊。

**Naval:** Yeah. It's not getting caught up in a half desire or a mimetic desire. It's really just being aware of what it is that you actually want at this point in time.
對。就是不要被一種半吊子的慾望、或模仿來的慾望給綁住。真正的關鍵是：清楚意識到你此時此刻究竟真正想要什麼。

**Naval:** And when you want something, then you will act on it with maximal capability. That's the time to act on it. In the meantime, just doing it because other people tell you you should, or society tells you you should, or you feel slightly guilty about it — these are half-hearted efforts, and half-hearted efforts don't get you there.
而當你真的想要某樣東西，你自然會用最大的能力去執行。那才是行動的時機。在那之前，只因為別人叫你做、社會叫你做、或你有點罪惡感才去做——這些都是半調子的努力，而半調子的努力帶不了你到目的地。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| sleepless | /ˋsliplɪs/ | adj. | 失眠的、睡不著的 |
| optimize | /ˋɑptəˏmaɪz/ | v. | 優化、最佳化 |
| addiction | /əˋdɪkʃən/ | n. | 成癮、癮 |
| half-hearted | /ˋhæfˋhɑrtɪd/ | adj. | 半調子的、不夠投入的 |
| domesticate | /dəˋmɛstəˏket/ | v. | 馴化、馴服 |
| mimetic | /mɪˋmɛtɪk/ | adj. | 模仿的（指模仿他人而來的慾望） |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`flog / beat myself up over ...`**：為某事苛責、鞭打自己；`beat oneself up over` 是很常用的口語。
- **`get into a good habit`**：養成好習慣；反面 `drop it`＝直接戒掉、放掉。
- **`get caught up in ...`**：陷進、被捲入（某種情緒或狀態）而無法自拔。
- **`in the meantime`**：在那之前、與此同時。
- **`get you there`**：帶你抵達目標（`there` 指成功／目的地）。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`a lot of change is more about A than it is about B`** — `more about A than about B` 比較句型，「與其說是 B，不如說更是 A」。
- **`There'll come a point where it's important to me.`** — `There will come + 名詞 + where 子句`，倒裝的存在句，「將會有一個⋯⋯的時刻」。
- **`aligning the thing that you want to do with the way that you feel`** — `align A with B`（把 A 與 B 對齊）；兩個 `that` 皆為關係子句。

---

## 44. 焦慮與壓力：壓力是兩股衝突的慾望、焦慮是未解問題的冰山

### 逐句對照

**主持人:** You mentioned anxiety before. "Imagine how effective you'd be if you weren't anxious all the time" is one of yours. And anxiety is the emotion du jour of the 21st century.
你剛才提到焦慮。「想想看，如果你不是整天焦慮，你會有多高效」這句是你說的。而焦慮正是二十一世紀當紅的情緒。

**主持人:** Lots of driven people are very anxious, very paranoid — that's what's caused them to be effective. They pay so much attention to detail, not letting things go, staying up at night thinking about it. That's the paranoia coming in. What have you come to learn about anxiety and dealing with it?
很多有幹勁的人都非常焦慮、非常多疑——那正是讓他們變得高效的原因。他們極度注重細節、放不下事情、半夜還醒著想。那就是多疑在作祟。關於焦慮、以及如何面對它，你學到了什麼？

**Naval:** So anxiety and stress are interesting. They're very related. Stress is when — if you look at an iron beam, when an iron beam is under stress, it's because it's being bent in two different directions at the same time.
焦慮和壓力很有意思，兩者高度相關。壓力就像——你看一根鐵樑，當鐵樑承受應力時，是因為它同時被往兩個不同方向拉扯。

**Naval:** So when your mind is under stress, it's because it has two conflicting desires at once. For example, you want to be liked, but you want to do something selfish, and you can't reconcile the two, so you're under stress.
所以當你的心承受壓力時，是因為它同時有兩個互相衝突的慾望。比方說，你想被人喜歡，但你又想做件自私的事，兩者你調和不了，於是你就有壓力。

**Naval:** You want to do something for somebody else, you want to do something for yourself. You don't want to go to work, but you want to make money, so you're under stress. So you have two conflicting desires.
你想為別人做點什麼，又想為自己做點什麼。你不想上班，但你想賺錢，於是你有壓力。所以你有兩個互相衝突的慾望。

**Naval:** And one of the ways to get through stress is to acknowledge: "Oh, I actually have two conflicting desires, and either I need to resolve it — pick one and be okay losing the other — or I'll decide later." Just being aware of why you're stressed can help alleviate a lot of stress.
而化解壓力的方法之一，就是承認：「喔，我其實有兩個互相衝突的慾望，要嘛我得解決它——選一個，然後接受失去另一個——要嘛我晚點再決定。」光是意識到自己為何有壓力，就能減輕很多壓力。

**Naval:** And then anxiety, I think, is sort of this pervasive, unidentifiable stress, where you're just stressed out all the time and you're not even sure why, and you can't identify the underlying problem.
至於焦慮，我覺得比較像是一種瀰漫、又說不清源頭的壓力，你就是無時無刻都很緊繃，卻連為什麼都不確定，也找不出底下真正的問題。

**Naval:** I think the reason is because you have so many unresolved problems, unresolved stress points that have piled up in your life, that you can no longer identify what the problems are. There's this mountain of garbage in your mind, and a little bit of it is poking out the top like an iceberg — and that's anxiety. But underneath there's a lot of unresolved things.
我認為原因在於：你累積了太多沒解決的問題、沒處理的壓力點，堆到你已經認不出問題到底是什麼。你腦中有一座垃圾山，只有一小角像冰山那樣冒出頂端——那就是焦慮。但底下藏著一大堆懸而未決的事。

**Naval:** So you need to go through very carefully, every time you're anxious: "Okay, why am I anxious this time? I don't know why. Let me sit here and think about it. Let me write down what the possible causes could be. Let me meditate on it. Let me journal. Let me talk to a therapist. Let me talk to my friends." Just kind of see: when does that stress go away?
所以每次焦慮時，你都得很仔細地梳理：「好，我這次為什麼焦慮？我不知道。那我坐下來想一想。把可能的原因寫下來。針對它冥想。寫日記。找治療師談。找朋友談。」就這樣去看：那股壓力什麼時候消退。

**Naval:** If you can identify and unravel and resolve these issues, then I think that helps get rid of anxiety. A lot of the anxiety is piled up because we move through life too quickly, not observing our own reactions to things. We don't resolve them.
如果你能辨識、拆解、並解決這些問題，我認為就能幫助你擺脫焦慮。很多焦慮之所以堆積，是因為我們過生活過得太快，沒去觀察自己對事情的反應。我們沒把它們解決掉。

**Naval:** So this goes counter to what I said earlier about not reflecting too much. But you reflect on the problems to observe them and solve them. You don't reflect on them to feel better about yourself, to indulge them.
所以這跟我先前說的「別過度反思」正好相反。但你反思問題，是為了觀察它、解決它。你反思它，不是為了讓自己感覺好過、去縱容那些情緒。

**主持人:** Well, if you're doing it just to feel better about yourself, that could be strengthening your personality and your ego, and could be creating a more fragile personality.
嗯，如果你反思只是為了讓自己好過一點，那可能反而在強化你的人格與自我，打造出一個更脆弱的人格。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| anxiety | /æŋˋzaɪətɪ/ | n. | 焦慮 |
| conflicting | /kənˋflɪktɪŋ/ | adj. | 互相衝突的 |
| reconcile | /ˋrɛkənˏsaɪl/ | v. | 調和、使一致 |
| alleviate | /əˋlivɪˏet/ | v. | 減輕、緩解 |
| pervasive | /pɚˋvesɪv/ | adj. | 瀰漫的、無所不在的 |
| unravel | /ʌnˋrævl/ | v. | 拆解、解開（謎團／糾結） |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`emotion du jour`**：借自法語 `du jour`（今日的、當令的），指「當紅、最流行的情緒」。
- **`stressed out`**：（被壓力壓得）緊繃、崩潰；口語裡極常用。
- **`poke out`**：（一小部分）冒出來、探出頭，如冰山露出水面。
- **`go counter to ...`**：與⋯⋯背道而馳、正好相反。
- **`get rid of ...`**：擺脫、除掉。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`Imagine how effective you'd be if you weren't anxious all the time.`** — 第二類條件句（與現在事實相反）：`if + 過去式, would + 原形`，表假設。
- **`either I need to resolve it ... or I'll decide later`** — `either ... or ...` 對等連接兩個選項。
- **`so many ... that you can no longer identify ...`** — `so + many + 名詞 + that ...`，「如此多⋯⋯以致於⋯⋯」的因果結構。

---

## 45. 以死亡化解焦慮：一切歸零、時間的浪費即不在場

### 逐句對照

**Naval:** One big anxiety resolver for me is just ruminating on death. I think that's a good one. You're going to die. It's all going to zero. You cannot take anything with you.
對我來說，一個很強的焦慮解方，就是反覆思索死亡。我覺得那招很好用。你終將一死。一切都會歸零。你什麼都帶不走。

**Naval:** And I know this is trite. And I know we don't spend enough time thinking about the big questions — we kind of give up on them when we're very, very young.
我知道這話很老套。我也知道我們花在思考那些大哉問上的時間太少了——我們在很小很小的時候就差不多放棄它們了。

**Naval:** A little child might ask the big questions like, "Why are we here? What's the meaning of life? What is this all about? Is there Santa Claus? Is there God?" But then as adults, we're taught not to think about these things, or we've given up on them.
一個小孩可能會問那些大哉問：「我們為什麼在這裡？生命的意義是什麼？這一切到底是怎麼回事？有聖誕老人嗎？有神嗎？」可是長大成人後，我們被教導別去想這些，或者早就放棄了。

**Naval:** But I think the big questions are the big questions for good reasons. And if you can keep the idea in front of you at all times that you're going to die, and that everything goes literally to zero...
但我認為，大哉問之所以是大哉問，是有充分理由的。而如果你能時時把這個念頭擺在眼前——你終將一死，一切真的都會歸零……

**Naval:** What's there to stress about?
那還有什麼好焦慮的？

**主持人:** Yeah. For better or worse, life is very short. How should people deal with its briefness?
是啊。不論好壞，人生就是很短。人們該怎麼面對它的短暫？

**Naval:** Enjoy it. Make the best of it. It's even briefer than that — each moment just disappears. It's gone. There's only a present moment, and it's gone instantly.
好好享受。把它發揮到極致。而且它比你想的還短——每一個當下都轉眼消失。它就沒了。只有一個當下存在，而它瞬間就消逝。

**Naval:** So if you're not there for it — if you're stressed out, or anxious, or thinking about something else — you missed it. Any moment when you're not in that moment, you are dead to that moment.
所以如果你沒有在場——如果你正緊繃、正焦慮、或在想別的事——你就錯過它了。任何一個你不在其中的當下，對那個當下而言你形同已死。

**Naval:** You might as well be dead, because your mind is off doing something else, or living in some imagined reality that is just a very poor substitute for the actual reality.
你不如死了算了，因為你的心跑去做別的事，或活在某個想像出來的現實裡——那只是真實現實的一個很差勁的替代品。

**Naval:** So one of my recent realizations was: what is wasted time? What is a waste of time? I don't like to waste time, but what is wasted time? And everything is wasted time in a sense, because nothing matters in the ultimate.
所以我最近的一個領悟是：什麼叫浪費掉的時間？什麼叫浪費時間？我不喜歡浪費時間，可是到底什麼算浪費掉的時間？在某種意義上，一切都是被浪費掉的時間，因為到了終極層面，沒有一件事重要。

**Naval:** But in each moment, the thing matters. In each moment, it's the only thing that matters. What's happening in front of you literally has all the meaning in the world. So what matters is just being present for the thing.
但在每一個當下，那件事很重要。在每個當下，它是唯一重要的事。眼前正在發生的事，確確實實承載著世上全部的意義。所以真正重要的，就是全然在場於那件事。

**Naval:** So if you're doing something you want to do and you're fully there for it, then it's not wasted time. If you don't want to do it, and your mind is running away from it, and you're reacting against it, and you're wishing you were somewhere else, and you're anticipating some future thing or regretting some past thing or being fearful of something — then that's wasted time.
所以如果你在做一件你想做的事，而且全然在場，那就不是被浪費的時間。如果你不想做它，你的心一直想逃開，你抗拒它，你希望自己在別處，你在期待某件未來的事、懊悔某件過去的事、或害怕某件事——那才是被浪費掉的時間。

**Naval:** That's time being wasted when you're not actually present for the reality in front of you. Yes, I do want some material things in life, and there are things that have more value than others within this life — but this life is very short and bounded.
那才是浪費：當你並沒有真正在場於眼前的現實。是的，我人生中確實想要一些物質的東西，人生裡也有些事物比其他更有價值——但這一生非常短暫、且有其邊界。

**Naval:** So the true wasted time is time that you're not present for. When you're not doing the thing you want to do to the best of your capability, such that you're immersed in it — if you're not immersed in this moment, then you're wasting your time.
所以真正被浪費的時間，是你沒有在場的時間。當你沒有用盡全力去做你想做的事、以至於能全然沉浸其中——如果你沒有沉浸在這個當下，那你就是在浪費你的時間。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| ruminate | /ˋrumənˏet/ | v. | 反覆思索、沉思 |
| trite | /traɪt/ | adj. | 老套的、陳腔濫調的 |
| briefness | /ˋbrifnɪs/ | n. | 短暫 |
| substitute | /ˋsʌbstəˏtjut/ | n. | 替代品 |
| bounded | /ˋbaʊndɪd/ | adj. | 有邊界的、有限的 |
| immersed | /ɪˋmɝst/ | adj. | 沉浸的、全神投入的 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`go to zero`**：歸零、化為烏有；`It's all going to zero.` 一切終將歸零。
- **`for better or worse`**：不論好壞、無論結果如何。
- **`be there for it / be present for ...`**：在場、全神貫注於當下（此處非「支持某人」的意思）。
- **`might as well be dead`**：`might as well + 原形`＝「不如、乾脆」，此處「不如死了算了」。
- **`make the best of it`**：善用（有限的條件）、把它發揮到最好。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`if you can keep the idea in front of you at all times that you're going to die`** — `the idea ... that you're going to die` 中 `that` 子句為 `idea` 的同位語；因 `in front of you at all times` 太長而後移。
- **`What's there to stress about?`** — `There is ... to + 原形` 的疑問句，「有什麼好⋯⋯的？」。
- **`to the best of your capability, such that you're immersed in it`** — `such that ...` 引導結果子句，「以至於⋯⋯」。

---

## 46. 大半人生其實不在場：意識是本體，身心是短暫

### 逐句對照

**主持人:** People get worried about dying and no longer being here, but they don't realize that so much of their life is spent not being here in any case.
人們擔心死去、擔心不再存在於此，卻沒意識到：他們這輩子有好大一部分，本來就是「不在場」度過的。

**Naval:** That's right. But I think people crave being here for it. And when you're here for it, you're actually not thinking about yourself — you're more immersed in the thing, the moment, the task at hand.
沒錯。但我認為人們其實渴望「在場」。而當你在場時，你其實不會想著自己——你更沉浸在那件事、那個當下、手邊的任務裡。

**主持人:** We don't want peace of mind. We want peace for our mind.
我們要的不是「心的平靜」，我們要的是「讓心得到安寧」。

**Naval:** That's right. Yeah. The mind is what can eat you alive if you let it. And there's more to you than the mind.
沒錯。是啊。心念這東西，你一放任它，它就能把你活活吞噬。而你，遠不只是你的心念而已。

**主持人:** How so?
怎麼說？

**Naval:** Well, I mean the very— I don't want to disassemble the body, so to speak, right?
嗯，我是說那個本身——我不想去「拆解身體」，姑且這麼說吧，對吧？

**主持人:** Please go on.
請繼續說。

**Naval:** Yeah. At the end of the day, everything arises within your consciousness, right? You've got nowhere else to experience it.
好。說到底，一切都是在你的意識之中生起的，對吧？你沒有別的地方能去經驗它。

**Naval:** And that consciousness is relatively static, in the sense that it's been exactly the same from the moment you were born to the moment you die. And everything you experience — from your body, from your mind, to the world, to everything — is within that consciousness.
而那個意識相對來說是恆定的，意思是：從你出生的那一刻到你死去的那一刻，它一直完全一樣。而你所經驗的一切——從你的身體、你的心念，到這個世界、到一切——都在那個意識之中。

**Naval:** That base layer of being — and this is what the Buddhists will tell you — is the real thing. Everything that comes and goes in the middle, including your mind, including your body, is unreal.
那個存在的底層——這也是佛家會告訴你的——才是真實的東西。中間那些來來去去的一切，包括你的心念、你的身體，都是虛妄的。

**Naval:** And trying to find stability in those transient things is your castle that you're building on sand — that's going to crumble.
而想在那些無常的事物裡尋求穩定，就是你蓋在沙上的城堡——終究會崩塌。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| crave | /krev/ | v. | 渴望、極度想要 |
| disassemble | /ˏdɪsəˋsɛmbl/ | v. | 拆解、拆卸 |
| consciousness | /ˋkɑnʃəsnɪs/ | n. | 意識 |
| static | /ˋstætɪk/ | adj. | 靜止的、恆定不變的 |
| transient | /ˋtrænʃənt/ | adj. | 短暫的、無常的 |
| crumble | /ˋkrʌmbl/ | v. | 崩塌、瓦解 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`eat you alive`**：把你活活吞噬、折磨得死去活來。
- **`there's more to you than ...`**：你遠不只是⋯⋯而已（強調還有更深的層面）。
- **`How so?`**：「怎麼說？何以見得？」用來請對方進一步解釋。
- **`so to speak`**：「姑且這麼說、可謂」，替不太精確的比喻打圓場。
- **`at the end of the day`**：說到底、歸根究柢。
- **`building on sand`**：建在沙上（典出聖經），比喻根基不穩、注定崩壞。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`peace of mind` vs. `peace for our mind`** — 靠介系詞的差別玩出雙關：`of`（心「的」平靜）對比 `for`（「給」心的安寧）。
- **`The mind is what can eat you alive if you let it.`** — `what` 引導名詞子句作主詞補語，「⋯⋯的那個東西」。
- **`in the sense that ...`** — 「在⋯⋯這個意義上」，用來限定前面說法的範圍。

---

## 47. 詮釋由你決定：最好不帶詮釋，讓事物如其所是

### 逐句對照

**Naval:** Life is going to play out the way it's going to play out. There will be some good and some bad. Most of it is actually just up to your interpretation.
人生會怎麼演，就會怎麼演。當中會有好的、有壞的。但大部分其實只取決於你怎麼詮釋。

**Naval:** You're born, you have a set of sensory experiences, and then you die. How you choose to interpret those experiences is up to you. And different people interpret them in different ways.
你出生，經歷一連串感官體驗，然後你死去。你選擇怎麼詮釋這些體驗，全由你決定。而不同的人，會用不同的方式去詮釋。

**Naval:** The old line about two people walking down the street — they're having the exact same experience. One is happy, one is sad. It's a narrative in their heads. It's how they choose to interpret.
就像那句老話：兩個人走在同一條街上——他們有著一模一樣的經歷。一個開心，一個難過。差別在於他們腦中的那套敘事，在於他們選擇怎麼詮釋。

**Naval:** So when I said that, it was a long time ago. I was talking more about having positive interpretations and negative interpretations. But these days, I think it's better just not to have any interpretations, and to just allow things to be.
所以我當初講那句話，是很久以前了。那時我談的比較是「正面詮釋」和「負面詮釋」。但這幾年，我覺得最好是根本不帶任何詮釋，就讓事物如其所是。

**主持人:** You're still going to have interpretations.
你還是會產生詮釋啊。

**Naval:** You can't stop it. And nor should you try. But even having an interpretation is just a thing you can leave alone.
你阻止不了它。你也不該去阻止。但即使你有了詮釋，那也只是一件你可以放著不管的事而已。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| play out | /ple aʊt/ | v. phr. | （事情）發展、上演到結束 |
| interpretation | /ɪnˏtɝprɪˋteʃən/ | n. | 詮釋、解讀 |
| sensory | /ˋsɛnsərɪ/ | adj. | 感官的 |
| narrative | /ˋnærətɪv/ | n. | 敘事、故事 |
| leave alone | /liv əˋlon/ | v. phr. | 放著不管、別去碰 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`be up to you`**：由你決定、取決於你。
- **`the old line about ...`**：「關於⋯⋯的那句老話」，引出眾所皆知的說法或典故。
- **`allow things to be`**：讓事物如其所是、不去干涉。
- **`leave (something) alone`**：放它一邊、不去理會或處理。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`Life is going to play out the way it's going to play out.`** — `the way (that) + 子句` 當副詞，「以⋯⋯的方式」；此處刻意重複同一句，語氣上帶「順其自然」的宿命感。
- **`And nor should you try.`** — `nor + 助動詞 + 主詞` 的倒裝否定，接續前面否定語氣，「你也不該（去試）」。
- **`even having an interpretation is just a thing you can leave alone`** — 動名詞片語 `having an interpretation` 當主詞；`(that) you can leave alone` 為省略關係代名詞的子句修飾 `a thing`。

---

## 48. 珍惜時間：觀照自己看見循環、活出不必抱歉的人生

### 逐句對照

**主持人:** I really want to dig in a little more to the best way to remind people that they should value their time — just how brief it is — the time that you spend ruminating, being distracted, fears of the past, regrets.
我很想再深入挖一點：提醒人們珍惜時間的最好方法是什麼——就是它有多短暫——那些你花在反覆糾結、分心、對過去的恐懼、悔恨上的時間。

**Naval:** Well, I don't want to tell anybody how to live their life. I would just say that, to the extent that you want to improve your quality of life, the easiest and best way to do that is to observe your own mind and your own thoughts.
嗯，我不想告訴任何人該怎麼過他的人生。我只會說：如果你想提升自己的生活品質，最簡單也最好的方法，就是去觀察自己的心念、自己的想法。

**Naval:** And be a little — not necessarily critical, but be observant of yourself more objectively — and then you'll realize your own loops and patterns. It takes time. It's not overnight. It's not instantaneous.
然後帶點——不一定要是批判——而是更客觀地觀照自己，接著你就會看見自己的那些循環和模式。這需要時間，不是一夜之間，也不是一瞬間就成的。

**主持人:** So you mean letting go is not a one-time event.
所以你的意思是，放下不是一次性的事件。

**Naval:** Yeah. And letting go is not necessarily even the right answer. Yes, if you're trying to be an enlightened being, live like a god, have everything be perfect, be a Buddha — sure, you can let go. But in practice it's actually quite hard to do.
對。而且放下甚至不見得就是正解。是啦，如果你想當個開悟的存在、活得像個神、讓一切都完美、成佛——當然，你可以放下。但實際操作起來其實相當難。

**Naval:** I would say you're going to find a lot of fulfillment out of life by just doing what you want to do and genuinely exploring what it is that you want — rather than doing what other people expect you to do, or society expects you to do, or what you might just think should be done by default.
我會說，你會從人生中得到很多的滿足感，靠的就是去做你真正想做的事、真誠地探索你到底想要什麼——而不是去做別人期待你做的、社會期待你做的、或你只是「預設」覺得該做的事。

**Naval:** You know, I think most older successful people will tell you that their life was best when they lived it unapologetically, on their own terms.
你知道嗎，我想大多數上了年紀的成功者都會告訴你：他們人生最好的時光，是當他們毫不抱歉地、照自己的方式去活的時候。

**主持人:** Be selfish.
自私一點。

**Naval:** Holistic selfishness. We can clip that little "selfish." Yeah.
是整體性的自私。我們可以把「自私」那小段剪出來當短片。哈，對啦。

**主持人:** Bad guy. Great.
壞人一個。太好了。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| ruminate | /ˋrumənˏet/ | v. | 反覆糾結、鑽牛角尖 |
| observant | /əbˋzɝvənt/ | adj. | 善於觀察的、留心的 |
| instantaneous | /ˏɪnstənˋtenɪəs/ | adj. | 瞬間的、即時的 |
| enlightened | /ɪnˋlaɪtnd/ | adj. | 開悟的、覺悟的 |
| fulfillment | /fʊlˋfɪlmənt/ | n. | 滿足感、成就感 |
| unapologetically | /ˏʌnəˏpɑləˋdʒɛtɪklɪ/ | adv. | 毫不抱歉地、理直氣壯地 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`dig in / dig into ...`**：深入探究、鑽研某個主題。
- **`to the extent that ...`**：「就⋯⋯的程度而言、如果你想⋯⋯的話」。
- **`a one-time event`**：一次性的事件（不是一勞永逸）。
- **`on your own terms`**：照自己的條件與方式（去做／去活）。
- **`by default`**：預設地、在沒特別選擇下就自動如此。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`you'll find a lot of fulfillment by just doing what you want ... rather than doing what other people expect`** — `by + 動名詞`（方法）對上 `rather than + 動名詞`（而非），形成鮮明對比。
- **`their life was best when they lived it unapologetically, on their own terms`** — `when` 時間子句點出「最佳狀態的條件」；`unapologetically` 副詞修飾 `lived`。
- **`if you're trying to be an enlightened being ... sure, you can let go`** — 讓步式的真實條件句，`sure` 為口語插入語，表勉強認可、「好啦、是可以」。

---

---

## 49. 頭腦 vs 直覺：直覺是精煉的判斷，睡一覺等它浮現

### 逐句對照

**主持人:** I had this insight, or a question, I guess. How much do you think that we should trust the voice in our heads? Because half of wisdom suggests to rely on your sort of bottom-up intuition, and then half of it has to be sort of top-down rational as possible. How do you navigate the tension between head and gut in this way?
我有個領悟，或者說是個疑問吧。你覺得我們該有多相信腦袋裡的那個聲音？因為有一半的智慧告訴你要靠那種由下而上的直覺，另一半又要你盡量走由上而下、理性的路線。你怎麼在頭腦和直覺這種張力之間拿捏？

**Naval:** I think the gut is what decides. The head is kind of what rationalizes it afterwards. The gut is the ultimate decision maker. And what is the gut? The gut is refined judgment. It's taste, aggregated.
我認為做決定的是直覺。頭腦某種程度上是事後把它合理化的那個。直覺才是最終的決策者。那直覺是什麼？直覺是精煉過的判斷，是累積出來的品味。

**Naval:** It could be aggregated through evolution, and it's in your genes and your DNA, or it could be aggregated through your experiences and what you've thought through. The mind is good at solving new problems in the external world that have defined edges, you know, beginnings and ends and objectives.
它可能是透過演化累積下來、寫在你的基因和 DNA 裡的，也可能是透過你的經歷、你想通的那些事累積出來的。頭腦擅長解決外在世界裡那些邊界清楚的新問題，你懂的，有開頭、有結尾、有明確目標的那種。

**Naval:** What the mind is actually really bad at is making hard decisions. So when you have a hard decision to make, I find it's better to—yes, you ruminate on it, you think through all the pros and cons, but then you sleep on it. You wait a couple of days. You wait until the gut answer appears with conviction and it feels right.
頭腦真正很不擅長的，其實是做艱難的決定。所以當你有個難題要決定時，我發現比較好的做法是——沒錯，你反覆琢磨它，把所有利弊都想過一遍，但接著你睡一覺再說。你等個幾天。你等到那個直覺答案帶著堅定的信念浮現、感覺對了為止。

**Naval:** And when you're younger, it takes longer because you just don't have as much experience. And when you're older, it can happen much faster.
年輕的時候會花比較久，因為你就是經驗沒那麼多。等你老一點，這個過程可以快得多。

**主持人:** And you have less time to—
而且你剩下的時間也比較少——

**Naval:** Yeah. And old people are just more set in their ways as a consequence, right? They know what they want. They know what they don't want. So it takes time to develop your gut instinct and judgment. But once you've developed them, don't trust anything else, because you can't go against your gut. It'll bite you in the end.
對。老人家因此就更加固執己見，對吧？他們知道自己要什麼，也知道自己不要什麼。所以培養你的直覺本能和判斷力是要花時間的。但一旦你培養出來了，就別再相信其他任何東西，因為你不能違背自己的直覺，到頭來它會反咬你一口。

**Naval:** Usually in relationships that failed, you can look back and say, "Oh, actually, I knew it was going to fail because of this reason, but I kind of went ahead anyway because I wanted it to be this way." I wanted this person to be a different way than they are, or I wanted to get a different thing out of it than I knew I was going to get, but I just wanted it.
通常在那些失敗的感情裡，你回頭看會說：「喔，其實我早就知道它會因為這個原因而失敗，但我還是硬著頭皮走下去了，因為我希望它是那個樣子。」我希望這個人不是他現在的樣子，或是我希望從中得到跟我明知會得到的不一樣的東西，但我就是想要。

**Naval:** So sometimes desire will override your judgment and then trap—
所以有時候慾望會壓過你的判斷，然後就把你困住——

**主持人:** Yeah. Wishful thinking.
對。一廂情願的想法。

**Naval:** It traps you into a pathway that chews up time.
它把你困進一條會吃掉你時間的路。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| intuition | /ˏɪntjʊˋɪʃən/ | n. | 直覺 |
| rationalize | /ˋræʃənəˏlaɪz/ | v. | 合理化、找理由 |
| ruminate | /ˋruməˏnet/ | v. | 反覆思索、沉思 |
| conviction | /kənˋvɪkʃən/ | n. | 堅定的信念 |
| set in one's ways | — | phr. | 積習難改、固執己見 |
| override | /ˏovɚˋraɪd/ | v. | 凌駕、壓過 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`gut`**：字面是「腸胃」，口語指「直覺」；`gut instinct`、`gut feeling` 都是「直覺、本能反應」。
- **`sleep on it`**：「先睡一覺、隔天再決定」——不急著當下拍板。
- **`it'll bite you in the end`**：「到頭來會反咬你一口、自食惡果」。
- **`chew up time`**：「大量吃掉／耗掉時間」，chew up 指消耗殆盡。
- **`wishful thinking`**：「一廂情願、痴心妄想」——把希望當成事實。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`half of wisdom suggests to rely on ... and then half of it has to be ... rational`** — `half of A ... half of it ...` 對比句式，把同一件事的兩面拆開講。
- **`you wait until the gut answer appears with conviction and it feels right`** — `wait until + 子句` 表「等到⋯⋯為止」；until 引導時間副詞子句。
- **`I wanted this person to be a different way than they are`** — `want + 受詞 + to V` 表期望；`than they are` 是與現況相比的比較子句。

---

## 50. 無法改變他人，只能改變自己：用讚美而非批評

### 逐句對照

**主持人:** What's that thing of yours? "We think we can't change ourselves, but we can. We think we can change other people, but we can't."
你那句話是怎麼說的來著？「我們以為自己改變不了自己，但其實可以；我們以為能改變別人，但其實不能。」

**Naval:** Exactly. To add to that, you can't change other people. You can change your reaction to them. You can change yourself, but other people only change through trauma or their own insight, on their own schedule, and never in a way that you like.
沒錯。再補一句，你改變不了別人。你能改變的是自己對他們的反應。你能改變自己，但別人只會透過創傷或他們自己的頓悟而改變，按他們自己的時間表，而且從來不會照你喜歡的方式改。

**主持人:** Yeah. Alain de Botton says that people do sometimes change, but rarely in relationships, and never when they're told to.
對。艾倫·狄波頓說過，人有時候確實會變，但在感情裡很少變，而且被要求變的時候絕對不會變。

**Naval:** Absolutely. The fastest way to alienate somebody is to tell them to change. In fact, the Dale Carnegie School of Public Speaking—the way that operates is, they get you up there and they realize that the number one problem with public speaking is that people are very self-conscious.
完全同意。要讓一個人跟你疏遠，最快的方式就是叫他改變。事實上，卡內基演講學校——它運作的方式是，他們讓你站到台上，然後他們發現公開演講的頭號問題，就是人會非常在意別人的眼光。

**Naval:** People who are practicing in the Dale Carnegie School—I never went through it, I heard this secondhand, so I could be wrong, but I like the story—they get up and they start speaking, and the people in the audience are only allowed to compliment them, genuine compliments not fake compliments, on things that they did well. But you're not allowed to criticize them on things that they did poorly. And eventually they get through it and they develop the self-confidence.
在卡內基學校練習的人——我沒真的上過課，這是聽來的二手消息，所以我可能講錯，但我喜歡這個故事——他們站起來開始講，台下的觀眾只被允許稱讚他們，是真心的稱讚而不是假的，稱讚他們做得好的地方。但你不准去批評他們做不好的地方。最後他們就熬過去了，也建立起了自信。

**Naval:** The same way, there's like the Michel Thomas school of language learning. What they do is, you listen to a teacher talking to a student. They're not teaching you. You're not expected to remember or memorize anything. You just listen to a student stumbling over the language. It's a better way to learn because you yourself don't feel flustered. You're not being tested, graded.
同樣地，有個叫米歇爾·湯瑪斯的語言學習法。他們的做法是，你聽一位老師跟一個學生對話。他們不是在教你。他們不要求你記住或背下任何東西。你只是聽一個學生磕磕巴巴地講那個語言。這是更好的學習方式，因為你自己不會覺得慌張。你不會被測驗、被打分數。

**主持人:** Oh, so you're not in your own head as much.
喔，所以你不會那麼陷在自己的腦袋裡。

**Naval:** Correct. You're not in your own head, and you might even be laughing at the student, or agreeing with the teacher, or sympathizing with the student. But because you are a passive observer, you can be more objective about it, and you aren't threatened or fearful, and you can learn better.
沒錯。你不會陷在自己的腦袋裡，你甚至可能會笑那個學生，或是認同老師，或是同情那個學生。但因為你是個被動的旁觀者，你可以更客觀地看待它，你不會覺得受威脅或害怕，於是你能學得更好。

**Naval:** Coming back to the original point of "you can't change people": if you do want to change someone's behavior, I think the only effective way to do it is to compliment them when they do something you want.
回到「你改變不了別人」這個原本的論點：如果你真的想改變某人的行為，我認為唯一有效的方式，就是在他們做了你想要的事時稱讚他們。

**主持人:** Not to be too positive—
不要太過正面——

**Naval:** Yeah, exactly. Not to insult them or be negative or critical when they do something you don't want. And we can't help it. It's obviously in our nature to criticize, and I do it as well. But it just reminds me that when somebody does something praiseworthy, don't forget to praise them. Definitely go out of your way—and it'll be genuine. It has to be genuine. It can't be a fake thing.
對，就是這樣。不要在他們做了你不想要的事時去侮辱他們、態度負面或批評他們。而我們也控制不住。批評顯然是我們的天性，我自己也會。但這只是提醒我，當有人做了值得稱讚的事，別忘了稱讚他們。一定要特地去做——而且它會是真心的。它必須是真心的。不能是假的。

**Naval:** This is not one of those "just dropping compliments" type things. Eventually people will see through that. They want authenticity. But just don't forget to praise people when they do something praiseworthy, and you'll get more of that behavior.
這不是那種「隨口撒讚美」的東西。到頭來人們會看穿那一套。他們要的是真誠。但就是別忘了在別人做了值得稱讚的事時稱讚他們，這樣你就會得到更多那樣的行為。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| alienate | /ˋeljənˏet/ | v. | 使疏遠、離間 |
| self-conscious | /ˋsɛlfˋkɑnʃəs/ | adj. | 忸怩、太在意他人眼光的 |
| flustered | /ˋflʌstɚd/ | adj. | 慌張、手足無措的 |
| compliment | /ˋkɑmpləmənt/ | n./v. | 稱讚、恭維 |
| praiseworthy | /ˋprezˏwɝðɪ/ | adj. | 值得讚揚的 |
| authenticity | /ˏɔθɛnˋtɪsətɪ/ | n. | 真誠、真實性 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`hear something secondhand`**：「聽來的二手消息、道聽塗說」，非親身經歷。
- **`stumble over the language`**：「講一種語言時結結巴巴、磕磕絆絆」。
- **`be in your own head`**：「陷在自己的思緒裡、鑽牛角尖」——過度自我意識。
- **`see through something`**：「看穿、識破」（虛假的東西）。
- **`go out of your way (to do)`**：「特地、不嫌麻煩地去做某事」。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`the fastest way to alienate somebody is to tell them to change`** — `The + 最高級 + way to V is to V` 是給建議的高頻句型。
- **`you're not expected to remember or memorize anything`** — `be expected to V` 被動語態，表「被期望／被要求」。
- **`we can't help it` / `it's in our nature to criticize`** — `can't help + N/Ving` 表「忍不住」；`it's in one's nature to V` 表「⋯⋯是天性」。

---

## 51. 愛的是這個人還是他的潛力：不可言說之處才有真愛

### 逐句對照

**主持人:** There was a really famous thread on Reddit about five questions to ask yourself if you're uncertain about your relationship. One of the questions was: "Are you truly in love with your partner, or just their potential, or the idea of them?" And that's the—you know, they show such great promise. They look at their ability for change and growth. They're on the right path.
Reddit 上有個非常有名的討論串，講的是如果你對自己的感情不確定，該問自己的五個問題。其中一個問題是：「你是真的愛你的伴侶，還是只愛他的潛力，或者你腦中對他的想像？」而這就是——你懂的，他們展現出這麼大的前景。他們看重的是對方改變與成長的能力。他們覺得對方走在正確的路上。

**Naval:** The partner-matching thing is so hard. When people come and ask me, like, "Oh, should I be with this person?"—well, if you're asking me, the answer is clearly no. Right? Because you wouldn't have to ask if you were with the right person.
挑對象這件事真的很難。當有人來問我：「喔，我該跟這個人在一起嗎？」——好吧，如果你得問我，那答案顯然是不該。對吧？因為如果你是跟對的人在一起，你根本就不必問。

**Naval:** Or when you ask someone why they're in a relationship with somebody, and they start reading out his or her resume—that's also a bad sign.
或者當你問某人為什麼跟某個人在一起，然後他開始把對方的履歷唸出來——這也是個壞徵兆。

**主持人:** What do you mean?
你是什麼意思？

**Naval:** Oh, it's like, "Oh, we have so much in common. We like to golf together." It's not a basis for a relationship. Or, "Oh, she's a ballerina," or, "He went to Harvard," or what have you. These are resume items. That's not who the person actually is.
喔，就是像「喔，我們有好多共同點。我們喜歡一起打高爾夫。」這不是一段感情的基礎。或者「喔，她是芭蕾舞者」，或「他念哈佛的」諸如此類。這些都是履歷上的條目。那不是這個人真正的樣子。

**主持人:** What's a better answer?
那什麼才是更好的答案？

**Naval:** "I just love being with this person. I just trust them. I enjoy being around them. I love how capable he is. I love how kind she is. I love her spirit. I love his energy."
「我就是喜歡跟這個人在一起。我就是信任他。我享受待在他身邊。我愛他有多能幹。我愛她有多善良。我愛她的靈魂。我愛他的能量。」

**Naval:** The more materially and concretely definable the reasons you're together are, the worse they are. The ineffable is actually where the sort of true love lies, because real love is a form of unity.
你們在一起的理由越是能用物質、用具體的方式定義出來，這些理由就越糟。那種無法言說的地方，其實才是真愛所在之處，因為真正的愛是一種合一。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| potential | /pəˋtɛnʃəl/ | n. | 潛力、潛能 |
| resume | /ˏrɛzjʊˋme/ | n. | 履歷表 |
| ballerina | /ˏbæləˋrinə/ | n. | 芭蕾女舞者 |
| concretely | /ˋkɑnkritlɪ/ | adv. | 具體地 |
| ineffable | /ɪnˋɛfəbl/ | adj. | 難以言喻的、不可名狀的 |
| unity | /ˋjunətɪ/ | n. | 合一、一體 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`show great promise`**：「展現出極大的前景／潛力」，promise 此處指「有前途」。
- **`have a lot in common`**：「有很多共同點」。
- **`or what have you`**：「諸如此類、之類的」——口語結尾語，等於 and so on。
- **`a bad sign`**：「一個壞徵兆、不好的跡象」。
- **`where true love lies`**：「真愛所在之處」，lie 此處指「存在於、位於」。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`you wouldn't have to ask if you were with the right person`** — 與現在事實相反的假設語氣：`would + V ... if + 過去式`。
- **`The more ... definable the reasons are, the worse they are`** — `The + 比較級 ..., the + 比較級 ...` 表「越⋯⋯就越⋯⋯」。
- **`the ineffable is where true love lies`** — `the + 形容詞` 當抽象名詞（那不可言說之物）；`where` 引導表地方／情境的名詞子句。

## 52. 愛、藝術、科學、神祕主義都在追求「合一」

### 逐句對照

**Naval:** It's a form of connection. It's connecting spirits—"Oh, you two, my consciousness meets your consciousness." The underlying drive in love, in art, in science, in mysticism is the desire for unity. It's a desire for connection.
它是一種連結。它是靈魂的相連——「喔，你們兩個，我的意識遇上了你的意識。」在愛裡、在藝術裡、在科學裡、在神祕主義裡，底層的那股驅力都是對合一的渴望。是對連結的渴望。

**Naval:** As Borges famously wrote, "In every human, there's a sense that something infinite has been lost." There's a God-shaped hole in you you're trying to fill.
就像波赫士那句名言寫的：「每個人心中都有一種感覺，覺得某種無限的東西已經失去了。」你心裡有一個上帝形狀的洞，你一直想把它填滿。

**Naval:** And so, we're always trying to find that connection. Love is trying to find it in one other person and saying, "Okay, you're male, I'm female, or whatever"—whatever your predilections are—"and now we connect, now we form a connected whole."
所以，我們總是在試著找到那個連結。愛，就是試圖在另一個人身上找到它，然後說：「好，你是男的，我是女的，或隨便什麼」——不管你的偏好是什麼——「而現在我們連上了，現在我們形成了一個相連的整體。」

**Naval:** Or in mysticism, it's all about "okay, sit down, meditate, and you'll feel the whole." In science, it's like, "atoms bouncing is mechanics, but that generates heat, so thermodynamics and motion, or kinetics, are one combined theory—that's a whole. Electricity and magnetism are one thing"—that's the whole that creates that sense of awe.
或者在神祕主義裡，重點全在於「好，坐下來，冥想，你就會感受到那個整體。」在科學裡，則像是「原子彈跳是力學，但那會產生熱，所以熱力學和運動、也就是動力學，是一套結合起來的理論——那就是一個整體。電和磁是同一件事」——那個整體就是創造出敬畏感的東西。

**Naval:** In art, it's like: I feel an emotion, I create a piece of art around it, and then you see that painting, or you see the Sistine Chapel, or you read the poem, and you feel that emotion. So again, it's creating unity. It's creating connection. And I think everybody craves that.
在藝術裡，則像是：我感受到一種情緒，我圍繞著它創造一件藝術品，然後你看到那幅畫，或你看到西斯汀禮拜堂，或你讀了那首詩，你也感受到了那份情緒。所以，這又是在創造合一，在創造連結。而我認為每個人都渴望那個。

**Naval:** So when you really love somebody, it's because you feel a sense of wholeness by being around them. And that sense of wholeness probably doesn't have anything to do with what school they went to, or what career they're in.
所以當你真正愛一個人，那是因為待在他身邊會讓你感受到一種完整。而那份完整感，大概跟他念過哪所學校、從事什麼職業一點關係都沒有。

**Naval:** Just tying that into the "life is short, stop fucking about": if you're faced with a difficult choice and you cannot decide, the answer is no. And the reason is, modern society is full of options.
把這個接回到「人生苦短，別再瞎混」這件事上：如果你面對一個困難的選擇而無法決定，那答案就是「不要」。原因是，現代社會充滿了選項。

**主持人:** Yeah.
對。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| consciousness | /ˋkɑnʃəsnɪs/ | n. | 意識 |
| mysticism | /ˋmɪstəˏsɪzəm/ | n. | 神祕主義 |
| predilection | /ˏpridɪˋlɛkʃən/ | n. | 偏好、偏愛 |
| thermodynamics | /ˏθɝmodaɪˋnæmɪks/ | n. | 熱力學 |
| awe | /ɔ/ | n. | 敬畏、讚嘆 |
| crave | /krev/ | v. | 渴望、渴求 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`a God-shaped hole`**：「上帝形狀的洞」——常見說法，指人內心對意義／超越性的空缺。
- **`have nothing to do with`**：「跟⋯⋯毫無關係」。
- **`a sense of wholeness / awe`**：`a sense of + 抽象名詞`＝「一種⋯⋯的感覺」（完整感／敬畏感）。
- **`stop fucking about`**（英式粗口）：「別再瞎混、別再鬼混浪費時間」。
- **`tie something into something`**：「把某事串連、扣回到某個主題上」。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`there's a sense that something infinite has been lost`** — `a sense that + 子句` 為同位語子句，補充說明 sense 的內容。
- **`a God-shaped hole in you you're trying to fill`** — 省略關係代名詞的接觸子句：`hole (that) you're trying to fill`。
- **`it's because you feel a sense of wholeness by being around them`** — `by + Ving` 表方法／途徑，「藉由⋯⋯」。
