## 70. 財富最糟的用途：投資而非消費、加倍善待最好的人

### 逐句對照

**主持人:** What about the worst places to spend wealth?
那花錢最糟的地方呢？

**Naval:** What is the old line? "If it flies, floats, or fornicates..."
那句老話怎麼說來著？「凡是會飛的、會浮的、會交配的⋯⋯」

**主持人:** Well, very nice way to change the final F. Very impressive.
嗯，把最後那個 F 開頭的字改得很漂亮嘛。真厲害。

**Naval:** That's the way I heard it. Can't take credit for that.
我聽到的版本就是這樣。這可不能算我的功勞。

**主持人:** I'm pretty sure it's Fox, but yeah.
我蠻確定是 Fox 講的，不過算了。

**Naval:** Yeah. I think that was—maybe it was Felix Dennis.
對。我想那是——也許是 Felix Dennis。

**主持人:** Okay.
好。

**Naval:** Who had that quote. Yeah, he said, "If it flies, floats, or fornicates, rent it." I think the last one was a little too... it's wrong. He didn't have a family, didn't have kids. So, you know, he missed the big one.
就是講那句話的人。對，他說：「凡是會飛的、會浮的、會交配的，用租的就好。」我覺得最後那一項有點太過了⋯⋯那是不對的。他沒有家庭，沒有小孩。所以，你知道的，他錯過了最重要的那一項。

**Naval:** But yeah, there are lots of bad ways to spend money. I believe in investment. I don't believe in consumption. Yes, you're born with a short housing position. You close that out, you get yourself a nice house.
但沒錯，花錢的爛方法有很多。我信奉投資，我不信奉消費。是啦，你一出生就等於背了一個房子的空頭部位，你把它平掉、給自己弄一間好房子。

**Naval:** Get yourself some help to free up your time so you're not doing things that other people can do better. Treat people well. Always overpay and expect the best. Pay them like they're the best and expect the best.
請些幫手來把你的時間釋放出來，這樣你就不用去做那些別人做得更好的事。善待別人。永遠付得比行情高，並期待最好的表現。把他們當成頂尖人才來付錢，然後期待頂尖的成果。

**Naval:** But overall, I think a good use of money is to take risks and build things and do things that other people can't do. Align it with your own unique talent so you can keep delivering to the world. I'm not going to sit idle. I'm not going to retire. That's a waste of whatever time I have left on this earth.
但整體而言，我認為金錢的好用途是去冒險、去打造東西、去做別人做不到的事。把它跟你自己獨一無二的天賦對齊，這樣你才能不斷向世界輸出價值。我不會閒著。我不會退休。那是在浪費我在這世上僅剩的時間。

**Naval:** And if I'm doing something I enjoy, then I'm already in perpetual retirement. Because work is just a set of things you have to do that you don't want to do. So if you want to do it, it's not work.
而如果我在做自己享受的事，那我其實已經處在永久退休的狀態了。因為工作不過是一堆你必須做、卻不想做的事。所以如果你想做，它就不算工作。

**Naval:** There are things that I want to do that don't feel like work. I can put money behind them and use that to instantiate them into reality. And I don't want to say "make the world a better place" because that's too trite. It's more just: create a product that I'm proud of, that wouldn't exist otherwise, that other people will get tremendous value from.
有些我想做的事並不像工作。我可以拿錢在後面撐它們，用錢把它們化為現實。我不想說什麼「讓世界更美好」，因為那太老套了。它更像是：創造一個我引以為傲、若非如此就不會存在、能讓別人得到巨大價值的產品。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| fornicate | /ˋfɔrnəˏket/ | v. | (正式)通姦、交合 |
| consumption | /kənˋsʌmpʃən/ | n. | 消費、消耗 |
| idle | /ˋaɪdl̩/ | adj. | 閒置的、無所事事的 |
| perpetual | /pɚˋpɛtʃʊəl/ | adj. | 永久的、持續不斷的 |
| instantiate | /ɪnˋstænʃɪˏet/ | v. | 具現化、使成為實例 |
| trite | /traɪt/ | adj. | 陳腔濫調的、老套的 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`the old line`**：「那句老話、老說法」，引用眾所周知的諺語時使用。
- **`can't take credit for that`**：「這功勞不能算在我頭上、不是我原創的」。
- **`close out a position`**：金融用語「平倉、了結部位」，此處比喻「解決掉住房這個需求」。
- **`free up your time`**：「把時間空出來、釋放時間」。
- **`sit idle`**：「閒著不動、無所事事」。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`Pay them like they're the best and expect the best.`** — `like + 子句` 口語用法（＝as if），「把他們當作是最好的那樣去付錢」。
- **`work is just a set of things you have to do that you don't want to do`** — 雙重關係子句連續修飾 `things`：先 `you have to do`，再 `that you don't want to do`。
- **`a product ... that wouldn't exist otherwise`** — `otherwise` 表「若非如此、否則」，隱含與現實相反的假設條件。

---

## 71. 財富＝自由去冒險：致富心法是高度情境化的

### 逐句對照

**主持人:** And it's been enabled through wealth, because you're able to take a level of risk that you wouldn't have been able to otherwise.
而這一切之所以成為可能，是靠財富，因為你能承擔一個原本不可能承擔的風險程度。

**Naval:** Exactly. Wealth gives you freedom. It gives you freedom to explore more options. And in my case, it gives me freedom to start businesses without having to ask other people for permission, or to warp my vision based on their desires to make a return, or how they think money should be made.
正是。財富給你自由。它給你自由去探索更多選項。以我而言，它給我自由去創業，不必向別人請求許可，也不必為了迎合他們想賺報酬的欲望、或他們認為錢該怎麼賺的想法，而去扭曲我的願景。

**主持人:** Is there anything that you'd add to the "How to Get Rich" thread? Anything where you thought, "[ __ ], if I could go in and edit and add one more in"?
你會想在那串「如何致富」的推文裡再加點什麼嗎？有沒有哪個瞬間你心想：「該死，要是我能回去編輯、再加一條進去就好了」？

**Naval:** No, there's like 10,000 things. I could talk about that topic forever, to be honest. That thread was so short, so limited, and so crafted in a sense—although I wrote it very spontaneously—it left so much on the cutting room floor that I could just talk about that topic for days.
不，那有大概一萬條。老實說，這個主題我可以講到天荒地老。那串推文非常短、非常受限、某種意義上也非常經過雕琢——雖然我寫得很即興——它捨棄掉的東西多到，光這個主題我就能講上好幾天。

**Naval:** But it's all contextual, right? Business is very, very contextual. You have to look at the particular business and understand what's being done, and why, and how—and then you can tear it apart, or reassemble it properly.
但這一切都是看情境的，對吧？做生意非常非常看情境。你得看那個具體的事業，去理解它在做什麼、為什麼做、怎麼做——然後你才能把它拆解開來，或者把它妥當地重新組裝起來。

**Naval:** And I like to think that that is actually where I have specific knowledge and expertise. My specific knowledge and expertise is not in happiness, not in philosophy. Yes, my life is very hacked to be very unique. But I don't think that's where my specific knowledge is.
而我傾向認為，那才是我真正擁有專門知識與專長的地方。我的專門知識與專長不在快樂，不在哲學。是啦，我的人生被我「破解」得非常獨特。但我不認為那是我專門知識所在之處。

**Naval:** My specific knowledge is in being able to analyze a business, especially a technology business, and take it apart at the seams, and predict in advance what is likely to work and what is not likely to work. Clubhouse notwithstanding.
我的專門知識，在於能夠分析一個事業，尤其是科技事業，把它從接縫處拆開，並事先預測什麼可能成功、什麼可能失敗。Clubhouse 那次除外啦。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| warp | /wɔrp/ | v. | 扭曲、使變形 |
| spontaneously | /spɑnˋtenɪəslɪ/ | adv. | 即興地、自發地 |
| contextual | /kənˋtɛkstʃʊəl/ | adj. | 依情境而定的 |
| reassemble | /ˏriəˋsɛmbl̩/ | v. | 重新組裝 |
| expertise | /ˏɛkspɚˋtiz/ | n. | 專業知識、專長 |
| notwithstanding | /ˏnɑtwɪθˋstændɪŋ/ | prep./adv. | 儘管、除⋯⋯之外 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`leave something on the cutting room floor`**：源自剪接室，「(內容)被剪掉、被捨棄」，指最終沒被收錄的東西。
- **`tear something apart`**：「把某物拆解開來、徹底分析」，也可指嚴厲批評。
- **`take it apart at the seams`**：字面「從接縫處拆開」，比喻「從結構的關鍵接點拆解剖析」。
- **`in advance`**：「事先、預先」。
- **`X notwithstanding`**：正式用語「儘管有 X、X 這個例外不算」，可置於名詞前後。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`a level of risk that you wouldn't have been able to otherwise`** — 第三類條件的省略：`wouldn't have been able to (take) otherwise`，隱含「若非有財富，過去就不可能」。
- **`without having to ask ... or to warp ...`** — `without + 動名詞 having to`，後接兩個並列不定詞 `to ask` 與 `to warp`，表「不必去做⋯⋯也不必去做⋯⋯」。
- **`My specific knowledge is in being able to ...`** — `be in + 動名詞` 表「(專長／重點)在於做某事」。

---

## 72. 多數時候仍會錯，但冪律回報：抽象談財富難在必須永遠成立

### 逐句對照

**Naval:** Because you're still going to be wrong most of the time. It's like playing the lottery, but you know one or two of the ticket's numbers in advance. You only have to be right a few times, or even just once, to get the big score.
因為你大多數時候還是會猜錯。這就像在買樂透，只不過你事先知道彩券上一兩個號碼。你只要對個幾次，甚至只對一次，就能拿到那筆大獎。

**Naval:** You know, Peter Thiel started PayPal, but he made all his money on Facebook, right? And now he's done more since then, obviously. But that was the big winner. And that's true in any power law distribution. Number one is going to return more than two through n put together. Two will return more than three through n put together.
你知道，Peter Thiel 創辦了 PayPal，但他所有的錢都是靠 Facebook 賺的，對吧？當然，自那之後他又做了更多事。但那才是那個大贏家。這在任何冪律分布裡都成立。第一名的回報會超過第二名到第 n 名加起來的總和。第二名的回報又會超過第三名到第 n 名加起來的總和。

**Naval:** You're operating in a highly leveraged intellectual domain, so the outcomes are going to be nonlinear. So I know a lot about that topic, but it's highly contextual. It makes a lot more sense if there's a specific business in front of me, a specific entrepreneur, and I can take that apart.
你是在一個高度槓桿的智識領域裡運作，所以結果會是非線性的。所以這個主題我懂得很多，但它高度依賴情境。如果我面前有一個具體的事業、一個具體的創業家，讓我能把它拆開來看，事情就會清楚得多。

**Naval:** So there are certain companies where I'll say, "Oh, this is not going to work, because you, the entrepreneur, are doing this for the wrong reasons. You're doing A so you can get to B. Just go to B." Or, "You're doing this to make money," when really the person who's doing it because they love the product is going to beat you.
所以有些公司我會說：「喔，這行不通，因為你，這位創業家，是為了錯誤的理由在做。你做 A 只是為了抵達 B。那就直接去 B 吧。」或者：「你是為了賺錢在做這件事。」而真正因為熱愛這個產品而做的人，會把你打敗。

**Naval:** Or you're raising money from the wrong people who are in it for the wrong reasons, or your co-founder is not in it for the right reasons, or you don't have the right kind of co-founder, or your vesting schedule is wrong, or you're starting the business in the wrong place, or you're approaching it from this angle instead of that angle.
或者你是在向錯誤的人募資，那些人抱著錯誤的動機參與；或者你的共同創辦人動機不對；或者你根本沒有對的那種共同創辦人；或者你的股權兌現時程設計錯了；或者你在錯的地方創業；又或者你是從這個角度切入，而不是那個角度。

**Naval:** And of course I'll be wrong too, but I've just seen a lot of data. I have my theories around it, and that's where I feel very comfortable operating.
當然我也會出錯，但我就是看過大量的資料。我對此有我自己的一套理論，而那正是我覺得運作起來非常自在的地方。

**Naval:** The problem is when I have to talk about how to create wealth—and "How to Get Rich" is a clickbait title deliberately—but when I talk about how to create wealth, talking about it in the abstract is very difficult. Because then you just want to speak truth. You have to say the timeless stuff. You have to be right in almost every context, and so it really limits what you can say.
問題在於，當我必須談「如何創造財富」時——「如何致富」是刻意取的釣魚標題——但當我談創造財富，在抽象層次談它就非常困難。因為這時你只想講真話。你必須講那些永恆不變的東西。你必須在幾乎每一種情境下都成立，所以這真的大大限制了你能說的內容。

**主持人:** The lack of specificity makes it—yeah.
缺乏具體性讓它變得——對。

**Naval:** Correct. It's back to philosophy. But if I can get specific about it, that's when the real knowledge could be like a counselor for people.
沒錯。那又回到哲學去了。但如果我能講得夠具體，那時候真正的知識才能像顧問一樣，替人們指點迷津。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| lottery | /ˋlɑtərɪ/ | n. | 樂透、彩券 |
| leveraged | /ˋlɛvərɪdʒd/ | adj. | 槓桿化的、高倍放大的 |
| nonlinear | /nɑnˋlɪnɪɚ/ | adj. | 非線性的 |
| vesting schedule | /ˋvɛstɪŋ ˋskɛdʒʊl/ | n. | 股權兌現時程 |
| clickbait | /ˋklɪkˏbet/ | n. | (誘人點擊的)釣魚標題 |
| specificity | /ˏspɛsəˋfɪsətɪ/ | n. | 具體性、明確性 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`get the big score`**：口語「大賺一筆、拿下大獎」。
- **`power law distribution`**：「冪律分布」，指少數項目佔絕大部分回報的分布型態（贏家通吃）。
- **`two through n`**：「第二名到第 n 名」，`X through Y` 表從 X 到 Y 的連續範圍。
- **`be in it for ...`**：「(參與某事)是為了⋯⋯(動機)」，如 `in it for the money`。
- **`in the abstract`**：「抽象地、在理論層面」，相對於 `in concrete terms`。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`Number one is going to return more than two through n put together.`** — `put together` 為過去分詞片語後置修飾，「(二到 n 名)加總起來」，等同 `... combined`。
- **`the person who's doing it because they love the product is going to beat you`** — 主詞後接關係子句 `who's doing it because ...`，主詞 the person 與主動詞 `is going to beat` 距離拉長，注意主謂一致。
- **`that's when the real knowledge could be like a counselor`** — `that's when ...` 強調句型，用 when 引導名詞子句點出「就是在那個時候」。

---

---

## 73. 哲學推特與不可壓縮的推文：真懂就能從第一性原理重建

### 逐句對照

**Naval:** Part of the reason why I started doing podcasts—and you know this is ego at play, so I'll admit it freely—when I was tweeting, I kind of pioneered philosophy Twitter, if you will, or a certain kind of practical philosophy Twitter.
我開始做 podcast 的部分原因——你知道這裡頭有自我在作祟，我坦白承認——是我在發推特的時候，某種程度上算是開創了「哲學推特」，或者說某種實用主義的哲學推特。

**Naval:** In 140 characters I would try to say something true in an interesting way that was insightful to me at the time. But then that got copied. There's thousands of us now, thousands of people spitting it out, ChatGPT trying to create these things all day long.
在 140 個字元裡，我會試著用一種有趣的方式講出某個真理，那在當時對我來說很有洞見。但後來這被大量複製了，現在有成千上萬個像我這樣的人，成千上萬個人在批量產出這種東西，ChatGPT 也整天在試著生成這些。

**Naval:** Although I like to think that my stuff is incompressible. I'm saying it in the tightest way possible—which is kind of a little failed poetry background.
不過我喜歡這樣想：我寫的東西是不可壓縮的。我已經用最精煉的方式把它說出來了——這大概跟我那點失敗的詩歌底子有關。

**Naval:** But what I realized was, if you truly have a deep understanding of something, then you can talk about it all day long. Then you can rederive everything you need from that understanding. No memorization required.
但我體悟到的是，如果你對某件事有真正深刻的理解，那你就能整天談它。你可以從那份理解裡把你需要的一切重新推導出來，完全不需要背誦。

**Naval:** You can get to it from first principles, and every piece of what you know is like a Lego block that just fits in and forms a steel frame. It's solid. It's locked in there.
你可以從第一性原理抵達它，而你所知道的每一塊都像一塊樂高積木，剛好嵌進去，組成一個鋼架。它很堅固，牢牢地鎖在那裡。

**Naval:** And so on a podcast, I can unload much more deeply about some of these topics. So for example, we can talk about any business you like, but it has to be in context. It has to be real. It has to be an actual problem. Then we can solve it.
所以在 podcast 上，我可以把這些主題挖得更深、講得更透。舉例來說，我們可以聊任何你想聊的生意，但它必須有脈絡、必須是真實的、必須是一個實際的問題，這樣我們才能解決它。

**主持人:** I just really love that heuristic of, if you're having to memorize something, it's because you don't understand it.
我真的很喜歡這個判準：如果你得靠背的，那就是因為你不懂它。

**Naval:** That's right. If you have to memorize something, it's because you don't understand it. And if you understand something, you don't have to memorize it.
沒錯。如果你得背某個東西，那是因為你不理解它；而如果你理解某個東西，你根本不需要背它。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| pioneer | /ˏpaɪəˋnɪr/ | v. | 開創、率先開拓 |
| incompressible | /ˏɪnkəmˋprɛsəbḷ/ | adj. | 不可壓縮的 |
| rederive | /ˏridɪˋraɪv/ | v. | 重新推導 |
| first principles | /fɝst ˋprɪnsəpḷz/ | n. | 第一性原理、基本原理 |
| unload | /ʌnˋlod/ | v. | 傾吐、盡情闡述 |
| heuristic | /hjʊˋrɪstɪk/ | n. | 經驗法則、判準 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`ego at play`**：「自我在作祟」——坦承某個行為背後有虛榮心的成分。
- **`if you will`**：「如果你願意這麼說的話」，插入語，用來對自己的措辭稍作保留。
- **`spit it out`**：字面「吐出來」，此處指「不假思索地大量產出、批量生產」內容。
- **`all day long`**：口語誇飾，「整天、沒完沒了地」。
- **`locked in`**：「牢牢固定、鎖死到位」，形容知識像積木般穩固嵌合。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`if you truly have a deep understanding..., then you can talk about it all day long`** — 第一類條件句（真實條件）：`if + 現在式..., 現在式/can`，陳述普遍成立的因果。
- **`every piece of what you know is like a Lego block that just fits in`** — `what you know` 是名詞子句當 `of` 的受詞；`that just fits in` 是關係子句修飾 `Lego block`。
- **`if you're having to memorize something`** — `be having to` 用進行式強調「當下正被迫、不得不」，比單純 `have to` 更帶情境感。

---

## 74. 聽起來聰明不等於聰明：贏不了 ChatGPT 的記憶，理解與品味才是關鍵

### 逐句對照

**Naval:** Yeah, again, just to sort of call out—a lot of what I tried to do, this redemption arc thing, of "if I sound smart, that's like being smart," right?
對，再一次，我想點破一件事——我過去做的很多事，那種「自我救贖弧線」的心態，就是「如果我聽起來很聰明，那就等於很聰明」，對吧？

**Naval:** You go, "well, ChatGPT has memorized the entire internet." Good luck competing with that. You're not going to beat it in memorization. You're not even going to beat a library at memorization. You're not going to beat any 10 books in memorization.
但你想想，「ChatGPT 已經把整個網際網路背下來了」，祝你好運跟那個比。你在記憶上贏不了它，你連一座圖書館都贏不了，你連隨便十本書都贏不了。

**Naval:** So memorization is not the thing. The value of memorization is going down by the day. It's already so low. Understanding is a thing. Judgment is the thing. Taste is a thing.
所以記憶不是重點。記憶的價值正一天天下滑，它已經低到不行了。理解才是關鍵，判斷力才是關鍵，品味才是關鍵。

**Naval:** And understanding, judgment, taste—these come out of having real problems and then solving them and then finding the commonalities. What is philosophy? You live long enough, you'll be a philosopher.
而理解、判斷、品味——這些都來自於面對真實的問題、解決它們、然後找出當中的共通點。什麼是哲學？你活得夠久，你自然就會成為一個哲學家。

**Naval:** Philosophy is just when you find the hidden generalizable truths among the specific experiences that you've had in life, and then you know how to navigate future specific experiences based on some heuristics, and you create a philosophy around that.
哲學，不過就是你在人生種種具體經驗當中，找出隱藏的、可推廣的真理，然後你就懂得依據一些經驗法則去應對未來的具體處境，並圍繞這些建立起一套哲學。

**Naval:** Any subject pursued deeply enough will eventually lead to philosophy. Mastery in anything, literally anything, will lead you to being a philosopher. You just have to stick with it long enough and generalize the truths back out.
任何一門學問只要鑽得夠深，最終都會通往哲學。對任何事物——真的是任何事物——的精通，都會引領你成為哲學家。你只需要堅持得夠久，再把那些真理歸納推廣出來。

**Naval:** And these are universal truths. It's back to the unity and variety. You can find unity in anything if you go deep enough. And that's why the trite stuff, unfortunately, sort of keeps coming back around. You're like, "well, look, this is cliché for a reason."
而這些是普世的真理。這又回到「統一與多樣」的主題。只要你挖得夠深，你能在任何事物裡找到統一性。這也是為什麼那些老掉牙的話很不幸地總是一再繞回來，你會發現「你看，這會變成陳腔濫調是有原因的」。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| memorization | /ˏmɛmərəˋzeʃən/ | n. | 記憶、背誦 |
| judgment | /ˋdʒʌdʒmənt/ | n. | 判斷力 |
| commonality | /ˏkɑməˋnælətɪ/ | n. | 共通點、共性 |
| generalizable | /ˋdʒɛnərəˏlaɪzəbḷ/ | adj. | 可推廣的、可歸納的 |
| mastery | /ˋmæstərɪ/ | n. | 精通、熟練掌握 |
| cliché | /kliˋʃe/ | n. | 陳腔濫調 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`call out`**：此處指「點破、指出（自己的心態）」。
- **`redemption arc`**：源自敘事用語「救贖弧線」，指角色從缺陷走向改過的歷程。
- **`good luck competing with that`**：反諷語氣，「你要跟那個比，祝你好運」＝根本比不過。
- **`by the day`**：「一天天地」，強調持續的變化趨勢。
- **`come back around`**：「繞一圈又回來」，指某想法反覆出現。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`You're not going to beat it in memorization.`** — `be going to` 表推斷性的未來否定，語氣近於「你注定贏不了」。
- **`Any subject pursued deeply enough will eventually lead to philosophy.`** — `pursued deeply enough` 是過去分詞片語後位修飾 `subject`，等同 `that is pursued deeply enough`。
- **`this is cliché for a reason`** — `for a reason`＝「不是沒有原因的」，常用來替看似陳腐的說法辯護。

## 75. 科學拓展哲學邊界：道德哲學會演進（奴隸制、嬰兒感不到痛）

### 逐句對照

**Naval:** It's cliché for reasons. But sometimes you learn new things. Sometimes you do figure out new things too—even in philosophy. For example, as science has advanced, it's actually expanded our boundaries of philosophy.
它變成陳腔濫調是有原因的。但有時候你確實會學到新東西，有時候你真的會弄懂新的事情——即使在哲學裡也是。比方說，隨著科學的進展，它其實拓展了我們哲學的邊界。

**Naval:** When we used to think that the earth was the center of the universe, you would actually have a different philosophical outlook than when you think the universe is vast and we're infinitesimally small.
當我們以前認為地球是宇宙的中心時，你的哲學觀，會跟你認為宇宙浩瀚、而我們渺小到微不足道時，截然不同。

**Naval:** The same way, if you think nature is driven by angels and demons and gods, versus if there are laws of physics that are computable and understandable—that will lead you to a different philosophical outlook.
同樣地，如果你認為大自然是由天使、惡魔和諸神所驅動，相對於你認為存在著可計算、可理解的物理定律——這會導向一種不同的哲學觀。

**Naval:** If you think knowledge is something passed down from above and through generations, versus something created on the fly and then tested against reality—that will lead you to a different philosophical outlook.
如果你認為知識是由上天、由世代相傳下來的，相對於知識是即時創造出來、再拿到現實中去檢驗的——這會導向一種不同的哲學觀。

**Naval:** If you think humans are created by God, as opposed to humans evolved from some unicellular organism—yeah, it still doesn't solve the original problem, who created that? But at least it takes you further down the road.
如果你認為人類是由上帝創造的，相對於人類是從某種單細胞生物演化而來——是啦，這仍然沒解決最原始的問題，那又是誰創造了那個？但至少它帶著你往前走得更遠一點。

**Naval:** Even sim theory is an attempt at reformulating philosophy based on what we know about computers, even though it kind of leads to a lot of the same conclusions as, you know, a creator. But it is at least philosophy that is informed by technology and by science.
就連「模擬理論」也是一種嘗試，想根據我們對電腦的認識來重構哲學，儘管它某種程度上導向的結論跟「造物主」差不多。但它至少是一種受科技與科學所啟發的哲學。

**Naval:** So philosophy can also evolve—moral philosophy evolves, right? There was a time when practically every conquering culture practiced slavery. Now almost all cultures abhor slavery. That's moral philosophy having evolved.
所以哲學也會演進——道德哲學會演進，對吧？曾經幾乎每一個征服型的文化都實行奴隸制，而現在幾乎所有文化都厭惡奴隸制。這就是道德哲學演進的結果。

**Naval:** This sounds too ludicrous to be true, and I don't know if it fully is, but there was a fairly large group of doctors, based on studies, who believed until the 1980s that babies couldn't feel pain.
這聽起來荒謬到不像是真的，我也不確定它是否完全屬實，但曾經有一大群醫生，根據當時的研究，一直到 1980 年代都相信嬰兒感覺不到疼痛。

**Naval:** So even to this day, I think circumcision is done without anesthesia, under the theory that very young children, babies, don't feel pain. And that's ludicrous. There was a study that came out in the '80s that said, "no, no, no, they do feel pain," and it's like, "oh yeah, of course."
所以直到今天，我想割包皮手術都還是在沒有麻醉的情況下進行，理由就是那套「非常年幼的孩子、嬰兒感覺不到痛」的理論。這太荒謬了。80 年代出現了一份研究說「不不不，他們確實會感到痛」，那感覺就是「喔對啊，這不是當然的嗎」。

**Naval:** So people can be stuck in bad philosophical traps for a long period of time. So even philosophy can make progress.
所以人們可能長時間困在糟糕的哲學陷阱裡。所以說，就連哲學也是會進步的。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| outlook | /ˋaʊtˏlʊk/ | n. | 觀點、看法 |
| infinitesimally | /ˏɪnfɪnəˋtɛsəmḷɪ/ | adv. | 微乎其微地 |
| unicellular | /ˏjunɪˋsɛljəlɚ/ | adj. | 單細胞的 |
| abhor | /əbˋhɔr/ | v. | 厭惡、憎惡 |
| ludicrous | /ˋludɪkrəs/ | adj. | 荒謬可笑的 |
| anesthesia | /ˏænəsˋθiʒə/ | n. | 麻醉 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`on the fly`**：「即時、臨場、當下」，指邊做邊生成，而非事先備好。
- **`test against reality`**：「拿到現實中檢驗」，強調以事實驗證想法。
- **`take you further down the road`**：「帶你在這條路上走得更遠」，指雖未終結問題但有推進。
- **`too ludicrous to be true`**：`too...to...` 結構，「荒謬到不像真的」。
- **`no, no, no`**：口語三連否定，強調推翻先前錯誤結論的語氣。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`you would actually have a different philosophical outlook than when you think...`** — `would` 表假設情境下的結果；`than` 引導比較，對比兩種世界觀。
- **`as science has advanced, it's actually expanded our boundaries`** — `as` 引導時間／伴隨子句「隨著⋯⋯」，主句用現在完成式承接結果。
- **`That's moral philosophy having evolved.`** — `having evolved` 為完成式動名詞（意義上主詞是 moral philosophy），濃縮表達「道德哲學已經演進了這件事」。

---

## 76. 化解古老悖論：在被提問的層次作答（意義、自由意志）

### 逐句對照

**Naval:** As an example, one of the realizations that I had—and this is thanks to David Deutsch and my friend James Pierce, and also thinking it through a little bit—is that there are these timeless old questions that we run into where the answers seem like paradoxes. So we stop thinking about them.
舉個例子，我有一個體悟——這要歸功於 David Deutsch、我的朋友 James Pierce，以及我自己把它稍微想通了一點——就是有些永恆的老問題，我們一碰到，答案看起來就像悖論，於是我們就不再去想它了。

**Naval:** So an example is free will. Do you have free will? Or, does anything matter? Is there a meaning to life? And we get stuck in them. Because, for example, is there a meaning to life?
比方說「自由意志」就是一個例子。你有自由意志嗎？或者，任何事情有意義嗎？人生有意義嗎？我們就卡在這些問題裡。因為，舉例來說，人生有意義嗎？

**Naval:** Yes, life has a meaning, because you're right here. You create your own meaning. This moment has all the meaning you could imagine. It's all the meaning there is. On the other hand, you're going to die. It all goes to zero. Heat death. The universe has no meaning. So which one is it?
有，人生是有意義的，因為你就在這裡。你創造你自己的意義。這一刻擁有你所能想像的一切意義，它就是全部的意義。但另一方面，你終將一死，一切歸零，熱寂，宇宙毫無意義。所以到底是哪一個？

**Naval:** The reason it seems paradoxical is because you're asking the question of a human here and now, at a certain scale and a certain time, and then you're answering it from the viewpoint of the universe over infinite time. So you pull the trick. You switch the level at which you're answering the question.
它之所以看起來矛盾，是因為你是站在「此時此地、某個尺度、某個時間點的一個人」去問這個問題，然後你卻是從「橫跨無限時間的宇宙」的視角去回答它。所以你耍了個花招，你偷換了回答問題所在的層次。

**Naval:** And questions should be answered at the level at which they're asked. So if you ask the question, is there meaning? You, Chris, are asking that question.
而問題應該在它被提出的那個層次上作答。所以如果你問「有意義嗎？」——是你，Chris，在問這個問題。

**主持人:** Yes.
對。

**Naval:** To Chris, there is meaning. There's meaning right here. This is the meaning. You can interpret any meaning you want onto it. Don't ask the question as Chris and then answer it as God or as the universe. That's the trick you're playing. That's why it seems paradoxical.
對 Chris 來說，是有意義的。意義就在這裡，這就是意義，你可以把任何你想要的意義加諸其上。別用 Chris 的身分提問，卻用上帝或宇宙的身分去回答。那就是你在耍的花招，那就是它看起來矛盾的原因。

**Naval:** The same way, you can say, "do I have free will?" People debate free will all day long. The question is answered at the wrong frame. So they ask, "do I as an individual have free will?" Hell yeah, I have free will. My mind-body system can't predict what I'm going to do next.
同樣地，你可以問「我有自由意志嗎？」人們沒完沒了地辯論自由意志。問題被放在錯誤的框架裡回答了。他們問的是「我作為一個個體，有自由意志嗎？」當然有，我有自由意志。我的身心系統無法預測我下一步要做什麼。

**Naval:** The universe is infinitely complex. I'm making a choice in my mind and I'm doing something. There's my free will. So answer at the level at which you were asked. Of course I have free will, because I feel like I have free will, and I treat you like you have free will, and you treat me like I have free will. We have free will.
宇宙是無限複雜的。我在腦中做出選擇，然後我採取行動，這就是我的自由意志。所以要在你被提問的那個層次上回答。我當然有自由意志，因為我感覺我有自由意志，而且我把你當成有自由意志來對待，你也把我當成有自由意志來對待。我們有自由意志。

**Naval:** The problem then is you start trying to answer the question as if you're the universe. You're like, "well, on the universal scale, big bang, particle collisions—no one makes any choices. How could you be any different than what the universe wants you to be? It's all one block universe. So you don't have free will."
接著問題出在你開始試著用「彷彿你就是宇宙」的角度去回答。你會說「唔，在宇宙尺度上，大爆炸、粒子碰撞——沒有人做出任何選擇。你怎麼可能不是宇宙要你成為的樣子？這是一整個『塊狀宇宙』。所以你沒有自由意志。」

**Naval:** Don't answer the question at the level at which it wasn't asked. So if God asked the question, is there free will? No, there is no free will. If the universe asks the question, there is no free will. But if an individual asks the question right now, then yes, there is free will.
別在一個「問題並非被提出的層次」上去回答它。所以如果是上帝在問「有自由意志嗎？」——沒有，沒有自由意志。如果是宇宙在問，沒有自由意志。但如果是一個個體此刻在問，那麼，有的，有自由意志。

**Naval:** So a lot of these paradoxes resolve themselves—philosophical paradoxes that people have been struggling with since the beginning of time—when you just realize that you're answering them at a scale and time different than they were asked.
所以很多這類悖論會自行化解——那些人們從遠古以來一直苦苦掙扎的哲學悖論——只要你意識到，你是在一個跟它被提出時不同的尺度與時間上去回答它。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| paradox | /ˋpærəˏdɑks/ | n. | 悖論、矛盾 |
| free will | /fri wɪl/ | n. | 自由意志 |
| viewpoint | /ˋvjuˏpɔɪnt/ | n. | 視角、觀點 |
| frame | /frem/ | n. | 框架、參照系 |
| collision | /kəˋlɪʒən/ | n. | 碰撞 |
| resolve | /rɪˋzɑlv/ | v. | 化解、解決 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`run into`**：「碰到、遇上」（問題、狀況）。
- **`pull the trick` / `the trick you're playing`**：「耍花招、玩把戲」，此處指偷換提問層次。
- **`hell yeah`**：口語強烈肯定，「當然有、太有了」。
- **`all day long`**：此處引申為「沒完沒了地（爭論）」。
- **`goes to zero`**：「歸零、化為烏有」。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`questions should be answered at the level at which they're asked`** — `the level at which...` 為「介系詞 + 關係代名詞」結構，等同 `the level that they're asked at`，較正式。
- **`How could you be any different than what the universe wants you to be?`** — 修辭問句表「不可能有別的樣子」；`any different than` 為口語比較用法（正式作 different from）。
- **`Don't answer the question at the level at which it wasn't asked.`** — 否定祈使句 + 帶否定的關係子句，強調「別在錯誤層次作答」。

---

## 77. 改變過的想法：不再那麼放任、文化與宗教解決協調問題

### 逐句對照

**主持人:** Speaking of updating beliefs, is there anything that you've changed your mind around recently?
說到更新信念，最近有沒有什麼是你改變了想法的？

**Naval:** Very recently. I mean, all the time. But are you talking about like philosophical, existential things, or like technological things?
最近才改的。我是說，其實一直都在改。不過你是指哲學性的、存在性的那些，還是科技方面的？

**主持人:** Philosophical, existential things, or anything that comes to mind—if there's anything front of mind where you go, "ah, yeah, that's a pretty big OS update."
哲學性、存在性的，或任何你想到的都行——如果有什麼是浮現在腦海最前面、讓你覺得「啊對，這是一次相當大的作業系統更新」的。

**Naval:** Yeah, I'm less laissez-faire than I used to be on a societal level. I think that culture and religion are good cooperating systems for humans. And so if you want to operate in a high-trust society, you need to have sets of rules that people need to follow and obey so they get along—even if one-size-fits-all doesn't work for everybody.
嗯，在社會層面上，我不像以前那麼放任了。我認為文化和宗教對人類來說是很好的協作系統。所以如果你想在一個高信任的社會裡運作，你就需要有一套人們必須遵守服從的規則，好讓大家能和睦相處——即使「一體適用」的做法對每個人不見得都管用。

**主持人:** Moved up a little bit from libertarian.
從自由意志主義往上挪了一點。

**Naval:** Yeah. I think pure libertarians get outcompeted and die, right? They get overrun, because they're every man for himself.
對。我認為純粹的自由意志主義者會在競爭中落敗、消亡，對吧？他們會被壓垮，因為他們是各人自掃門前雪。

**主持人:** They can't coordinate.
他們無法協調合作。

**Naval:** They can't coordinate, exactly. So, the coordination problems, right? Culture exists to solve fundamental coordination problems. Religion solves coordination problems. Ethnicity solves coordination problems, historically.
他們無法協調，正是如此。所以，這就是協調問題，對吧？文化的存在，是為了解決根本的協調問題。宗教解決協調問題。從歷史上看，族群認同也解決協調問題。

**Naval:** And when you break down those coordination systems too fast and don't replace them with anything else, you get societal breakdown. So you can have very malfunctioning societies. Go to Japan versus go to any western city, and you can see the difference between a culture that's working and a culture that's not.
而當你把那些協調系統拆解得太快、又沒有用別的東西去取代它們，你就會得到社會的崩解。於是你會看到運作嚴重失靈的社會。去日本，對比去任何一座西方城市，你就能看出「運作正常的文化」和「運作失常的文化」之間的差別。

**Naval:** So I think that's a broader set of things that I've changed my mind on quite a fair bit. I used to be much more laissez-faire on that stuff, let's put it that way.
所以我想這是一整組我改變了相當多想法的東西。以前我在這些事情上放任得多得多，姑且這麼說吧。

**Naval:** What else? On child raising, I've gotten a lot looser. I'm still not completely laissez-faire, but I've much more realized, like, kids are going to be kids, and you kind of let them do their thing.
還有什麼？在養小孩這件事上，我變得寬鬆很多。我還沒有到完全放任，但我更加體認到，孩子就是孩子，你多少得讓他們做自己的事。

**主持人:** Is it Taleb that has the ascending levels of anarchism versus conservatism? Is that his insight? Like, at the local level I'm this... It seems like you've gone the other way. It's like, at the child level I'm an anarchist, and at the societal level I'm a conservative.
是 Taleb 提出那個「隨層級遞升，從無政府主義到保守主義」的說法嗎？那是他的洞見嗎？就像，在地方層級我是這樣⋯⋯而你似乎走了相反的方向。像是在孩子這一層我是無政府主義者，而在社會這一層我是保守主義者。

**Naval:** No, he was quoting somebody else, some brothers—I forget which ones—but he was making the point eloquently, as he often does. That at the family, local level, he's a communist. At the family level, you're a communist. At maybe the extended family level, you're a socialist. At the local level, you're kind of a democrat, and so on, until at the federal level, you're a libertarian.
不是，他是在引用別人的話，某對兄弟——我忘了是哪一對——但他一如往常地把那個論點講得很漂亮。就是說在家庭、地方這一層，他是個共產主義者。在家庭層級，你是共產主義者；也許在大家族層級，你是社會主義者；在地方層級，你算是個民主派；以此類推，一直到聯邦層級，你是個自由意志主義者。

**主持人:** So you've done it the other way. You're being a libertarian with the kids and you're being a religious conservative societally.
所以你是反過來做的。你對孩子當一個自由意志主義者，而在社會層面當一個宗教保守派。

**Naval:** No, that's a funny way of looking at it. I don't know if the scale is that simple.
不，那是個有趣的看法。我不確定這個尺度有那麼單純。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| laissez-faire | /ˏlɛseˋfɛr/ | adj. | 放任主義的、不干預的 |
| libertarian | /ˏlɪbɚˋtɛrɪən/ | n. | 自由意志主義者 |
| coordination | /koˏɔrdṇˋeʃən/ | n. | 協調、統合 |
| ethnicity | /ɛθˋnɪsətɪ/ | n. | 族群、族裔 |
| malfunctioning | /mælˋfʌŋkʃənɪŋ/ | adj. | 運作失靈的 |
| eloquently | /ˋɛləkwəntlɪ/ | adv. | 雄辯地、有說服力地 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`change your mind around`**：「改變對某事的想法」，口語常加 around／on。
- **`OS update`**：科技比喻，「作業系統更新」＝認知框架的重大升級。
- **`every man for himself`**：「各顧各的、人人自保」。
- **`kids are going to be kids`**：「孩子就是孩子（會有孩子的樣子）」，表接納天性。
- **`let's put it that way`**：「姑且這麼說吧」，緩和或收束語氣。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`I'm less laissez-faire than I used to be`** — `less...than...` 比較級，搭配 `used to be` 對比過去與現在。
- **`when you break down those systems too fast and don't replace them..., you get societal breakdown`** — `when` 條件／時間子句 + 主句現在式，陳述普遍因果。
- **`I don't know if the scale is that simple.`** — `if` 引導名詞子句表「是否」；`that + 形容詞` 口語程度副詞用法，「有那麼⋯⋯」。

## 78. 現代 AI 是自然語言電腦：無創造力、非 AGI、ASI 是幻想

### 逐句對照

**Naval:** What else have I changed my mind on? I mean, I think modern AI is really cool, but I think these are natural language computers. They're starting to show evidence of kind of reasoning at some levels, but I don't think they do creativity.
我還改變了什麼想法？我是說，我覺得現代 AI 真的很酷，但我認為這些是「自然語言電腦」。它們開始在某些層面顯露出某種推理的跡象，但我不認為它們具備創造力。

**Naval:** One of my favorite takes on that is from Dwarkesh Patel. He says, if you gave any human on the planet 0.0001% of the consumption that an LLM has—any LLM—they would have come up with thousands of new ideas.
關於這一點，我最喜歡的觀點之一來自 Dwarkesh Patel。他說，如果你給地球上任何一個人，只給他一個 LLM 所吸收內容量的 0.0001%——任何一個 LLM——他都會想出好幾千個新點子。

**Naval:** Give me one new idea, one fundamental new idea, that's been generated.
給我一個新點子，一個由它生成的、根本性的新點子（看看）。

**Naval:** Yeah, like, I'm big into poetry. Every poem ever written by an LLM is garbage. I think even their fiction writing is terrible. Even the new GPT-4.5—with all due respect to Sam and crew—I think they're terrible, terrible writers.
對，比方說，我很熱衷詩歌。LLM 寫過的每一首詩都是垃圾。我覺得連它們的小說寫作也很糟。即使是新的 GPT-4.5——恕我對 Sam 和團隊直言——我認為它們是糟糕透頂的寫手。

**Naval:** I find them really bad at summarizing. They're really good at extrapolating paperwork, but they're very bad at actually distilling the essence of something and what's important. They don't have opinions or a point of view. But they're still unbelievably powerful breakthroughs.
我發現它們很不擅長摘要。它們很擅長把文書工作往外擴寫，但它們非常不擅長真正提煉出一件事的本質、以及什麼才是重點。它們沒有意見，也沒有觀點。但它們仍然是強得不可思議的突破。

**Naval:** They solve search. They solve natural language computing. They make English a programming language. They solve driving. They solve simple coding and backup coding. They solve translation. They solve transcription. They are a fundamental breakthrough in computing.
它們解決了搜尋。它們解決了自然語言運算。它們讓英文成為一種程式語言。它們解決了駕駛。它們解決了簡單的程式編寫和輔助程式編寫。它們解決了翻譯，解決了轉錄。它們是運算領域一項根本性的突破。

**Naval:** It is a different way to program a computer. Rather than you explicitly speak its language and write the code and then run the data through it, you just run enough data through it until it figures out how to write the program. That's huge.
這是一種給電腦編程的全新方式。不再是你明確地講它的語言、寫出程式碼、然後把資料丟進去跑，而是你把足夠的資料餵進去，直到它自己搞懂怎麼寫出那個程式。這很了不起。

**Naval:** But are they AGI? Not yet. And I don't see a direct path from here to there. Maybe we'll have to solve a few more problems before that happens. And I think ASI is a fantasy. I don't think there's any such thing as artificial super intelligence, where it has some kind of intelligence that humans can't fathom.
但它們是 AGI（通用人工智慧）嗎？還不是。而且我看不到一條從這裡直達那裡的路徑。也許在那之前我們還得先解決幾個問題。至於 ASI（超級人工智慧），我認為是個幻想。我不認為存在所謂「超級人工智慧」這種東西——那種擁有人類無法理解的某種智能的東西。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| reasoning | /ˋrizn̩ɪŋ/ | n. | 推理 |
| extrapolate | /ɪkˋstræpəˏlet/ | v. | 外推、據已知往外擴 |
| distill | /dɪˋstɪl/ | v. | 提煉、萃取（精華） |
| breakthrough | /ˋbrekˏθru/ | n. | 突破 |
| transcription | /trænˋskrɪpʃən/ | n. | 轉錄、聽打成文字 |
| fathom | /ˋfæðəm/ | v. | 理解、看透 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`take`**（名詞）：口語「觀點、看法」，`my favorite take` ＝我最愛的一種見解。
- **`big into ...`**：「非常熱衷於⋯⋯」。
- **`with all due respect`**：「恕我直言」，禮貌地引出負評。
- **`run data through it`**：「把資料餵進去跑」，機器學習口語。
- **`there's no such thing as ...`**：「根本不存在⋯⋯這種東西」。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`if you gave any human ... they would have come up with thousands of new ideas`** — 混合條件句：`if + 過去式`（假設現在）搭配 `would have + p.p.`（假設結果），口語中常見的鬆散用法。
- **`Rather than you explicitly speak its language..., you just run enough data through it`** — `rather than + 子句` 對比兩種做法，`until` 引導結果子句。
- **`I don't think there's any such thing as ...`** — 否定移前（`I don't think` 而非 `I think there isn't`），英文習慣把否定放在主要動詞。

---

## 79. 非 AI 末日論者：另一種智能、幻覺使其無法用於關鍵任務

### 逐句對照

**主持人:** Okay. Yeah, it seems like—I don't know if you're from the Bostrom camp or whatever.
好。嗯，聽起來像是——我不確定你是不是 Bostrom（末日）那一派的。

**Naval:** No, I'm not an AI doomer. I think that's such a flawed line of reasoning. But let's say you came out of the LessWrong, Slate Star Codex world, and there was this sort of lineage: from computers, and AI gets more powerful, more powerful, more powerful, and then you end up with AGI, ASI.
不，我不是 AI 末日論者。我覺得那是一套很有瑕疵的推理。不過假設你是從 LessWrong、Slate Star Codex 那個圈子出來的，那裡有一種脈絡：從電腦出發，AI 越來越強、越來越強、越來越強，最後你就走到 AGI、ASI。

**主持人:** And it seems like LLMs have been this sort of orthogonal move from that. Are you saying you don't believe they are a step on that? It's kind of a bit of a different branch.
而 LLM 看起來像是相對於那條路徑的一次「正交」移動。你是說你不相信它們是那條路上的一步嗎？它比較像是分岔出去的另一條支線。

**Naval:** I think Stephen Wolfram puts it better: it's a different form of intelligence. It's like if you see a jaguar in the jungle, it has a different form of intelligence. Like, a plant has a form of intelligence, how it can photosynthesize and grow. It's a different form of intelligence.
我覺得 Stephen Wolfram 說得更好：它是另一種形式的智能。就像你在叢林裡看到一隻美洲豹，牠有另一種形式的智能。又像是一株植物也有一種形式的智能，看牠怎麼行光合作用、怎麼生長。那是另一種形式的智能。

**Naval:** Intelligence—again, like love or like happiness—is this overloaded word that means many things to many people. But by my definition, where the true test is you get what you want out of life: it doesn't even have a life. It doesn't even want anything. It's a different thing.
「智能」——就像「愛」或「快樂」一樣——是個負載過重的詞，對不同的人意味著不同的東西。但按照我的定義，真正的檢驗標準是「你能從人生中得到你想要的」：它連生命都沒有，它甚至什麼都不想要。它是另一種東西。

**Naval:** I do think it's unbelievably useful. I'm glad it exists. You don't see it much yet in large-scale production systems replacing humans, because of this tendency to hallucinate. So you can't put it into anything mission-critical.
我確實認為它有用得不可思議。我很慶幸它存在。你目前還不太會在大規模的正式生產系統裡看到它取代人類，因為它有這種「產生幻覺」的傾向。所以你沒辦法把它放進任何攸關成敗的關鍵任務裡。

**主持人:** Confidently wrong one time out of 10.
十次裡有一次會信心滿滿地出錯。

**Naval:** Correct. And it doesn't even know when it's wrong. Maybe they'll get that one out of 10 down to one out of 100. But you'll kind of always want human oversight for critical things.
沒錯。而且它甚至不知道自己什麼時候錯了。也許他們會把那個「十分之一」壓到「百分之一」。但對於關鍵的事情，你多少總會希望有人在旁邊把關。

**Naval:** I always feel so bitter—I'm petty sometimes. My less economical version is petty, and I always want to teach it a lesson if it gets something wrong. Like, "how the [beep] —no, you were so confident." I'm treating it... but I'm anthropomorphizing. It doesn't have a point of view.
我總是覺得很不爽——我有時候很小心眼。我那個比較不理性的版本很小心眼，只要它答錯了我就想給它一點教訓。像是「搞什麼——不，你剛剛明明那麼有信心」。我在把它當人對待⋯⋯但我這是在擬人化，它其實沒有觀點。

**Naval:** And they are going to get a lot better. They might get to the point where the error rates are so low that you can put them into certain bounded problems—like self-driving, I think, will be solved completely, because it's a bounded problem. Cars don't go off-road and drive through houses.
而且它們會變得好非常多。它們可能會進步到錯誤率低到，你能把它們放進某些「有邊界的問題」裡——比方說自動駕駛，我認為會被徹底解決，因為那是個有邊界的問題。車子不會開離道路、直接撞穿房子。

**Naval:** And the same way, certain kinds of coding—the creative side of coding, I think, doesn't go away. If anything, programmers get even more leverage and more powerful. And rather than computing replacing programmers, programmers use AI to replace everybody else.
同樣地，某些類型的程式編寫——編程當中創造性的那一面，我認為不會消失。如果有什麼變化，那就是程式設計師會擁有更大的槓桿、更強的能力。與其說是運算取代了程式設計師，不如說是程式設計師用 AI 去取代其他所有人。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| doomer | /ˋdumɚ/ | n. | 末日論者、悲觀主義者 |
| orthogonal | /ɔrˋθɑgənḷ/ | adj. | 正交的、彼此獨立的 |
| photosynthesize | /ˏfotoˋsɪnθəˏsaɪz/ | v. | 行光合作用 |
| hallucinate | /həˋlusn̩ˏet/ | v. | 產生幻覺（AI 亂編） |
| anthropomorphize | /ˏænθrəpəˋmɔrfaɪz/ | v. | 擬人化 |
| bounded | /ˋbaʊndɪd/ | adj. | 有界限的、受限的 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`from the ... camp`**：「屬於⋯⋯陣營／派別」。
- **`overloaded word`**：「負載過重的詞」，指一字被賦予太多不同含義。
- **`mission-critical`**：「攸關成敗的、關鍵任務級的」。
- **`teach it a lesson`**：「給它一點教訓」。
- **`if anything`**：「要說有什麼變化的話，反倒是⋯⋯」，用來提出相反或加強的看法。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`the error rates are so low that you can put them into ...`** — `so + 形容詞 + that...` 結果句型，「如此⋯⋯以致於⋯⋯」。
- **`rather than computing replacing programmers, programmers use AI to ...`** — `rather than + 動名詞（replacing）` 對比，帶意義上主詞 `computing`。
- **`Confidently wrong one time out of 10.`** — 省略句（省 be 動詞），口語中把 `It's confidently wrong...` 直接濃縮成形容詞片語。

---

## 80. Tesla vs Waymo、生育率下降不需刻意對抗

### 逐句對照

**主持人:** On Tesla versus Waymo, would you bet on software or hardware for self-driving?
在 Tesla 對上 Waymo 這件事上，談到自動駕駛，你會押注在軟體還是硬體？

**Naval:** Yeah. I think Tesla's in the stronger, longer-term position, but it's hard to argue with what's working right now, and Waymo is working right now. So I would not underestimate them, because there's a learning curve you go through when you actually deploy something, and Waymo is way ahead in that regard.
嗯。我認為 Tesla 處在更強、更長線的位置，但你很難去反駁「當下正在運作的東西」，而 Waymo 現在就正在運作。所以我不會低估他們，因為當你真正把一個東西部署上線時，會經歷一段學習曲線，而 Waymo 在這方面領先很多。

**Naval:** But Tesla's camera-only approach, if it works, is superior. It's much more scalable, and Tesla knows how to print cars—they can just mass-manufacture cars. But I think they'll both be around. They'll both be fine. It's everybody else who doesn't have a self-driving vehicle that's screwed.
但 Tesla 那套「純攝影鏡頭」的路線，如果行得通，是更優越的。它的可擴展性強得多，而且 Tesla 懂得怎麼「印車」——他們可以直接大規模量產汽車。不過我認為他們兩家都會存活下來，都會過得不錯。真正完蛋的，是其他所有沒有自駕車的人。

**主持人:** You mentioned kids there, and you had a tweet that said, "I'm not convinced that declining fertility needs to be proactively fought."
你剛提到孩子，你有一則推特寫道：「我並不認為生育率下降需要被主動去對抗。」

**Naval:** I forgot that one.
我忘了那一則了。

**主持人:** You're going to have to—I dug deep. Why?
你得回想一下——我可是挖得很深。為什麼？

**Naval:** Well, think back—what was it, 30 years ago, 20 years ago? Everybody was saying overpopulation of the earth is going to be a problem. A Malthusian ending—we're going to have too many people. And now all of a sudden we're going to have too few people. So part of it is just the doomerism meme is always alive and well, right? Or it just gets repackaged.
這樣想，回想一下——是多久前，30 年前、20 年前？大家都在說地球人口過剩會是個問題。一個馬爾薩斯式的結局——我們會有太多人。而現在突然間，我們又要人太少了。所以部分原因就是，末日論這個迷因永遠活得好好的，對吧？或者說它只是被重新包裝了一遍。

**Naval:** Yeah. "We're running out of oil." "We have too much oil." "The world is cooling." "The world is warming." There's always something to scream about. "The world is ending." "There's no progress in technology." "AI is going to blow up the world." So people tend to overdo it in both directions.
對啊。「我們的石油要用光了。」「我們的石油太多了。」「世界在變冷。」「世界在變熱。」永遠都有東西可以尖叫。「世界要毀滅了。」「科技毫無進步。」「AI 會把世界炸掉。」所以人們往往在兩個方向上都做過頭。

**Naval:** Now, what is the actual fertility problem? Well, people are having fewer kids. Are they having fewer kids because there's a disease? Was there a virus? Did they lose their fertility—the microplastics in the testicles? No, people are having fewer kids because they're choosing to have fewer kids.
那麼，真正的生育率問題到底是什麼？嗯，人們生得比較少。他們生得比較少，是因為有什麼疾病嗎？有病毒嗎？他們喪失生育能力了嗎——睪丸裡的微塑膠之類的？不是，人們生得比較少，是因為他們選擇少生。

**Naval:** Women have gotten emancipation, independence in the workforce, and they're making more money. People don't need kids as insurance policies, so they have fewer kids. Maybe they're living hedonistic lives—God bless them. They want to have more fun, they want to have fewer kids. I don't see the act of choosing to have fewer kids as a problem.
女性獲得了解放、在職場上的獨立，而且她們賺得更多了。人們不再需要把孩子當成保險，所以他們少生。也許他們過著享樂主義的生活——祝福他們。他們想多點樂子、想少生孩子。我不認為「選擇少生孩子」這個行為本身是個問題。

**Naval:** Okay, so let's move one level up. It's because of retirees. It's because a large percentage of the population is essentially retiring at the guaranteed age of 65 or 70, thanks to social security. And so they need other people to pay for it. They need more workers in the workforce. And if the workforce is shrinking, then you have a small number of people supporting a large number of retirees.
好，那我們往上提一個層次。問題出在退休人口。因為很大比例的人口，靠著社會保險，基本上都在被保證的 65 歲或 70 歲退休了。於是他們需要別人來替他們買單，他們需要勞動力市場裡有更多工作者。而如果勞動力在萎縮，那你就會落到「少數人在供養一大群退休人口」的局面。

**Naval:** And in democracies, you can't take pensions away—the voters vote you out. So they slowly strangle the economy. So what do you do? Then you have a bunch of immigration, and then the whole culture changes. You end up in a low-trust society, and people start fighting over limited resources.
而在民主國家裡，你沒辦法把退休金拿掉——選民會把你投下台。於是他們慢慢地把經濟勒死。那你該怎麼辦？接著你就會引入大量移民，然後整個文化就變了。你最後落到一個低信任的社會，人們開始為有限的資源爭鬥。

**主持人:** So you end up in kind of this trap where the low fertility rate is upstream of the downstream problems that are cultural and societal.
所以你最後陷進一種陷阱：低生育率位在上游，而它下游衍生出的，是那些文化與社會層面的問題。

**Naval:** But I'm not sure you're going to solve that by making people have more kids. How are you going to meme them into having more kids? And I'm not even sure it's necessarily a problem, because keep in mind, you have more resources now, you have less of a burden.
但我不確定你能靠「逼人們多生孩子」來解決那個問題。你要怎麼用迷因洗腦他們去多生？而且我甚至不確定它必然是個問題，因為別忘了，你現在擁有更多資源、負擔更輕。

**Naval:** Now, there's a flip side, where every kid is a lottery ticket and an invention. So there's some benefit to having more kids. But you can't force it. I think it'll work itself out.
當然，這也有另一面，就是每個孩子都是一張樂透彩券、一項發明。所以多生孩子確實有一些好處。但你沒辦法硬逼。我認為它會自己解決的。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| scalable | /ˋskeləbḷ/ | adj. | 可擴展的、易規模化的 |
| fertility | /fɝˋtɪlətɪ/ | n. | 生育率、生育力 |
| Malthusian | /mælˋθuzɪən/ | adj. | 馬爾薩斯（人口論）的 |
| emancipation | /ɪˏmænsəˋpeʃən/ | n. | 解放、解除束縛 |
| hedonistic | /ˏhidn̩ˋɪstɪk/ | adj. | 享樂主義的 |
| strangle | /ˋstræŋgḷ/ | v. | 勒死、扼殺 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`bet on`**：「押注在⋯⋯、看好⋯⋯」。
- **`way ahead`**：「遙遙領先」，`way` 為口語強調副詞。
- **`alive and well`**：「活得好好的、依然盛行」。
- **`God bless them`**：字面「上帝保佑他們」，此處帶輕鬆調侃的祝福語氣。
- **`upstream / downstream`**：「上游／下游」，比喻因果或問題的先後鏈條。
- **`work itself out`**：「（事情）自行解決、自然理順」。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`It's everybody else who doesn't have a self-driving vehicle that's screwed.`** — 強調句 `It's ... that/who ...`，把焦點放在 `everybody else`。
- **`How are you going to meme them into having more kids?`** — `meme` 當動詞（新造用法）+ `into + 動名詞` 表「說服／促使某人去做」，如 `talk someone into doing`。
- **`the low fertility rate is upstream of the downstream problems`** — 名詞化的方位比喻 `upstream of / downstream`，描述因果的先後位置。

## 81. 亞當斯的慢動作災難定律：經濟與誘因會自行解決

### 逐句對照

**Naval:** Scott Adams has this great law which he calls the Adams law of slow-moving disasters. When disasters are very slow-moving, like peak oil or global warming or population collapse, and everyone can kind of see them coming, economics and society as a force solve them, because enough individual people have incentives to go solve them.
Scott Adams 有一條很棒的定律，他稱之為「亞當斯慢動作災難定律」。當災難進展得非常緩慢，像是石油峰值、全球暖化或人口崩潰，而且大家多少都看得到它正在逼近時，經濟和社會這股力量會把它解決掉，因為有夠多的個人有誘因去解決它。

**Naval:** So I don't know exactly how it gets solved, but I think it could get solved in various ways. One example could be, you know, maybe people retire later. Maybe AI and automation and robots take care of the older people.
所以我不確定它究竟會怎麼被解決，但我認為它有可能以各種方式被解決。舉個例子，也許大家會更晚退休。也許 AI、自動化和機器人會照顧老年人。

**Naval:** Maybe we figure out how to have immigrants while still keeping a high trust society. We kind of put more rules around immigration that protect some of the high trust benefits. Maybe we outsource more things. Maybe we just have more land and housing to go around.
也許我們會想出辦法，在維持高信任社會的同時接納移民。在移民政策上設下更多規則，保護一些高信任帶來的好處。也許我們會把更多事情外包。也許我們就是有更多土地和住房可以分配。

**Naval:** Believe me, if we were having too many kids, everybody would complain about how there's no housing and there's no land, right? So they'll always find something to care about.
相信我，如果我們生太多小孩，大家就會抱怨沒有住房、沒有土地，對吧？所以他們永遠都能找到東西來擔憂。

**Naval:** So I just don't view this as like a thing that any individual or government action is going to solve. I think economics and incentives over time will solve it. And I'm not even convinced it's like that big of a problem.
所以我不認為這是任何個人或政府行動能解決的事。我認為隨著時間過去，經濟和誘因會把它解決。而且我甚至不太相信它是個那麼大的問題。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| disaster | /dɪˋzæstɚ/ | n. | 災難 |
| incentive | /ɪnˋsɛntɪv/ | n. | 誘因、動機 |
| collapse | /kəˋlæps/ | n. | 崩潰、崩塌 |
| immigration | /ˏɪməˋgreʃən/ | n. | 移民（行為／制度） |
| outsource | /ˋaʊtˏsors/ | v. | 外包 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`slow-moving`**：字面「移動緩慢的」，這裡指災難「進展很慢、有時間反應」。
- **`see them coming`**：「看得出它要來了、預見得到」。
- **`to go around`**：「足夠分配、夠大家用」。例：`enough food to go around`（食物夠分）。
- **`Believe me`**：口語加強語氣，「相信我、真的」。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`If we were having too many kids, everybody would complain...`** — 第二類條件句（與現在事實相反）：`if + 過去式..., would + 原形`，表示與現況相反的假設。
- **`I'm not even convinced it's that big of a problem.`** — `that big of a problem` 是口語誇張用法，`that + 形容詞`表「那麼⋯⋯」；`of a` 為美式口語加強結構。

## 82. 生育率可能自我修正：孩子帶來意義、糟糕的心理學研究

### 逐句對照

**Naval:** It may be self-correcting too, which is that if there are too few kids in society, the returns to having kids literally might just go up. It might just be easier to have the incentive to now have a child, because there's so few around, they're going to get the best job. They're going to have opportunity, resources.
它也可能會自我修正，意思是如果社會上小孩太少，生小孩的報酬率可能就會直接上升。現在生小孩的誘因可能會變得更強，因為周遭的小孩太少了，他們將會得到最好的工作、擁有機會和資源。

**主持人:** I suppose if you could come at it from a pain side, which is you look at all of the other people around who don't have kids. Let's say that pensions completely drop off and the only way that old people are able to survive is if their children pay them some sort of stipend, like reverse, you know, send money back up the generations. You go, okay, well, that's a pretty good incentive.
我想，如果你能從「痛苦」那一面切入，也就是你看看周遭那些沒有小孩的人。假設退休金完全消失，老年人唯一能活下去的方式，就是子女付給他們某種津貼，像是反過來，把錢往上一代送。你就會想，好吧，這是個相當強的誘因。

**Naval:** That's a good incentive. I also think that people have been memed into thinking that kids make your life worse, and that's a pretty bad meme.
那是個很好的誘因。我也認為，人們被一種迷因洗腦，以為小孩會讓你的人生變糟，而那是個相當糟糕的迷因。

**主持人:** What's your experience been?
你的經驗是怎樣？

**Naval:** Kids make your life better in every possible way. If you want an automatic built-in meaning to life, have kids. And I think there are these bad psych studies, like most psych studies, unfortunately, that say that people are unhappy when they have kids.
小孩讓你的人生在各種可能的層面上都變得更好。如果你想要一個自動內建的人生意義，就生小孩。而我認為有些糟糕的心理學研究，很不幸地，就像大多數心理學研究一樣，說人們有了小孩會不快樂。

**Naval:** It's because you're caught in the middle of changing a diaper and you're saying like, "Are you glad you had kids or not?" Or they don't even say that. They say, "Are you happy or not?" And they say, "No, I'm not happy right now."
那是因為你正夾在換尿布的當下，然後他們問你：「你慶幸自己生了小孩嗎？」或者他們根本不這樣問，而是問：「你現在快樂嗎？」然後對方說：「不，我現在不快樂。」

**Naval:** But what they don't realize is that person has found something more important than being happy in the moment. They found meaning. And the meaning comes from kids.
但他們沒意識到的是，那個人已經找到了比「當下快樂」更重要的東西。他們找到了意義。而意義來自於孩子。

**Naval:** And if you ask parents, do you regret having kids? I think it would be 99 to 1 against. It would be, "No, I don't regret having kids. I love having kids. I'm so glad I had kids." It's incredibly rare to meet a parent that regretted having children.
如果你問父母：你後悔生小孩嗎？我認為答案會是 99 比 1 的反對。會是：「不，我不後悔生小孩。我很愛有小孩。我很慶幸自己生了小孩。」要遇到一個後悔生小孩的父母，是極其罕見的。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| self-correcting | /ˏsɛlfkəˋrɛktɪŋ/ | adj. | 自我修正的 |
| returns | /rɪˋtɝnz/ | n. | 報酬、回報 |
| pension | /ˋpɛnʃən/ | n. | 退休金 |
| stipend | /ˋstaɪpɛnd/ | n. | 津貼、定期給付 |
| diaper | /ˋdaɪɚpɚ/ | n. | 尿布 |
| regret | /rɪˋgrɛt/ | v. | 後悔 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`be memed into thinking`**：被迷因（網路流行說法）洗腦而相信⋯⋯，`meme` 當動詞用，很新潮的口語。
- **`drop off`**：這裡指「（數量）驟降、消失」。
- **`built-in`**：「內建的、自帶的」。
- **`99 to 1 against`**：「99 比 1 反對」，用比數形容壓倒性傾向。
- **`caught in the middle of`**：「正夾在⋯⋯的當下、卡在⋯⋯之中」。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`the returns to having kids might just go up`** — `returns to + 動名詞` 表「做某事的報酬」；`just` 在口語中軟化語氣，「就這麼、直接」。
- **`If you want an automatic built-in meaning to life, have kids.`** — 第一類條件句 + 祈使句：`if + 現在式..., 祈使句`，直接給建議。

## 83. 幾乎沒人後悔生孩子：寵物是孩子的替代品、Naval 對孩子的期望

### 逐句對照

**主持人:** It's pretty good odds.
這機率相當好。

**Naval:** It's extremely good odds. And I think a lot of people get late into life and, you know, then they can't admit that they didn't want kids, that they should have had kids. It's kind of late in the game.
機率極好。而我認為很多人到了人生後段，就沒辦法承認自己當初不想要小孩、承認自己其實應該生小孩。到那時已經有點太遲了。

**Naval:** But a lot of times you see everybody who has a pet, right? And they're pushing them around in a stroller, right? What is that? That's a sublimated desire for children.
但很多時候你會看到那些養寵物的人，對吧？他們用嬰兒車推著寵物到處走，對吧？那是什麼？那是一種被昇華的、對孩子的渴望。

**主持人:** Yeah. Malcolm Collins says that having a pet is to children as using porn is to sex. He basically thinks that it's sort of a surrogate.
對。Malcolm Collins 說，養寵物之於小孩，就像看色情片之於性愛。他基本上認為那算是一種替代品。

**Naval:** It's definitely in that direction. And, you know, I like pets, I like animals, but I don't like the idea of neutering or spaying something and then keeping it as a prisoner in the house and having to train it. It's just I don't want to be responsible for that.
它絕對是朝那個方向。而且，你知道，我喜歡寵物、喜歡動物，但我不喜歡那種把動物結紮、然後像囚犯一樣關在家裡、還得訓練牠的做法。就是，我不想為那件事負責。

**主持人:** Given that you've been thinking more about child rearing, what do you hope that your kids learn from their childhood?
既然你最近比較常思考育兒的事，你希望你的孩子從童年學到什麼？

**Naval:** They should just be happy and do what they want. I don't have particular goals in mind for them. I think that's another route to unhappiness.
他們就應該快樂、做自己想做的事。我對他們沒有特定的目標。我認為那是通往不快樂的另一條路。

**主持人:** That's different though, right? Learn versus goals. What do you want them to want out of life? Like, you had that idea that your number one job as a parent is to provide unconditional love to your kids.
但那不一樣吧？「學到」和「目標」是兩回事。你希望他們從人生中想要什麼？像是，你有過一個想法：身為父母，你的第一要務是給孩子無條件的愛。

**Naval:** Yeah, that's it. I want my kids to feel unconditionally loved and I want them to have high self-esteem as a consequence of that. But I don't get to choose any— all I get to choose is my output. I can output love. I can't choose what they feel. I can't choose how they behave. I can't choose what they turn out to be.
對，就是這樣。我希望我的孩子感受到被無條件地愛著，也希望他們因此擁有高度的自尊。但我無法選擇任何——我唯一能選擇的是我的輸出。我可以輸出愛。我無法選擇他們的感受，無法選擇他們的行為，也無法選擇他們最後會變成什麼樣的人。

**主持人:** And downstream from that, there should be freedom. There should be a degree of freedom that comes from the self-esteem that comes from the unconditionality.
而由此往下延伸，就會有自由。會有某種程度的自由，來自那份自尊，而那份自尊又來自那份無條件。

**Naval:** They should make their own mistakes and learn their own lessons and have their own desires and fulfill them as is appropriate. Like any parent, I wouldn't want them to be hurt. I wouldn't want them to be unhappy. But I cannot control these things.
他們應該犯自己的錯、學自己的教訓、擁有自己的渴望，並在適當的範圍內去實現它們。像任何父母一樣，我不希望他們受傷、不希望他們不快樂。但這些事我無法控制。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| odds | /ɑdz/ | n. | 機率、勝算 |
| stroller | /ˋstrolɚ/ | n. | 嬰兒推車 |
| sublimated | /ˋsʌbləˏmetɪd/ | adj. | 被昇華的 |
| surrogate | /ˋsɝəgɪt/ | n. | 替代品、代理者 |
| self-esteem | /ˏsɛlfəsˋtim/ | n. | 自尊 |
| unconditional | /ˏʌnkənˋdɪʃən!/ | adj. | 無條件的 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`late in the game`**：「為時已晚、局勢後段」，源自比賽用語。
- **`A is to B as C is to D`**：「A 之於 B，如同 C 之於 D」，經典類比句型。
- **`in that direction`**：「朝那個方向、差不多是那樣」，口語軟化肯定。
- **`downstream from that`**：「由此往下延伸、隨之而來」，Naval 常用的思路比喻。
- **`turn out to be`**：「結果變成、最後成為」。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`they can't admit that they should have had kids.`** — `should have + p.p.` 表「當初本應做卻沒做」的後悔。
- **`all I get to choose is my output`** — `all (that) + 主詞 + 動詞 is...` 強調句，「我唯一能⋯⋯的就是」。
- **`fulfill them as is appropriate`** — `as is appropriate` 是固定慣用語，「在適當的範圍內、視情況而定」，`as` 引導的省略關係子句。

## 84. IYI 育兒偽科學：同睡與哭到睡的恐懼源於爛研究

### 逐句對照

**主持人:** You replied to my friend Rob Henderson. He was talking about how kids fall asleep more quickly when they're being carried, and you said cry it out and co-sleeping is dangerous. What's IYI science?
你回覆了我朋友 Rob Henderson。他在談小孩被抱著時會更快睡著，而你說「哭到睡」和「同床共眠」很危險。什麼是 IYI 科學？

**Naval:** IYI is Nassim Taleb. He talks about "intellectual yet idiot." These are people who are overeducated and they deny basic common sense.
IYI 是 Nassim Taleb 提出的。他講的是「智識分子卻是白痴」。這些人受了過多教育，卻否定基本常識。

**主持人:** Okay.
好。

**Naval:** So there's a lot of that that goes on in child rearing, thanks to really bad studies and bad public medical directives. So for example, a few parents— maybe they're drunk or they're high or they have other issues— and they roll over their kid when they're sleeping, the kid suffocates, or they neglect their kid.
所以在育兒領域裡有很多這種東西，都要拜那些很爛的研究和糟糕的公共醫療指示所賜。舉例來說，有少數父母——也許他們喝醉了、嗑了藥，或有其他問題——睡覺時翻身壓到小孩，小孩就窒息了，或者他們疏忽了小孩。

**主持人:** Is that co-sleeping, having them in the bed?
那就是同床共眠，把他們放在床上嗎？

**Naval:** Yeah. Exactly. Or the modern proclamation. And so because of that, they say, "Well, don't co-sleep with your kids." Well, the kids in every society through all of human history co-slept with their parents. Where else do you think they were sleeping? They didn't have houses with multiple rooms.
對，沒錯。或說是現代的那套宣示。就因為這樣，他們說：「好，別跟你的小孩同睡。」可是，人類歷史上每一個社會的小孩都跟父母同睡。不然你以為他們睡哪裡？他們可沒有好幾個房間的房子。

**主持人:** Yeah. Exactly. "Put them in the other tent."
對，沒錯。「把他們放到另一個帳篷去。」

**Naval:** It's just nonsense. Co-sleeping has been around since the dawn of time. So has feeding kids cow milk or goat milk when breast milk runs out or is not available. Yet we're told formula, made with soy and corn syrup, which was invented recently, is somehow better than cow milk.
這根本是胡扯。同床共眠自古就存在。餵小孩喝牛奶或羊奶——在母奶用盡或無法取得時——也是一樣。然而我們卻被告知，用大豆和玉米糖漿做的、近代才發明的配方奶，不知怎地竟然比牛奶還好。

**Naval:** And cow milk can be dangerous for your kids and co-sleeping is dangerous for your kids and cry it out is the right answer. All of that is nonsense. It's very clear that we raised children throughout human history without these interventions.
還說牛奶對你的小孩可能有害、同床共眠對你的小孩有害、「哭到睡」才是正確答案。這一切都是胡扯。很清楚的是，人類歷史上我們一直在沒有這些干預的情況下養育孩子。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| overeducated | /ˏovɚˋɛdʒəˏketɪd/ | adj. | 受過多教育的 |
| directive | /dəˋrɛktɪv/ | n. | 指示、命令 |
| suffocate | /ˋsʌfəˏket/ | v. | 使窒息 |
| neglect | /nɪgˋlɛkt/ | v. | 疏忽、忽視 |
| proclamation | /ˏprɑkləˋmeʃən/ | n. | 宣告、公告 |
| intervention | /ˏɪntɚˋvɛnʃən/ | n. | 干預、介入 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`cry it out`**：育兒法「哭到睡」——讓嬰兒自己哭到睡著、不去安撫。
- **`co-sleeping`**：「同床共眠」——親子睡同一張床。
- **`intellectual yet idiot (IYI)`**：Taleb 的譏諷語，「智識上很高、實則是白痴」。
- **`since the dawn of time`**：「自古以來、從遠古開始」。
- **`run out`**：「用完、耗盡」。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`So has feeding kids cow milk...`** — 倒裝的 `So + 助動詞 + 主詞` 表「⋯⋯也是如此」；此處助動詞 `has` 呼應前句的現在完成式 `has been around`。
- **`we're told formula... is somehow better`** — 被動語態 `be told + that 子句`（that 省略），「我們被告知⋯⋯」。

## 85. 過度外推的垃圾科學、疫苗崇拜過頭、相信本能勝過育兒書

### 逐句對照

**Naval:** And to me, the idea that you're going to let your kid cry it out— I get why that's done for practical reasons, so that you can get some sleep and go to work in the morning. But the reality is, when you let the kid cry it out, you're letting the kid bawl until it finally gives up.
對我來說，「讓你的小孩哭到睡」這個想法——我懂為什麼會這樣做，出於實際考量，這樣你才能睡點覺、早上去上班。但事實是，當你讓小孩哭到睡，你是在讓小孩嚎啕大哭到最後放棄為止。

**Naval:** I mean, the kid left by itself to cry it out in the wild— it's going to get eaten by a tiger. So this kid is starting off on the wrong foundation. The one I mentioned earlier about the idea that babies don't feel pain— like, that's ludicrous, right?
我是說，一個被獨自留下、在野外哭到睡的小孩——牠會被老虎吃掉。所以這個小孩是在錯誤的地基上起步。我先前提到的那個「嬰兒感覺不到痛」的說法——那太荒謬了吧？

**主持人:** I've never heard that before. That's such a wild idea.
我從沒聽過。那想法太離譜了。

**Naval:** Yeah, I'm not saying that's 100% true. I read it on Twitter and I did one level of confirmation on it, but it's so ludicrous that I should probably do two or three levels of confirmation on it before I talk about it.
對，我不是說那百分之百為真。我在 Twitter 上看到的，我做了一層查證，但它實在太荒謬，我在談論它之前大概應該做兩三層的查證才對。

**Naval:** But there are definitely some people who believe that— enough that it was a thing in certain circles for a while. But I think we just go through these IYI beliefs, these intellectual beliefs come from people who take a little bit of knowledge and extrapolate it too far.
但確實有些人相信那個——多到讓它在某些圈子裡風行了一陣子。但我認為我們就是會經歷這些 IYI 信念，這些智識分子的信念來自那些拿了一點點知識、卻把它外推得太過頭的人。

**Naval:** They think we know more than we know due to recent scientific studies, and these are junk science. These are low-power studies on very certain contexts that then get over-applied. Behavioral psych is very guilty of this, but it's true across a lot of science.
他們因為近期的科學研究就以為我們懂得比實際更多，而這些是垃圾科學。這些是在非常特定情境下做的低檢定力研究，然後被過度套用。行為心理學在這方面非常有罪，但這在很多科學領域都成立。

**Naval:** And there are a whole bunch of things you're just not supposed to talk about. You can't say anything negative about vaccines, because god forbid, what if they don't get the polio vaccine, right? And that's part of the reason for the recent vaccine debate, because we've taken our worship for vaccines too far.
還有一大堆事情你就是不該談。你不能對疫苗說任何負面的話，因為天啊，萬一他們不去打小兒麻痺疫苗怎麼辦，對吧？這也是近期疫苗爭論的部分原因，因為我們把對疫苗的崇拜推得太過頭了。

**Naval:** The same way, there's this whole SIDS thing, sudden infant death syndrome. It's like, no, kids don't suddenly mysteriously die. More likely there was neglect or there was a problem, and whoever was the caretaker doesn't want to admit to it. Kids don't just spontaneously die in the crib.
同樣地，還有整個 SIDS 那套東西，嬰兒猝死症。就像，不對，小孩不會突然神秘地死掉。更可能是有疏忽、有問題，而照顧者不想承認。小孩不會就這樣在嬰兒床裡自發地死掉。

**主持人:** It's a real minefield.
這真是個雷區。

**Naval:** It's a minefield. And you have these scared parents having a kid for the first time and they open a book and start reading how to raise children, when I would argue that your natural instincts on what to do with your child are actually pretty good.
是雷區。你會看到這些嚇壞了的父母，第一次生小孩，翻開一本書開始讀怎麼養小孩，而我會主張，你對於該怎麼對待孩子的天生本能其實相當不錯。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| ludicrous | /ˋludɪkrəs/ | adj. | 荒謬可笑的 |
| extrapolate | /ɪkˋstræpəˏlet/ | v. | 外推、推斷 |
| junk science | /dʒʌŋk ˋsaɪəns/ | n. | 垃圾科學 |
| worship | /ˋwɝʃɪp/ | n. | 崇拜 |
| spontaneously | /spɑnˋtenɪəslɪ/ | adv. | 自發地、無緣由地 |
| instinct | /ˋɪnstɪŋkt/ | n. | 本能、直覺 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`bawl`**：「嚎啕大哭、放聲大哭」。
- **`start off on the wrong foundation`**：「一開始就站錯根基」（類似 `get off on the wrong foot`）。
- **`it was a thing`**：口語「那曾經蔚為風潮、真有其事」。
- **`god forbid`**：「但願別發生、天啊千萬別」，表擔憂。
- **`a minefield`**：「地雷區」——比喻充滿風險、動輒得咎的領域。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`the kid left by itself to cry it out in the wild`** — 過去分詞片語 `left by itself` 當後位修飾，等於 `the kid that is left by itself`。
- **`it's so ludicrous that I should probably do two or three levels of confirmation`** — `so + 形容詞 + that 子句`，「如此⋯⋯以致於⋯⋯」。
- **`we've taken our worship for vaccines too far`** — `take something too far` 表「把某事做得太過頭」。

## 86. 孩子不是有缺陷的成人：教解釋性理論而非死背（細菌學說）

### 逐句對照

**Naval:** Children are not deficient adults who can't reason. To some extent that's true, but mostly it's not true. Mostly they have very good reasons for what they want, and you as a parent mostly have communication problems with them. They can't yet communicate to you and you can't communicate to them.
孩子不是不會思考、有缺陷的成人。某種程度上那是真的，但大部分情況並非如此。多數時候他們對自己想要的東西有很好的理由，而你身為父母，主要是跟他們有溝通問題。他們還無法對你表達，你也無法對他們表達。

**Naval:** So early on with my kids, I tried to focus on teaching them basic explanatory theories, as opposed to having them memorize things. That's just the most Knowledge-based solution.
所以在孩子還小的時候，我試著把重點放在教他們基本的解釋性理論，而不是讓他們死背東西。那才是最符合「知識」精神的做法。

**Naval:** I'll give you a very simple example, right? Okay, so this is Twitter and this is the "how to get rich without getting lucky" thread. A simple one is, you know, how does knowledge get created? If you follow the critical rationalism David Deutsch philosophy, then it's by guessing and then by testing your guesses.
我給你一個很簡單的例子，好嗎？好，這是 Twitter，這是那則「不靠運氣如何致富」的推文串。一個簡單的例子是，知識是怎麼被創造出來的？如果你認同 David Deutsch 的批判理性主義哲學，那答案就是：靠猜測，然後測試你的猜測。

**Naval:** So whenever they ask me something like, "Well, why do you think that is?"— "Well, how would we figure out if that's true?" Right? So that's a basic game you can play.
所以每當他們問我像「你為什麼覺得是那樣？」我就回：「那我們要怎麼弄清楚那是不是真的？」對吧？這就是一個你可以玩的基本遊戲。

**主持人:** Involving them.
把他們拉進來一起想。

**Naval:** Involving them. But another one is that a lot of the rules that you teach kids have to do with hygiene, right? You must brush your teeth, cover your mouth when you cough, clean up after yourself, don't touch that, wash your hands after you do this, don't eat food off the floor.
把他們拉進來。但另一個例子是，你教小孩的很多規矩都跟衛生有關，對吧？你必須刷牙、咳嗽要摀嘴、自己收拾乾淨、別碰那個、做完這個要洗手、別撿地上的食物來吃。

**Naval:** But all of these are subsumed under the germ theory of disease, right? So if you instead go on YouTube and show them videos of germs, or if you have them look under a microscope at anything, they're like, "Ah!"— they can infer what's going on.
但這些全都可以被歸納在「疾病的細菌學說」之下，對吧？所以如果你改成上 YouTube 給他們看細菌的影片，或讓他們用顯微鏡看任何東西，他們就會「啊！」——他們能自己推論出是怎麼回事。

**主持人:** Yeah, there's creepy-crawlies everywhere and I've got to watch out for them.
對，到處都是那些噁心的小蟲子，我得小心提防它們。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| deficient | /dɪˋfɪʃənt/ | adj. | 有缺陷的、不足的 |
| explanatory | /ɪkˋsplænəˏtorɪ/ | adj. | 解釋性的 |
| memorize | /ˋmɛməˏraɪz/ | v. | 死記、背誦 |
| hygiene | /ˋhaɪdʒin/ | n. | 衛生 |
| subsume | /səbˋsjum/ | v. | 歸入、涵蓋於 |
| infer | /ɪnˋfɝ/ | v. | 推論、推斷 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`as opposed to`**：「而不是、相對於」，用來對比兩種做法。
- **`have to do with`**：「與⋯⋯有關」。
- **`clean up after yourself`**：「自己收拾善後、清理自己弄亂的」。
- **`creepy-crawlies`**：口語「爬來爬去的噁心小蟲」，帶童趣。
- **`watch out for`**：「小心提防、留意」。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`Children are not deficient adults who can't reason.`** — 關係子句 `who can't reason` 修飾 `adults`，`reason` 在此為動詞「推理、思考」。
- **`all of these are subsumed under the germ theory`** — 被動語態 `be subsumed under`，「被歸納／涵蓋在⋯⋯之下」。
- **`if you have them look under a microscope`** — 使役動詞 `have + 受詞 + 原形動詞`，「讓某人做某事」。

---

## 87. 病原體是真正的天敵：老化源於此、紅皇后假說、CRISPR

### 逐句對照

**Naval:** And then you can talk about how, if you look at humans, our real enemy are pathogens. I think a lot of aging and disease are actually downstream of our competition with pathogens over time, to a point that people still don't fully appreciate.
接著你可以談到，如果你觀察人類，我們真正的敵人是病原體。我認為很多老化和疾病其實都源自我們長期以來與病原體的競爭，其程度是人們至今仍未充分認識到的。

**Naval:** There's a Red Queen hypothesis, which is that we undergo sexual selection to mix up our genes. So every 20 years, every generation, you mix up your genes. But if you look at how bacteria and viruses mutate through just random mutations, their mixup rate and evolution rate is roughly the same as ours.
有一個「紅皇后假說」，意思是我們透過有性生殖的選擇來混合我們的基因。所以每 20 年、每一個世代，你就混合一次基因。但如果你看細菌和病毒如何僅靠隨機突變來變異，牠們基因的混合速率和演化速率大致跟我們相同。

**Naval:** Even though they go through thousands of generations in those 20 years, because they're not doing sexual selection, they're doing asexual replication and mutation, their evolutionary rate is roughly equivalent to ours. So we're in a Red Queen race where we're both running at roughly the same speed using very different strategies.
儘管牠們在那 20 年裡經歷了數千個世代，因為牠們不是做有性選擇，而是做無性複製和突變，牠們的演化速率大致與我們相當。所以我們正處在一場「紅皇后競賽」中，雙方以大致相同的速度奔跑，卻使用非常不同的策略。

**Naval:** But a lot of how we're evolved is around pathogens. Our immune system is one of the most expensive things to run in the body. So much is about immune system optimization— that's about pathogens.
但我們的演化有很大一部分是圍繞著病原體。我們的免疫系統是身體裡運作成本最高的東西之一。有這麼多都是關於免疫系統的最佳化——那都是為了對付病原體。

**Naval:** Junk DNA in bacteria— and CRISPR was discovered because in bacteria their DNA is evolved to fight viruses. And the way it does that is by taking viral DNA and snipping it up every time there's a viral attack, and storing it in their own DNA, so they have a copy and can recognize it next time it attacks.
細菌裡的垃圾 DNA——CRISPR 之所以被發現，正是因為細菌的 DNA 演化出對抗病毒的能力。它做到這件事的方式，是每次遭到病毒攻擊時，就把病毒的 DNA 切下來、存進自己的 DNA 裡，這樣牠們就有一份副本，下次再被攻擊時就能辨認出來。

**Naval:** A lot of the population structure of a species determines how long their lifespans are. So if in a given species there's a very high rate of infection, then you'll have these older members of the population carrying diseases that will then infect the young.
一個物種的族群結構，很大程度上決定了牠們的壽命有多長。所以，如果在某個物種裡感染率非常高，那麼你就會有這些年長的成員帶著疾病，接著去感染年幼的個體。

**Naval:** So it's important for that species to get rid of the old faster. So the higher the disease rate in a given population, the less long-lived the entire population, so the older ones don't infect the younger ones. That's a hypothesis and I think it's true.
所以對那個物種而言，更快淘汰老一輩就變得很重要。因此，一個族群裡的疾病率越高，整個族群就越短命，好讓年長的不去感染年幼的。這是一個假說，而我認為它是真的。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| pathogen | /ˋpæθədʒən/ | n. | 病原體 |
| mutate | /ˋmjutet/ | v. | 突變、變異 |
| asexual | /eˋsɛkʃʊəl/ | adj. | 無性的 |
| replication | /ˏrɛpləˋkeʃən/ | n. | 複製 |
| immune system | /ɪˋmjun ˋsɪstəm/ | n. | 免疫系統 |
| lifespan | /ˋlaɪfˏspæn/ | n. | 壽命 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`Red Queen hypothesis`**：「紅皇后假說」——物種必須不斷演化才能維持相對地位（典出《愛麗絲鏡中奇緣》）。
- **`downstream of`**：「源自於、是⋯⋯的下游結果」。
- **`mix up`**：「打散混合」，這裡指基因重組。
- **`snip up`**：「剪碎、切下」。
- **`get rid of`**：「除去、淘汰」。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`the higher the disease rate..., the less long-lived the entire population`** — `the + 比較級..., the + 比較級...` 句型，「越⋯⋯就越⋯⋯」。
- **`Even though they go through thousands of generations..., their evolutionary rate is roughly equivalent to ours.`** — `Even though` 引導讓步子句，「儘管⋯⋯」。
- **`the way it does that is by taking... and storing...`** — `by + 動名詞` 表達「藉由做⋯⋯的方式」，兩個動名詞並列。

---

## 88. 體內恆定與抗病原：外源激素被抵銷、激素為何脈衝式分泌

### 逐句對照

**主持人:** It's an interesting hypothesis.
這是個有趣的假說。

**Naval:** Homeostasis within the human body— how we're always returning to a given level of things— that's a fundamental part of our makeup. Our temperature, pH, blood pressure, and so on are under homeostasis. But if you engage in any kind of signaling, like you take a peptide, that's a signaling molecule. You take a hormone externally, the body will counteract it.
人體內的恆定狀態——我們總是回到某個既定的水準——是我們構造的根本部分。我們的體溫、酸鹼值、血壓等等都受恆定機制調控。但如果你進行任何一種訊號傳遞，比如你服用一種胜肽，那是一種訊號分子。你從外部攝取一種激素，身體就會去抵銷它。

**Naval:** You take testosterone, the body will downregulate its own production very fast. And the body releases its own hormones in pulses rather than steady state. Why is that? Well, that's because bacteria and viruses can infect your body and trick your body. They can take it over. Toxoplasmosis does this, rabies does this. They take over macroscopic structures.
你攝取睪固酮，身體會很快地下調自己的生產。而且身體是以脈衝的方式、而非穩定持續的方式來釋放自己的激素。為什麼呢？那是因為細菌和病毒可以感染你的身體、欺騙你的身體。牠們可以接管它。弓形蟲病會這樣做，狂犬病會這樣做。牠們接管了宏觀的結構體。

**Naval:** Small bacteria and viruses would hack our bodies and literally take them over if we didn't have defense mechanisms. And one of those defense mechanisms is homeostasis. Anytime you see something getting out of whack, you immediately push back really hard on it, because— did I just get infected? Is something trying to take me over?
如果我們沒有防禦機制，微小的細菌和病毒就會駭進我們的身體、真的把它接管過去。而那些防禦機制之一就是恆定。任何時候你看到某樣東西失衡了，你就立刻非常用力地把它推回去，因為——我是不是剛剛被感染了？是不是有什麼東西想接管我？

**Naval:** It's also why hormones get released in pulses at night rather than in steady state low levels, because enemy bacteria can release toxins or the same signaling molecules in small quantities, but they can't pulse. They can't coordinate to pulse.
這也是為什麼激素會在夜間以脈衝方式釋放、而非以穩定的低水準釋放，因為敵方的細菌可以釋放毒素、或以少量釋放相同的訊號分子，但牠們無法脈衝式地釋放。牠們無法協調一致地做出脈衝。

**主持人:** So your body can coordinate to pulse as a macroscopic object, but microscopic objects can't coordinate to create the same pulses.
所以你的身體身為一個宏觀的物體，可以協調出脈衝，但微觀的物體無法協調出同樣的脈衝。

**主持人:** Oh, that's cool.
喔，那很酷。

**主持人:** So you know that it's coming from you. Is that why?
所以你知道那是來自你自己。是這個原因嗎？

**Naval:** Correct. It's endogenous rather than exogenous. And that's why we resist a lot of exogenous treatments. A lot of our medical treatments don't work.
沒錯。它是內源性的，而不是外源性的。這也是為什麼我們會抵抗許多外源性的療法。我們很多的醫療手段之所以無效，正是這個緣故。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| homeostasis | /ˏhomɪəˋstesɪs/ | n. | 體內恆定、恆定狀態 |
| hormone | /ˋhɔrmon/ | n. | 激素、荷爾蒙 |
| counteract | /ˏkaʊntɚˋækt/ | v. | 抵銷、對抗 |
| downregulate | /ˏdaʊnˋrɛgjəˏlet/ | v. | 下調（分泌／表現） |
| endogenous | /ɛnˋdɑdʒənəs/ | adj. | 內源性的 |
| exogenous | /ɛksˋɑdʒənəs/ | adj. | 外源性的 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`take over`**：「接管、佔據掌控」，此處指病原體「劫持」身體。
- **`out of whack`**：口語「失常、失衡、亂了套」。
- **`push back on`**：「推回、抵抗、反制」。
- **`in pulses`**：「以脈衝方式、一陣一陣地」（相對 `steady state` 穩定持續）。
- **`Is that why?`**：口語追問「是因為這樣嗎？」

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`if we didn't have defense mechanisms, small bacteria... would hack our bodies`** — 第二類條件句（與現在事實相反）：`if + 過去式..., would + 原形`。
- **`Anytime you see something getting out of whack, you immediately push back`** — `Anytime` 引導時間副詞子句，等於 `whenever`；`see something getting` 為感官動詞 + 現在分詞，表進行中的狀態。
- **`It's endogenous rather than exogenous.`** — `A rather than B` 句型，「是 A 而非 B」，用於精確對比。

## 89. 微生物在食物鏈頂端：宗教戒律即抗病原、教孩子這套哲學與大哉問

### 逐句對照

**Naval:** There's a bunch more I could go on with, but a lot of— you see this in cancers, where a lot of bacteria show up. Like the Epstein-Barr virus shows up in a lot of cancers. And now it seems like the gut microbiome influences so many things.
我還能繼續講一大堆，但很多——你在癌症裡就看得到，很多細菌會冒出來。像 EB 病毒（Epstein-Barr virus）就出現在很多癌症裡。現在看起來，腸道微生物群（gut microbiome）影響的東西多到不行。

**Naval:** Basically, bacteria and viruses are at the top of the food chain compared to us. Like, we are the top of the well-known food chain, but bacteria and viruses eat us. Fungus eats us. So these microscopic predators are our natural predators.
基本上，跟我們比起來，細菌和病毒才是食物鏈的頂端。我們是「已知」食物鏈的頂端沒錯，但細菌和病毒會吃掉我們，真菌也會吃掉我們。所以這些微觀的掠食者，才是我們天然的天敵。

**Naval:** And so a lot of aging, societal structure, hygiene, religious strictures against pork, circumcision—all of these things are designed to resist bacteria and viruses. So if you can teach children this philosophy at an early age, you shortcut all the debates.
所以很多老化現象、社會結構、衛生習慣、宗教上禁食豬肉的戒律、割禮——這些全都是為了抵抗細菌和病毒而設計的。所以如果你能在孩子很小的時候就教他們這套哲學，你就跳過了所有的爭辯。

**主持人:** How effective have you been at teaching that philosophy to children?
你把這套哲學教給孩子，成效如何？

**Naval:** That one, I think I've been pretty effective. I've drilled that one at home. The one I haven't quite gotten around to yet is evolution. I'm starting to do little bits of that, like "we came from monkeys—what does that mean?"
那套喔，我覺得我教得還蠻成功的，在家我一直反覆灌輸。我還沒真正著手的是演化論。我開始講一點點了，像是「我們是從猴子演化來的——那是什麼意思？」

**Naval:** I've already got them thinking about some of the deeper questions. I did ask my young son, like, "Can nothing exist?" I thought that was a fun question. I like to throw out a fun question.
我已經讓他們開始思考一些更深層的問題了。我還問過我小兒子：「『無』能存在嗎？」我覺得那是個很好玩的問題。我喜歡丟出一個好玩的問題。

**主持人:** How old is he now? Like, four? Three?
他現在幾歲？大概四歲、三歲？

**Naval:** No, no, he's eight. An eight-year-old and a six-year-old. So I asked them both, "Can nothing exist?" And they had pretty good answers, right? Another one we played with the other day was, "What is the matrix? What is all this?"
不不，他八歲。一個八歲、一個六歲。所以我問他們兩個：「『無』能存在嗎？」他們的答案都還不錯呢。另一個我們前幾天玩的問題是：「母體（the matrix）是什麼？這一切到底是什麼？」

**Naval:** I just find it entertaining. It's just fun to talk about these questions with your kids. I'm not saying that's a good way of child-raising. It's not leading to any deeper learning, other than maybe just having them continue to question the basic structure of reality and not move past it so quickly. Also to take joy.
我只是覺得這很有意思。跟孩子聊這些問題就是很好玩。我不是說這是好的育兒方式，它也沒帶來什麼更深的學習，頂多就是讓他們持續去質疑現實的基本結構、不要那麼快就跳過它，還有從中得到樂趣。

**Naval:** You know what's the meta lesson that's being taught there? Dad spends time asking questions to which there aren't necessarily an answer, because there's something enjoyable in the process of learning and trying to decipher what's happening. Also, dad tries not too hard to teach people things. I don't want to be didactic.
你知道這裡面被傳達的「後設課題（meta lesson）」是什麼嗎？就是：爸爸會花時間去問一些不見得有答案的問題，因為在學習、在試著解讀正在發生的事情這個過程裡，本身就有某種樂趣。還有，爸爸不會太用力去教別人東西。我不想當個愛說教的人。

**主持人:** He helps them to arrive at it.
你是幫他們自己走到那個答案。

**Naval:** Yeah. Correct. Dad is here to help you solve problems when you have problems—and you constantly have problems. So if you come to dad, dad can help explain how he would solve the problem. But most of the time they don't want that. Most of the time they just want me to solve the problem. So sometimes they have to play it dumb.
對，沒錯。爸爸是在你有問題的時候幫你解決問題——而你隨時都有問題。所以你來找爸爸，爸爸可以幫你講解他會怎麼解這個問題。但大多數時候他們不要這個，大多數時候他們只是要我直接把問題解決掉。所以有時候他們得裝傻。

**Naval:** It's like, "Why is my Wi-Fi not working on my computer?" I'm like, "I don't know. Did you click on that thing?"
就像：「我電腦的 Wi-Fi 為什麼不能用？」我就說：「我不知道欸，你有沒有點那個東西？」

**主持人:** Look, you've got like a rebellious, sovereign child.
你看，你養了個叛逆又自主的孩子。

**Naval:** Sovereign as they may be, but sometimes they still need the dad to step in.
再怎麼自主，有時候還是需要爸爸出手介入。

### 🔑 重點單字 / 片語

| 單字 / 片語 | KK 音標 | 詞性 | 中文 |
|---|---|---|---|
| microbiome | /ˏmaɪkroˋbaɪom/ | n. | 微生物群、菌叢 |
| predator | /ˋprɛdətɚ/ | n. | 掠食者、天敵 |
| stricture | /ˋstrɪktʃɚ/ | n. | 戒律、嚴格的限制 |
| circumcision | /ˏsɝkəmˋsɪʒən/ | n. | 割禮、包皮環切 |
| didactic | /daɪˋdæktɪk/ | adj. | 說教的、好為人師的 |
| sovereign | /ˋsɑvrɪn/ | adj. | 自主的、主權獨立的 |

### 💬 慣用語 & 口語解析

- **`shortcut all the debates`**：直接「抄捷徑跳過所有爭辯」——省去繞遠路的討論。
- **`get around to (something)`**：終於「騰出時間去做」某件一直擱著的事。
- **`throw out a question`**：隨口「拋出／丟出一個問題」。
- **`play it dumb`**：故意「裝傻、裝作不懂」。
- **`step in`**：（在需要時）「介入、出手幫忙」。

### 📝 文法 / 句型註記

- **`if you can teach children this philosophy... you shortcut all the debates.`** — 第一類條件句（真實可能）：`if + 現在式..., 現在式...`，表示合理成立的因果。
- **`questions to which there aren't necessarily an answer`** — 「介系詞 + 關係代名詞」的正式寫法：`to which` = `that... to`，修飾 `questions`。
- **`Sovereign as they may be, but...`** — 讓步倒裝：`形容詞 + as + 主詞 + may be` = 「儘管他們再怎麼自主」，等於 `Although they may be sovereign`。
